Hajj — Pilgrimage
beginner
6 min
Conditions for Obligation of Hajj
Ruling on Hajj obligation with conditions and proofs

Learning Objective
By the end of this lesson, you will be able to state the conditions that make Hajj obligatory in the Hanafi school and apply them to determine whether a specific person must perform Hajj.

Core Idea
Hajj is obligatory only when a Muslim has sufficient surplus wealth beyond essential needs and dependents' maintenance.

This passage from Al-Quduri's matn opens the chapter on Hajj by listing who is obligated and under what conditions. Understanding these conditions is critical for determining when the obligation of Hajj actually applies to an individual. We will examine each condition and the proofs that support them.

Guided Path
1
Identify the act and its ruling
The act is Hajj, and the ruling is that it is obligatory (wajib/fard) upon specific categories of people once in a lifetime.
Hanafis consider Hajj as fard because it is established by qat'i evidence.
2
List the conditions
The matn enumerates: being free, adult, sane, healthy, having the means (provision and mount) in excess of essential needs (dwelling, indispensable items, dependents' maintenance), and a secure path.
These are conditions for obligation, not for validity of the act itself.
3
Locate the dalil
The primary dalil is the Quranic verse 3:97. Additionally, three hadiths are cited: the hadith of the Khath'ami woman (permissibility of delegating Hajj), the hadith of the pen being lifted (excluding children and insane), and the hadith defining ability as provision and mount.
Each hadith supports a specific condition.
4
Understand the qualification of ability
Ability (istita'ah) means having surplus wealth after fulfilling one's basic needs and those of dependents. The dwelling is not to be sold, and dependents must be provided for until return.
This prevents hardship and ensures obligations toward family are not neglected.

Source Text
⚠ Extracted via Advanced OCR ∼97% accuracy, minor errors may remain — always verify against original Arabic books
قَالَ - رَحِمَهُ اللهُ -: الْحَجُ وَاجِبٌ عَلَى الْأَحْرَارِ الْبَالِغِينَ الْعُقَلَاءِ الْأَصِحَاءِ إِذَا قَدَرُوا عَلَى الزَّادِ وَالرَّاحِلَةِ فَاضِلًا عَنْ مَسْكَنِهِ وَمَا لَا بُدَّ مِنْهُ وَعَنْ نَفَقَةِ عِيَالِهِ إِلَى حِينِ عَوْدِهِ وَكَوْنُ الطَّرِيقِ آمِنًا.
الوجه الأول: الْحَدِيثُ لِثُبُوتِ الْحَجِّ وَاجِبٌ عَلَى الْأَحْرَارِ الْبَالِغِينَ الْعُقَلَاءِ، قَالَ اللهُ تَعَالَى: {وَلِلَّهِ عَلَى النَّاسِ حِجُّ الْبَيْتِ مَنِ اسْتَطَاعَ إِلَيْهِ سَبِيلًا} [آل عمران: 97].
الوجه الثاني: الْحَدِيثُ لِثُبُوتِ الْحَجِّ وَاجِبٌ عَلَى الْأَحْرَارِ الْبَالِغِينَ الْعُقَلَاءِ الْأَصِحَاءِ إِذَا قَدَرُوا عَلَى الزَّادِ وَالرَّاحِلَةِ، عَنْ عَبْدِ اللهِ بْنِ عَبَّاسٍ قَالَ: كَانَ الْفَضْلُ بْنُ عَبَّاسٍ رَدِيفَ رَسُولِ اللهِ صَلَّى اللهُ عَلَيْهِ وَسَلَّمَ فَجَاءَتْهُ امْرَأَةٌ مِنْ خَثْعَمٍ ... فَقَالَتْ: يَا رَسُولَ اللهِ، إِنَّ فَرِيضَةَ اللهِ عَلَى عِبَادِهِ فِي الْحَجِّ أَدْرَكَتْ أَبِي شَيْخًا كَبِيرًا لَا يَسْتَطِيعُ أَنْ يَثْبُتَ عَلَى الرَّاحِلَةِ، أَفَأَحُجُّ عَنْهُ؟ قَالَ: «نَعَمْ، وَذَلِكَ فِي حَجَّةِ الْوَدَاعِ». (رَوَاهُ أَبُو دَاوُدَ: بَابُ الرَّجُلِ يَحُجُّ عَنْ غَيْرِهِ، 1809)
الوجه الثالث: الْحَدِيثُ لِثُبُوتِ الْحَجِّ وَاجِبٌ عَلَى الْأَحْرَارِ الْبَالِغِينَ الْعُقَلَاءِ، عَنِ ابْنِ عَبَّاسٍ قَالَ: مُرَّ عَلَى عَلِي بْنِ أَبِي طَالِبٍ رَضِيَ اللهُ عَنْهُ بِمَعْنَى عُثْمَانَ، قَالَ: أَوَ مَا تَذْكُرُ أَنَّ رَسُولَ اللهِ صَلَّى اللهُ عَلَيْهِ وَسَلَّمَ قَالَ: «رُفِعَ الْقَلَمُ عَنْ ثَلَاثَةٍ: عَنِ الْمَجْنُونِ الْمَعْلُوبِ عَلَى عَقْلِهِ حَتَّى يَفِيقَ، وَعَنِ النَّائِمِ حَتَّى يَسْتَيْقِظَ، وَعَنِ الصَّبِيِّ حَتَّى يَحْتَلِمَ». (رَوَاهُ أَبُو دَاوُدَ: بَابٌ فِي الْمَجْنُونِ يَسْرِقُ أَوْ يُصِيبُ حَدًّا، 4401)
الوجه الرابع: الْحَدِيثُ لِثُبُوتِ الْحَجِّ وَاجِبٌ عَلَى الْأَحْرَارِ الْبَالِغِينَ الْعُقَلَاءِ، عَنِ ابْنِ عُمَرَ قَالَ: جَاءَ رَجُلٌ إِلَى النَّبِيِّ صَلَّى اللهُ عَلَيْهِ وَسَلَّمَ فَقَالَ: يَا رَسُولَ اللهِ مَا يُوجِبُ الْحَجَّ؟ قَالَ: «الزَّادُ وَالرَّاحِلَةُ». (رَوَاهُ التِّرْمِذِيُّ: بَابُ مَا جَاءَ فِي إِيجَابِ الْحَجِّ بِالزَّادِ وَالرَّاحِلَةِ، 813)
He (the author) said - may Allah have mercy on him: Hajj is obligatory upon free, adult, sane, healthy persons when they are able to afford provisions and a mount, beyond what is needed for their dwelling and what is indispensable, and for the maintenance of their dependents until their return, and that the road be secure. The first aspect: The hadith for establishing that Hajj is obligatory upon free, adult, sane persons: Allah Most High said: 'And [due] to Allah from the people is a pilgrimage to the House – for whoever is able to find thereto a way.' [Al-i-Imran 3:97]. The second aspect: The hadith for establishing that Hajj is obligatory upon free, adult, sane, healthy persons when they are able to afford provisions and a mount: from Abdullah ibn Abbas, he said: Al-Fadl ibn Abbas was riding behind the Messenger of Allah ﷺ when a woman from Khath'am came... she said: O Messenger of Allah, the obligation of Allah upon His servants in Hajj has overtaken my father, an old man who cannot sit firmly on a mount; may I perform Hajj on his behalf? He said: 'Yes, and that was during the Farewell Pilgrimage.' (Narrated by Abu Dawood: Chapter on a man performing Hajj on behalf of another, 1809). The third aspect: The hadith for establishing that Hajj is obligatory upon free, adult, sane persons: from Ibn Abbas, he said: [A case] was presented to Ali ibn Abi Talib (may Allah be pleased with him) regarding the meaning of Uthman [i.e., a similar case], he said: Do you not remember that the Messenger of Allah ﷺ said: 'The pen has been lifted from three: from the insane person who is overcome by his loss of reason until he recovers, from the sleeper until he awakens, and from the child until he reaches puberty.' He said: You have spoken truthfully. (Narrated by Abu Dawood: Chapter on the insane person who steals or commits a hadd [offense], 4401). The fourth aspect: The hadith for establishing that Hajj is obligatory upon free, adult, sane persons: from Ibn Umar, he said: A man came to the Prophet ﷺ and said: O Messenger of Allah, what makes Hajj obligatory? He said: 'Provision and a mount.' (Narrated by al-Tirmidhi: Chapter on what has been narrated regarding the obligation of Hajj by provision and mount, 813).
Source pages p. 234

Commentary
This passage is the opening of Kitab al-Hajj in Al-Quduri's matn, stating the ruling on whom Hajj is obligatory upon. It begins with the base ruling that Hajj is wajib (obligatory) upon specific categories of people with specific conditions. The matn enumerates conditions: free (not slave), adult (baligh), sane (aqil), healthy (sahih), having the means (provision and mount) in excess of one's essential needs (dwelling, indispensable items, and dependents' maintenance until return), and the road being safe. The inclusion of 'secure path' covers the requirement of safety from bandits and general danger. The commentary then provides four hadith proofs: (1) the Quranic verse (Al-i-Imran 3:97) establishing the obligation; (2) the hadith of the woman from Khath'am whose father was old, showing that Hajj is a direct obligation but can be delegated if the person is unable to perform it themselves; (3) the hadith of the three whose actions are not recorded (child, insane, sleeper) indicating that obligation only applies to adults of sound mind; (4) the hadith defining the means of ability as provision and mount. These proofs support the matn's conditions. The ruling is a foundational statement in Hanafi fiqh: Hajj is fard (obligatory) once in a lifetime for those who meet these conditions. Note that the Hanafi school considers Hajj to be fard (not just wajib in the technical sense) because it is established by the Quran and mutawatir Sunnah. The term 'wajib' here is used in the general linguistic sense of obligatory.

Key Terms
الزَّادُ وَالرَّاحِلَةُ (al-zad wa al-rahilah): Provision (food and supplies for the journey) and a mount (riding animal or means of transport). This is the minimal standard of istita'ah (ability).
فَاضِلًا عَنْ مَسْكَنِهِ (fadilan 'an maskanihi): Surplus beyond the value of one's dwelling (the house one lives in). The house is not to be sold to fund Hajj.
نَفَقَةُ عِيَالِهِ (nafaqatu 'iyalihi): Maintenance of one's dependents (family) during the period of travel and until return. This is a condition; if the dependents would suffer, Hajj is not obligatory.

Key Terms from Source Passage

Checkpoint
According to the matn, what is required for Hajj to be obligatory regarding one's dwelling?
A) One must sell one's house to afford Hajj
B) The cost of Hajj must be surplus beyond the dwelling's essential value
C) One must own a house in Mecca
D) The dwelling must be at least two years old

Key Takeaway
Hajj is obligatory only when one has surplus wealth beyond all essential needs and dependents' maintenance, and the journey is safe.

Definition of Hajj: The Pillar and Its Core Meaning
Definition of Hajj as a pillar with time and manner constraints

Learning Objective
By the end of this lesson, you will be able to state the definition of Hajj as given in the Hanafi usool and identify its two essential elements: specific time and specific manner.

Core Idea
Hajj is not merely visiting Mecca; it is a prescribed intention at a prescribed time in a prescribed manner.

This lesson introduces the formal definition of Hajj from the Hanafi usool. The text succinctly establishes Hajj as one of the five pillars of Islam, then defines it by two essential constraints: a specific time (the months of Hajj) and a specific manner (the rituals of ihram, tawaf, sa'y, wuquf, etc.). Understanding this definition is the foundation for all subsequent rulings on Hajj.

Guided Path
1
Identify the definition
Read the Arabic text and locate the definition. It states: 'Hajj is a pillar of Islam. By Hajj is meant intending the House of Allah in a specific manner and at a specific time.'
The definition has three parts: (1) it is a pillar, (2) it is intention for the House, (3) constrained by specific manner and time.
2
Break down the components
Separate the three components: (a) Rukn – a foundational obligation, (b) Qasd al-Bayt – intention directed at the Ka'bah, (c) Bi khas tariqah wa khas waqt – the actions and timing are fixed by Shari'ah.
The specific manner includes ihram, talbiyah, tawaf, sa'y, wuquf, etc. The specific time is the months of Hajj: Shawwal, Dhu al-Qa'dah, and first ten days of Dhu al-Hijjah, with arafah on the 9th.
3
Understand the significance
The constraints exclude casual visits or actions performed at other times. Only when both conditions are met does the act become Hajj.
This definition is a memorization anchor for the entire chapter on Hajj.
4
Apply the definition
Given a scenario, decide if it qualifies as Hajj. For example, visiting Mecca in Ramadan and performing tawaf does NOT meet the time condition. Intending the House at the right time but without ihram also fails the manner condition.
Both elements are necessary; absence of either prevents the act from being Hajj.

Source Text
⚠ Extracted via Advanced OCR ∼97% accuracy, minor errors may remain — always verify against original Arabic books
اصول : حج اسلام کا رکن ہے، حج سے مراد خاص طریقہ اور خاص وقت پر بیت اللہ کا ارادہ کرنا ہے۔
Usul: Hajj is a pillar of Islam. By Hajj is meant intending the House of Allah in a specific manner and at a specific time.
Source pages p. 234

Commentary
This is a brief definition from the Usool section. It defines Hajj linguistically and technically: it is a pillar (rukn) of Islam, meaning it is one of the obligatory acts upon which the religion is based. The technical definition: ‘intending the House of Allah’ (Bayt Allah, i.e., the Ka'bah) with specific actions (e.g., ihram, tawaf, sa'y, wuquf) at specific times (the months of Hajj: Shawwal, Dhu al-Qa'dah, and the first ten days of Dhu al-Hijjah). This sets the framework for the entire book of Hajj.

Key Terms
رکن (rukn): A foundational pillar; Hajj is one of the five pillars of Islam, fard upon those who meet conditions.
خاص طریقہ (khas tariqah): The specific manner prescribed by the Shari'ah: ihram, talbiyah, tawaf, sa'y, wuquf, etc.
خاص وقت (khas waqt): The specific time: the months of Hajj, particularly the Day of Arafah and the days of Mina.

Key Terms from Source Passage

Checkpoint
According to this text, what is Hajj?
A) Any visit to Mecca
B) Intending the House of Allah in a specific manner and time
C) Only standing at Arafah
D) Performing tawaf only

Key Takeaway
Hajj is defined as intending the Ka'bah with the specific rituals at the specific time of Hajj, making it a unique act of worship.

Condition of Mahram for Women's Hajj
The matn requires a mahram or husband for a woman to perform Hajj if the journey is three days or more.

Learning Objective
By the end of this lesson, you will be able to state the Hanafi ruling on the requirement of a mahram for a woman's Hajj, cite the hadith proof, and apply the distance threshold of three days.

Core Idea
A woman's Hajj journey of three days or more requires a mahram or husband – without him, the obligation is deferred.

This lesson examines the Hanafi condition that a woman must be accompanied by a mahram or her husband when traveling for Hajj if the journey is three days or more. The ruling is derived from explicit hadiths and reflects the school's concern for safety and protection.

Guided Path
1
Identify the act and condition
The act is a woman performing Hajj. The condition is having a mahram or husband with her if the journey is three days or more.
The condition is not a pillar of Hajj itself but a requirement for the journey.
2
Locate the hadith proof
Two hadiths are cited: one from Abu Sa'id al-Khudri and one from Abu Umamah. Both prohibit travel beyond three days without a mahram.
The hadiths are ahad (singular), giving zanni certainty.
3
Analyze the wajh al-dalalah
The phrase 'لا يحل' indicates prohibition. In Hanafi usul, this implies the act is makruh tahrimi or haram without necessity. For Hajj, it conditions permissibility on the mahram.
The prohibition is tied to the distance (‘fawqa thalathati ayyam’).
4
Note the cross-madhhab difference
Shafi'is require a mahram for any journey, while Hanafis limit it to three days or more.
This distinction is crucial for practical application.
5
Apply the ruling to a scenario
Given a specific distance, determine if a mahram is needed. E.g., a 2-day journey does not require one; a 4-day journey does.

Source Text
⚠ Extracted via Advanced OCR ∼97% accuracy, minor errors may remain — always verify against original Arabic books
وَيُعْتَبَرُ فِي الْمَرْأَةِ أَنْ يَكُونَ لَهَا مَحْرَمٌ يَحُجُّ بِهَا أَوْ زَوْجٌ، وَلَا يَجُوزُ لَهَا أَنْ تَحُجَّ بِغَيْرِهِمَا إِذَا كَانَ بَيْنَهَا وَبَيْنَ مَكَّةَ مَسِيرَةُ ثَلَاثَةِ أَيَّامٍ فَصَاعِدًا.
الوجه الأول: الْحَدِيثُ لِثُبُوتِ وَيُعْتَبَرُ فِي الْمَرْأَةِ أَنْ يَكُونَ لَهَا مَحْرَمٌ يَحُجُّ بِهَا، عَنْ أَبِي سَعِيدٍ الْخُدْرِيِّ قَالَ: قَالَ رَسُولُ اللهِ صَلَّى اللهُ عَلَيْهِ وَسَلَّمَ: «لَا يَحِلُّ لِامْرَأَةٍ تُؤْمِنُ بِاللهِ وَالْيَوْمِ الْآخِرِ أَنْ تُسَافِرَ سَفَرًا فَوْقَ ثَلَاثَةِ أَيَّامٍ فَصَاعِدًا، إِلَّا وَمَعَهَا أَبُوهَا أَوْ أَخُوهَا أَوْ زَوْجُهَا أَوِ ابْنُهَا أَوْ ذُو مَحْرَمٍ مِنْهَا». (رَوَاهُ أَبُو دَاوُدَ: بَابٌ فِي الْمَرْأَةِ تَحُجُّ بِغَيْرِ مَحْرَمٍ، 1726)
الوجه الثاني: الْحَدِيثُ لِثُبُوتِ وَيُعْتَبَرُ فِي الْمَرْأَةِ أَنْ يَكُونَ لَهَا مَحْرَمٌ يَحُجُّ بِهَا، عَنْ أَبِي أُمَامَةَ قَالَ: سَمِعْتُ رَسُولَ اللهِ صَلَّى اللهُ عَلَيْهِ وَسَلَّمَ يَقُولُ: «لَا تُسَافِرِ امْرَأَةٌ سَفَرًا ثَلَاثَةَ أَيَّامٍ أَوْ تَحُجَّ إِلَّا وَمَعَهَا زَوْجُهَا». (رَوَاهُ الدَّارَقُطْنِيُّ: بَابُ كِتَابِ الْحَجِّ، 2442)
And it is considered regarding a woman that she have a mahram who performs Hajj with her, or a husband. And it is not permissible for her to perform Hajj without them when between her and Mecca there is a journey of three days or more. The first aspect: The hadith for establishing that a woman must have a mahram to perform Hajj with her: from Abu Sa'id al-Khudri who said: The Messenger of Allah ﷺ said: 'It is not lawful for a woman who believes in Allah and the Last Day to travel a journey of more than three days unless accompanied by her father, or her brother, or her husband, or her son, or a mahram of hers.' (Narrated by Abu Dawood: Chapter on a woman performing Hajj without a mahram, 1726). The second aspect: The hadith for establishing that a woman must have a mahram to perform Hajj with her: from Abu Umamah who said: I heard the Messenger of Allah ﷺ say: 'A woman should not travel a journey of three days or perform Hajj unless accompanied by her husband.' (Narrated by al-Daraqutni: Chapter on the Book of Hajj, 2442).
Source pages p. 234

Commentary
This passage continues the matn, adding a specific condition for women: the presence of a mahram (a male relative whom she is permanently prohibited from marrying) or her husband during the Hajj journey. The distance triggering this restriction is three days' travel or more between her residence and Mecca. This is a Hanafi ruling based on the hadiths that prohibit women from undertaking long journeys without a mahram. The commentary provides two hadith proofs: one from Abu Sa'id stating the general prohibition for journeys over three days, and another from Abu Umamah specifically mentioning Hajj. Note that the Hanafi position differs from the Shafi'i school, which requires a mahram for any journey, short or long. For shorter distances (less than three days), the Hanafi school allows a woman to travel with a group of trustworthy women or in safe circumstances. The matn includes the phrase 'if the distance is three days or more', indicating that the mahram condition is tied to the duration of travel. This nuance is important for practical application.

Key Terms
مَحْرَمٌ (mahram): A male relative whom a woman is permanently prohibited from marrying due to blood kinship (e.g., father, brother, son, uncle), or by relationship through marriage (e.g., father-in-law, stepson). The mahram must be an adult, sane Muslim capable of performing Hajj.
مَسِيرَةُ ثَلَاثَةِ أَيَّامٍ (masiratu thalathati ayyam): A journey of three days' travel (approximately 48-72 miles depending on mode of transport, but traditionally about 24 farsakh or ~144 km). This is the distance that makes a mahram necessary.

Key Terms from Source Passage

Checkpoint
What is the minimum distance that triggers the requirement for a mahram in a woman's Hajj according to the Hanafi school?
A) Any journey
B) One day's journey
C) Three days' journey or more
D) One week's journey

Key Takeaway
A mahram or husband is a required condition for a woman's Hajj journey of three days or more; for shorter journeys, the condition does not apply.

Continuation of Hajj after Puberty or Emancipation
Ruling on child/slave hajj after status change

Learning Objective
By the end of this lesson, you will be able to state the Hanafi ruling for a child reaching puberty or a slave freed during hajj, and identify why the hajj does not count as the obligatory Hajj.

Core Idea
A hajj begun before full obligation remains valid as nafl but does not discharge the fard.

This passage from Al-Quduri addresses a specific situation: a child who enters ihram for hajj and then reaches puberty, or a slave who enters ihram and is later freed. In both cases, the person continues their hajj, but it does not fulfill the obligatory Hajj (Hajjat al-Islam) that becomes due upon them after the change in status. Understanding this ruling clarifies the conditions for a hajj to count as obligatory.

Guided Path
1
Identify the two cases
The matn gives two scenarios: a child (sabi) who enters ihram then reaches puberty, and a slave (abd) who enters ihram then is freed. Note the common element: the change in legal status (becoming mukallaf or free) occurs after starting ihram.
The child and slave are not considered fully responsible at the moment of ihram.
2
Determine the ruling on continuation
The matn says 'madayaa 'ala hajjihima' - they continue with that hajj. They do not break it and start anew. The hajj already begun remains valid as an act of worship.
Continuation is required, not optional.
3
Grasp the limit of sufficiency
The matn states 'lam yujzihima 'an Hajjat al-Islam' - it does not suffice for the obligatory hajj. Even though the hajj is performed properly, it does not fulfill the fard that becomes binding after they become fully responsible.
The condition for a hajj to count as fard is that the person be both free and mukallaf at the time of ihram.
4
Contrast with a hajj begun after obligation
If an adult free Muslim enters ihram for hajj, that hajj is valid and counts as the obligatory Hajj (if it is the first). The key difference is the timing of the obligation relative to the start of ihram.
This highlights the principle that obligation (wujub) is tied to the person's status at ihram.

Source Text
⚠ Extracted via Advanced OCR ∼97% accuracy, minor errors may remain — always verify against original Arabic books
وَإِذَا بَلَغَ الصَّبِيُّ بَعْدَمَا أَحْرَمَ أَوْ أَعْتَقَ الْعَبْدُ فَمَضَيَا عَلَى حَجِّهِمَا ذَلِكَ لَمْ يُجْزِهِمَا عَنْ حَجَّةِ الْإِسْلَامِ
And when a child reaches puberty after having entered ihram, or a slave is freed, and they continue with their Hajj, that does not suffice them for the Hajj of Islam (i.e., the obligatory Hajj).
Source pages p. 235

Commentary
This passage presents a ruling about two specific situations: (1) a minor who enters ihram for Hajj and then reaches puberty (bulugh) during the rites, and (2) a slave who enters ihram and then is freed before completing the Hajj. In both cases, the individual is to continue with the Hajj they have started (they do not break it and restart). However, this Hajj will not count as the obligatory Hajj (Hajjat al-Islam) that becomes due upon them after they become mukallaf (adult/free). They must perform a separate Hajj later to fulfill the obligation. The ruling stems from the principle that a valid Hajj requires the person to be both mukallaf and free at the time of ihram. Since the condition was not fully met at the start, the Hajj is valid (as a nafila or tatawwu‘) but does not satisfy the fard. The matn uses 'lam yujzihima' meaning it does not suffice. The Hanafi school treats the Hajj as a nafl (supererogatory) in this case. No proofs are given in this passage; it is a direct ruling statement.

Key Terms
حَجَّةُ الْإِسْلَامِ (Hajjat al-Islam): The obligatory Hajj that is a fard upon every free, adult, capable Muslim once in a lifetime.
لَمْ يُجْزِهِمَا (lam yujzihima): It does not suffice for them; the Hajj performed does not fulfill the obligation that becomes due after the change in status.

Key Terms from Source Passage

Checkpoint
If a child enters ihram for Hajj and reaches puberty during the Hajj, what is the ruling on that Hajj?
A) It counts as the obligatory Hajj
B) It is invalid and must be repeated
C) It is valid but does not count as the obligatory Hajj
D) It becomes a wajib Hajj

Key Takeaway
A Hajj begun by a child or slave is valid as a nafl but does not fulfill the obligatory Hajj because the condition of being mukallaf and free at the time of ihram was not met.

The Five Miqat Boundaries: Ruling and Hadith Proof
Matn listing miqat with hadith proofs

Learning Objective
By the end of this lesson, you will be able to state the five miqat boundaries for Hajj and 'Umrah and identify the hadith evidence that establishes each.

Core Idea
Crossing a miqat without ihram is impermissible — the Prophet’s designated boundaries are binding.

This lesson presents the five miqat boundaries as stated in the matn of al-Quduri and the hadith proofs that establish them. You will learn the ruling that one must assume ihram before crossing these points and the specific locations for each region. The commentary supplies two authentic hadith chains that together cover all five miqat.

Guided Path
1
Identify the act and its ruling
Read the matn: 'al-mawaqitu allati la yajuzu an yatajawazaha al-insanu illa muhriman.' The act is crossing the miqat without ihram; the ruling is that it is not permissible.
The ruling carries a wajib obligation to assume ihram before crossing.
2
List the five miqat and their regions
Memorize: Dhu al-Hulayfah for Madinah, Dhat 'Irq for Iraq, al-Juhfah for Syria, Qarn for Najd, Yalamlam for Yemen.
These are the classical locations; modern equivalents may be used if the exact site is unknown.
3
Examine the first hadith proof
The hadith from Ibn Abbas (Bukhari 1524, Muslim 1181) mentions four miqat. Note that Iraq is not included because it was conquered later.
This hadith is the primary proof for four miqat.
4
Examine the second hadith proof
The hadith from 'Aisha (Abu Dawud 1739, Bukhari 1531) specifies Dhat 'Irq for the people of Iraq, completing the list.
Both hadiths together establish all five miqat.
5
Understand the epistemological weight
The thubut (transmission) of these hadiths is qat'i (mutawatir in meaning), but the dalala (indication) is zanni — the command 'waqqata' implies obligation through the Hanafi usul principle that a command indicates obligation (al-amr yufidu al-wujub).
This is why the ruling is wajib, not fard.

Source Text
⚠ Extracted via Advanced OCR ∼97% accuracy, minor errors may remain — always verify against original Arabic books
وَالْمَوَاقِيتُ الَّتِي لَا يَجُوزُ أَنْ يَتَجَاوَزَهَا الْإِنْسَانُ إِلَّا مُحْرِمًا: لِأَهْلِ الْمَدِينَةِ ذُو الْحُلَيْفَةِ، وَلِأَهْلِ الْعِرَاقِ ذَاتُ عِرْقٍ، وَلِأَهْلِ الشَّامِ الْجُحْفَةُ، وَلِأَهْلِ نَجْدٍ قَرْنٌ، وَلِأَهْلِ الْيَمَنِ يَلَمْلَمُ.
الوجه الأول: الْحَدِيثُ لِثُبُوتِ الْمَوَاقِيتِ، عَنِ ابْنِ عَبَّاسٍ قَالَ: «إِنَّ النَّبِيَّ صَلَّى اللهُ عَلَيْهِ وَسَلَّمَ وَقَّتَ لِأَهْلِ الْمَدِينَةِ ذَا الْحُلَيْفَةِ، وَلِأَهْلِ الشَّأْمِ الْجُحْفَةَ، وَلِأَهْلِ نَجْدٍ قَرْنَ الْمَنَازِلِ، وَلِأَهْلِ الْيَمَنِ يَلَمْلَمَ، هُنَّ لَهُمْ وَلِمَنْ أَتَى عَلَيْهِنَّ مِنْ غَيْرِهِنَّ مِمَّنْ أَرَادَ الْحَجَّ وَالْعُمْرَةَ، وَمَنْ كَانَ دُونَ ذَلِكَ فَمِنْ حَيْثُ أَنْشَأَ حَتَّى أَهْلُ مَكَّةَ مِنْ مَكَّةَ». (رَوَاهُ الْبُخَارِيُّ: بَابُ مَهَلِّ أَهْلِ مَكَّةَ لِلْحَجِّ وَالْعُمْرَةِ، 1524 / مُسْلِمٌ: بَابُ مَوَاقِيتِ الْحَجِّ وَالْعُمْرَةِ، 1181)
الوجه الثاني: الْحَدِيثُ لِثُبُوتِ الْمَوَاقِيتِ، عَنْ عَائِشَةَ رَضِيَ اللهُ عَنْهَا أَنَّ رَسُولَ اللهِ صَلَّى اللهُ عَلَيْهِ وَسَلَّمَ «وَقَّتَ لِأَهْلِ الْعِرَاقِ ذَاتَ عِرْقٍ». (رَوَاهُ أَبُو دَاوُدَ: بَابٌ فِي الْمَوَاقِيتِ، 1739 / الْبُخَارِيُّ: بَابٌ: ذَاتُ عِرْقٍ لِأَهْلِ الْعِرَاقِ، 1531)
And the miqat stations which it is not permissible for a person to pass except in the state of ihram: for the people of Madinah, Dhu al-Hulayfah; for the people of Iraq, Dhat ‘Irq; for the people of Syria, al-Juhfah; for the people of Najd, Qarn; for the people of Yemen, Yalamlam. The first aspect: The hadith for establishing the miqat stations: from Ibn Abbas, he said: 'The Prophet ﷺ designated for the people of Madinah Dhu al-Hulayfah, for the people of Syria al-Juhfah, for the people of Najd Qarn al-Manazil, and for the people of Yemen Yalamlam. These are for them and for anyone who comes upon them from other than their people, from those who intend Hajj and ‘Umrah. And whoever is within them, then from where he begins, until the people of Makkah [do so] from Makkah.' (Narrated by Bukhari: Chapter on the ihram stations for the people of Makkah for Hajj and 'Umrah, 1524 / Muslim: Chapter on the miqat stations for Hajj and 'Umrah, 1181). The second aspect: The hadith for establishing the miqat stations: from 'A'ishah (may Allah be pleased with her) that the Messenger of Allah ﷺ 'designated for the people of Iraq Dhat 'Irq.' (Narrated by Abu Dawood: Chapter on the miqat stations, 1739 / Bukhari: Chapter: Dhat 'Irq for the people of Iraq, 1531).
Source pages p. 235

Commentary
This passage lists the five miqat boundaries designated by the Prophet ﷺ. The matn specifies: for Madinah, Dhu al-Hulayfah (also known as Abyar 'Ali); for Iraq, Dhat 'Irq; for Syria (Sham), al-Juhfah; for Najd, Qarn (also called Qarn al-Manazil); for Yemen, Yalamlam. The rule is that one must not pass these points without assuming ihram. People residing within the miqat (such as the residents of Makkah) begin their ihram from their homes. The commentary provides two hadith proofs: the famous hadith from Ibn Abbas listing the miqat for most regions, and a separate hadith from Aisha specifically for Iraq (since Iraq was not mentioned in the first hadith as it was conquered later). The Hanafi school follows these designations. Note that 'Dhat 'Irq' is the miqat for Iraq according to the Hanafi school, while the Shafi'i school also recognizes the same but with some differences in location due to changes in geography.

Key Terms
الْمَوَاقِيتُ (al-mawaqit): The designated places where one must enter the state of ihram for Hajj or 'Umrah. They are boundaries; passing them without ihram is impermissible.
مُحْرِمًا (muhriman): In the state of ihram (intention and recitation of talbiyah). One must have assumed ihram before crossing the miqat.

Key Terms from Source Passage

Checkpoint
What is the miqat for the people of Iraq according to the matn?
A) Dhu al-Hulayfah
B) Dhat 'Irq
C) Al-Juhfah
D) Yalamlam

Key Takeaway
The five miqat boundaries established by the Prophet ﷺ are binding; one must assume ihram before crossing them.

Permissibility of Ihram Before the Miqat
Ruling with proof on early ihram

Learning Objective
By the end of this lesson, you will be able to state the Hanafi ruling on assuming ihram before the miqat and cite the supporting hadith evidence.

Core Idea
Ihram before the miqat is permissible; the Prophet ﷺ commanded 'Umrah from al-Tan'im as proof.

This passage from al-Quduri clarifies a common point of confusion: can one enter the state of ihram before reaching the designated miqat? The matn gives a clear ruling of permissibility, and the commentary provides two hadith proofs. Understanding this ruling ensures that pilgrims do not unnecessarily restrict themselves or worry about the validity of early ihram.

Guided Path
1
Identify the act and its ruling
Determine what the passage is ruling upon. The act is 'taqdim al-ihram' (advancing the ihram before the miqat). The ruling is 'jaza' (it is permissible).
The ruling is permissibility (ibaha), not obligation or recommendation.
2
Locate the dalil
The commentary cites two hadith: (a) the Prophet ordered for Aisha to perform Umrah from al-Tan'im (Bukhari), and (b) the Prophet said 'Do not pass the miqat except in ihram' (Tabarani).
Both hadith are from the Sunnah, though the second is weaker in authenticity.
3
Trace the wajh al-dalalah
The first hadith shows that ihram can be assumed from a place inside the haram (after the miqat), implying that it is not restricted to the exact miqat. The second hadith requires being in ihram when crossing the miqat, not that one must wait until the miqat.
The dalala (indication) is zanni, but sufficient for permissibility.
4
Note the ikhtilaf and mufta bihi
The Shafi'i school considers early ihram makruh if done very early (e.g., from home), while the Hanafi school permits it absolutely. The mufta bihi is the Hanafi position of permissibility.
This difference has practical implications for pilgrims traveling long distances.

Source Text
⚠ Extracted via Advanced OCR ∼97% accuracy, minor errors may remain — always verify against original Arabic books
فَإِنْ قَدَّمَ الْإِحْرَامَ عَلَى هَذِهِ الْمَوَاقِيتِ جَازَ.
الوجه الأول: الْحَدِيثُ لِثُبُوتِ جَوَازِ تَقْدِيمِ الْإِحْرَامِ، أَنَّ النَّبِيَّ صَلَّى اللهُ عَلَيْهِ وَسَلَّمَ «أَمَرَ أَنْ يُرْدِفَ عَائِشَةَ وَيُعْمِرَهَا مِنَ التَّنْعِيمِ». (رَوَاهُ الْبُخَارِيُّ: بَابُ عُمْرَةِ التَّنْعِيمِ، 1748)
الوجه الثاني: الْحَدِيثُ لِثُبُوتِ جَوَازِ تَقْدِيمِ الْإِحْرَامِ، عَنِ ابْنِ عَبَّاسٍ أَنَّ النَّبِيَّ صَلَّى اللهُ عَلَيْهِ وَسَلَّمَ قَالَ: «لَا تَجَاوَزُوا الْوَقْتَ إِلَّا بِإِحْرَامٍ». (الْمُعْجَمُ الْكَبِيرُ لِلطَّبَرَانِيِّ، 12236 / مُصَنَّفُ ابْنِ أَبِي شَيْبَةَ: مَنْ كَرِهَ أَنْ يَدْخُلَ مَكَّةَ بِغَيْرِ إِحْرَامٍ، 13517)
If one performs ihram before these miqat, it is permissible. The first aspect: The hadith for establishing the permissibility of advancing the ihram: that the Prophet ﷺ ordered that he [Abd al-Rahman ibn Abi Bakr] take Aisha behind him on the mount and let her perform 'Umrah from al-Tan'im. (Narrated by Bukhari: Chapter on the 'Umrah of al-Tan'im, 1748). The second aspect: The hadith for establishing the permissibility of advancing the ihram: from Ibn Abbas that the Prophet ﷺ said: 'Do not pass the time (al-waqt) except with ihram.' (Al-Mu'jam al-Kabir of al-Tabarani, 12236 / Musannaf Ibn Abi Shaybah: Chapter on those who dislike entering Makkah without ihram, 13517).
Source pages p. 235

Commentary
This passage addresses the permissibility of assuming ihram before arriving at the designated miqat boundaries. The matn says 'if one advances the ihram before these miqat, it is permissible.' This means one can enter the state of ihram from a point before the miqat, even from one's home. The commentary provides two proofs: first, the hadith of Aisha performing 'Umrah from al-Tan'im, which is within the miqat area (actually within the haram, but the point is that she assumed ihram from a place that is after the miqat? Wait, al-Tan'im is actually inside the haram, not before the miqat. This hadith shows that one can assume ihram from a place within the miqat region. The second hadith: 'Do not pass the time except with ihram' clearly indicates that one must have ihram before crossing the miqat. The permissibility to do ihram earlier is established by the fact that the Prophet and companions assumed ihram from their homes before reaching the miqat. However, it is mustahabb (recommended) to assume ihram at the miqat itself to follow the Sunnah. Advancing ihram is valid but may involve extra restrictions for longer period. The Hanafi school considers it permissible, but the better practice is to assume at the miqat. This ruling is important for travelers who might pass the miqat at night and wish to avoid the difficulty of finding a place to change.

Key Terms
تَقْدِيمُ الْإِحْرَامِ (taqdim al-ihram): Assuming the state of ihram before reaching the miqat boundary.
جَازَ (jaza): It is permissible; the ruling is permissibility (ibaha). It does not imply any sin.

Key Terms from Source Passage

Checkpoint
What is the ruling on performing ihram before reaching the miqat according to this passage?
A) Impermissible (haram)
B) Disliked (makruh)
C) Permissible (ja'iz)
D) Obligatory (wajib)

Key Takeaway
Assuming ihram before the miqat is permissible (ja'iz) based on prophetic practice; the better practice is at the miqat.

Eight Conditions for Hajj Obligation
Urdu summary listing conditions for Hajj obligation

Learning Objective
By the end of this lesson, you will be able to list and explain the eight conditions that make Hajj obligatory (fard) upon a Muslim.

Core Idea
Hajj is obligatory only when all eight conditions are met — any missing condition lifts the obligation.

In this lesson, we examine the classical Hanafi enumeration of conditions for Hajj to become fard. This list serves as a foundational checklist for determining whether a person must perform Hajj. Understanding these conditions prevents common mistakes in applying the obligation.

Guided Path
1
Memorize the list
Learn the eight conditions in order: free, Muslim, sane, adult, able (provision & mount), dependents maintained, healthy, safe route.
Use the Urdu text as a mnemonic anchor.
2
Understand each condition
For each condition, grasp why it is a prerequisite. E.g., a slave lacks full control over his time and resources.
Refer to the commentary for details.
3
Distinguish wujub from ada
These conditions are for obligation (wujub). The conditions for validity (ada) during performance are different (e.g., ihraam, standing at Arafat).
Adulthood is required for wujub but not for validity (a child's Hajj is nafl).
4
Apply to scenarios
Given a person's situation, check each condition. If all met, Hajj is obligatory. If any missing, not obligatory until that condition is fulfilled.
Practice with the tasks below.

Source Text
⚠ Extracted via Advanced OCR ∼97% accuracy, minor errors may remain — always verify against original Arabic books
اصول : حج فرض ہونے کے شرائط : ۱ آزاد ۲ مسلمان ۳ عاقل ۴ بالغ ۵ توشه پر قادر ۴ اہل و عیال کے نان و نفقہ کا مکمل انتظام ہونا ہے تندرست ۸ راستہ کا پر امن ہونا۔
Usul: Conditions for Hajj being obligatory: 1 free, 2 Muslim, 3 sane, 4 adult, 5 able to afford provisions, 4 [6] complete arrangement for dependents' food and spending, healthy, 8 [7] the route being safe.
Source pages p. 235

Commentary
This Urdu summary enumerates the eight conditions for Hajj to become fard (obligatory). They are: (1) Freedom: not a slave, (2) Islam: must be Muslim, (3) Sanity: not insane, (4) Adulthood: reached puberty, (5) Ability: having provision and mount as per the matn, (6) Support of dependents: must leave sufficient maintenance for family until return, (7) Health: physically able to perform Hajj, (8) Safety of route: road should be free from danger. These match the Arabic matn. Note the number '4' appears twice mistakenly; the correct list of 8 is given.

Key Terms
آزاد (azad): Free (not a slave). A slave is not obligated to perform Hajj.
توشہ پر قادر (toshah par qadir): Able to afford provisions and transport (mount).

Key Terms from Source Passage

Checkpoint

A) 5
B) 7
C) 8
D) 10

Key Takeaway
Hajj is obligatory only when a person meets all eight conditions: freedom, Islam, sanity, adulthood, ability, dependent support, health, and safe route.

Woman's Hajj Without Mahram: Ruling and Proof
Ruling on woman's Hajj without mahram with hadith proof

Learning Objective
By the end of this lesson, you will be able to state the Hanafi ruling on a woman performing Hajj without a mahram for a journey of three days or more, and explain the hadith evidence and its implication.

Core Idea
A woman's Hajj without a mahram for three days or more is not permissible.

This lesson addresses a common concern: can a woman perform Hajj without a male guardian? The Hanafi school, based on a clear hadith, prohibits such travel when the journey takes three days or more. We will examine the ruling, the proof, and how it applies in practice.

Guided Path
1
Identify the act and its ruling
What act is being ruled upon? It is a woman traveling to perform Hajj without a mahram (husband or unmarriageable male relative). The ruling is that it is not permissible.
The text says 'لا يَجُوزُهَا' – it is not allowed.
2
Locate the dalil
The proof is a hadith narrated by Abu Umamah from the Prophet (peace be upon him). The hadith is from Sunan al-Daraqutni.
The hadith is ahad, meaning its transmission is not mutawatir.
3
Trace the wajh al-dalalah
The hadith uses a negative command 'لَا تُسَافِرِ' (do not travel). In Hanafi usul, a negative command indicates prohibition (haram).
The phrase 'أَوْ تَحُجَّ' is interpreted as a continuation of the prohibition.
4
Note the ikhtilaf
Other schools (e.g., Shafi'i) may allow a woman to travel with a group of trustworthy women, based on other evidence. The Hanafi school insists on the mahram requirement.
The divergence stems from different interpretations of the hadith and its scope.
5
Evaluate the tarjih
The Hanafi position is mufta bihi (relied upon for fatwa) within the school, as it is based on the apparent meaning of the hadith and supported by the principle of blocking harm.
This ruling is from Zahir al-Riwayah and is not overridden by istihsan.

Source Text
⚠ Extracted via Advanced OCR ∼97% accuracy, minor errors may remain — always verify against original Arabic books
كِتَابُ الْحَجّ وَلَا يَجُوزُهَا أَنْ تَحُجَّ بِغَيْرِهِمَا إِذَا كَانَ بَيْنَهَا وَبَيْنَ مَكَّةَ مَسِيرَةُ ثَلَاثَةِ أَيَّامٍ فَصَاعِدًا وَيُعْتَبَرُ فِي الْمَرْأَةِ أَنْ يَكُونَ لَهَا مَحْرَمٌ يَحُجُ بِمَا عَنْ أَبِي أُمَامَةَ قَالَ: سَمِعْتُ رَسُولَ اللَّهِ صَلَّى اللهُ عَلَيْهِ وَسَلَّمَ يَقُولُ: «لَا تُسَافِرِ امْرَأَةٌ سَفَرًا ثَلَاثَةَ أَيَّامٍ أَوْ تَحُجَّ إِلَّا وَمَعَهَا زَوْجُهَا» (سنن الدار قطني باب كتاب الحج، نمبر: 2442)
The Book of Hajj: And it is not permissible for her to perform Hajj without the two of them (husband or mahram) when between her and Makkah is a distance of three days or more. And it is considered for the woman that she have a mahram to perform Hajj with, as narrated from Abu Umamah who said: I heard the Messenger of Allah (peace be upon him) say: 'A woman should not travel for three days or perform Hajj except with her husband with her.' (Sunan al-Daraqutni, Book of Hajj, no. 2442)
Source pages p. 235

Commentary
This passage states the ruling that a woman is prohibited from performing Hajj if she is not accompanied by a mahram (her husband or a male relative within prohibited degrees) when the distance to Makkah is three days or more. The hadith from Abu Umamah is cited as proof, indicating the general prohibition of travel without a mahram for such a distance. The Hanafi school considers this travel prohibited (haram) for women without a mahram, and thus Hajj is not obligatory on her if she cannot find a mahram.

Key Terms
مَحْرَم (mahram): A male relative whom a woman is permanently prohibited to marry (e.g., father, brother, son), with whom travel is permissible.
حَج (hajj): Pilgrimage to Makkah during specific days, obligatory once in a lifetime for those who can afford it.

Key Terms from Source Passage

Checkpoint
What is the ruling for a woman performing Hajj without a mahram from a distance of three days or more?
A) Permissible if she is with a group
B) Not permissible
C) Permissible only with a husband
D) Permissible if she is over 50 years old

Key Takeaway
A woman may not travel for Hajj without a mahram if the journey is three days or more, based on the explicit hadith, and failure to find a mahram lifts the obligation of Hajj.

Conditions for Hajj Being Obligatory
List of conditions for Hajj to be fard

Learning Objective
By the end of this lesson, you will be able to state the eight conditions for Hajj to be fard and identify which condition concerns financial ability.

Core Idea
Hajj is fard only when eight conditions are met — check each one before obligation arises.

This lesson covers the essential conditions (shara'it) that must be present for Hajj to become obligatory upon a Muslim. Understanding these conditions prevents confusion about when Hajj is binding and ensures that no one is charged with an obligation they cannot fulfill.

Guided Path
1
Identify the act and its ruling
Hajj is fard (obligatory) upon every Muslim who meets the conditions. This lesson lists those conditions.
The ruling is fard once in a lifetime.
2
List all conditions from the passage
Read the Urdu text carefully and enumerate the eight conditions: free, Muslim, sane, adult, able to afford provisions, providing for dependents, healthy, safe route.
The numbering in the source has a typo; ignore the numbers and focus on the content.
3
Categorize by type
Group conditions into: personal status (free, Muslim, sane, adult), financial (provisions, family support), and physical/contextual (health, safe route).
This helps in memorization and application.
4
Apply the conditions to a scenario
Consider a hypothetical Muslim in need: check each condition to determine if Hajj is obligatory.
If any condition is missing, Hajj is not fard.

This Urdu note lists the conditions that must be met for Hajj to be obligatory (fard) on a person. These are standard in Hanafi fiqh: being free (not a slave), Muslim, sane, adult (puberty), having the financial and physical ability (provisions, health), ensuring dependents are provided for, and a safe journey. The numbering is erroneous but the meaning is clear.

شرائط (shara'it): Conditions that must be fulfilled for an act to be obligatory.
وجوب (wujub): Obligation; the state of being fard or wajib.
توشه (toshah): Provisions, i.e., sufficient funds and supplies for the journey.

Hajj — Pilgrimage

Mawaqit: The Designated Places and Times for Ihram
Ruling on times and places for ihram with hadith proofs

Learning Objective
By the end of this lesson, you will be able to state the Hanafi ruling on entering ihram before the miqat and identify the correct miqat for pilgrims from different locations (beyond the miqat, within the miqat, and residents of Makkah).

Core Idea
The miqat binds the pilgrim: entering ihram before is allowed but against the sunnah; each pilgrim's miqat depends on their location.

The timing and location for entering the state of ihram are crucial for the validity of hajj and umrah. In this lesson, we examine the Hanafi position on the mawaqit—the designated places and times for ihram. The text from al-Quduri presents the basic rulings on when and where one should assume ihram, supported by the hadith of Ibn Abbas, which lists the mawaqit for different regions. We will also understand the distinction between the hill and the haram for those residing in Makkah.

Guided Path
1
Identify the ruling on early ihram
The text states: 'فَإِنْ قَدَّمَ الْإِحْرَامَ عَلَى هَذِهِ الْمَوَاقِيتِ جَازَ' – entering ihram before reaching the miqat is permissible (ja'iz). This is the first key ruling.
The word جَازَ indicates permissibility, not recommendation.
2
Distinguish the three categories of pilgrims
The passage divides pilgrims into three groups: (1) those coming from beyond the mawaqit – their miqat is the hill area before the Haram; (2) those residing within the miqat boundaries but not in Makkah – their miqat is the hill (wherever they live); (3) residents of Makkah – for hajj their miqat is the Haram itself, for umrah the hill.
The hill (حل) is the area between the miqat and the Haram.
3
Analyze the primary proof from hadith
The hadith of Ibn Abbas (Bukhari and Muslim) explicitly lists the mawaqit for different regions and includes the phrase: 'وَمَنْ كَانَ دُونَ ذَلِكَ فَمِنْ حَيْثُ أَنْشَأَ' – those within these boundaries start from their own homes. This is the direct dalil for the second category.
The dalil is zanni al-thubut (ahad) but qati al-dalala due to clear designation.
4
Extract the additional proof from the story of Aisha
The hadith of Jabir (Bukhari) relates that Aisha performed umrah from Tan'im (in the hill) after hajj, confirming that the miqat for umrah for a Makkan is the hill.
This ruling applies even after hajj, showing the general rule.
5
Consolidate the legal principles
The Urdu usool sections summarize: (1) entering ihram before miqat is unanimously allowed; (2) those within the miqat enter ihram from their point of departure; (3) the hill includes areas between the miqat and the Haram.
No dispute among schools on these basics.

Source Text
⚠ Extracted via Advanced OCR ∼97% accuracy, minor errors may remain — always verify against original Arabic books
كِتَابُ الْحَجّ ه جَازَ وَمَنْ كَانَ بَعْدَ الْمَوَاقِيتِ فَوَقْتُهُ الْحِلُ له وَمَنْ كَانَ بِمَكَّةَ فَمِيقَاتُهُ فِي الْحَجَ الْحَرَمُ وَفِي الْعُمْرَةِ الحِلُ
وجه : (۳) قول الصحابي لثبوت فَإِنْ قَدَّمَ الْإِحْرَامَ عَلَى هَذِهِ الْمَوَاقِيتِ جَازَا عَنِ ابْنِ عَبَّاسِ، «أَنَّهُ كَانَ يَرُدُّهُمْ إِلَى الْمَوَاقِيتِ، الَّذِينَ يَدْخُلُونَ مَكَّةَ بِغَيْرِ إِحْرَامٍ» (مصنف ابن أبي شيبة: في الرَّجُلِ إِذَا دَخَلَ مَكَّةَ بِغَيْرِ إِحْرَامٍ مَا يَصْنَعُ، نمبر: 14182)
دوجه: (1) الحديث لثبوت وَمَنْ كَانَ بَعْدَ الْمَوَاقِيتِ فَوَقْتُهُ الْحِلُ \ عَنِ ابْنِ عَبَّاسٍ، قَالَ: «إِنَّ النَّبِيِّ صَلَّى اللهُ عَلَيْهِ وَسَلَّمَ وَفَّتَ لِأَهْلِ المَدِينَةِ ذَا الحُلَيْفَةِ، وَلِأَهْلِ الشَّامِ الجُحْفَةَ، وَلِأَهْلِ نَجْدٍ قَرْنَ المَنازِلِ، وَلِأَهْلِ اليَمَن يَلَمْلَمَ، هُنَّ هَنَّ، وَلِمَنْ أَتَى عَلَيْهِنَّ مِنْ غَيْرِهِنَّ مِمَّنْ أَرَادَ الحَجَّ وَالْعُمْرَةَ، وَمَنْ كَانَ دُونَ ذَلِكَ، فَمِنْ حَيْثُ أَنْشَأَ حَتَّى أَهْلُ مَكَّةَ مِنْ مَكَّةَ» (بخاري: بَابُ مُهَلِ أَهْلِ مَكَّةَ لِلْحَجِّ وَالعُمْرَةِ، نمبر 1524/ مسلم بَابُ مَوَاقِيتِ الْحَجَ وَالْعُمْرَةِ، نمبر: 1181) وجه : (۲) الحديث لثبوت وَمَنْ كَانَ بَعْدَ الْمَوَاقِيتِ فَوَقْتُهُ الْحِلُ \ فَمَنْ كَانَ دُونَهُنَّ، فَمُهَلُّهُ مِنْ أَهْلِهِ، وَكَذَاكَ حَتَّى أَهْلُ مَكَّةَ يُهِلُّونَ مِنْهَا» بخاري: بَابُ مُهَلِ أَهْلِ مَكَّةَ لِلْحَجِّ وَالعُمْرَةِ، نمبر : 1526/ مسلم: بَابُ مَوَاقِيتِ الْحَجَ وَالْعُمْرَةِ، نمبر: 1181)
توجه: (1) الحديث لثبوت وَمَنْ كَانَ بِمَكَّةَ فَمِيقَاتُهُ فِي الْحَجَ الْحَرَمُ \ فَمَنْ كَانَ دُونَهُنَّ، فَمُهَلُهُ مِنْ أَهْلِهِ، وَكَذَاكَ حَتَّى أَهْل مَكَّةَ يُهلُّونَ مِنْهَا» بخاري: بَابُ مُهَل أَهْل مَكَّةَ لِلْحَجَ وَالعُمْرَةِ، غير : 1526/ مسلم: بَابُ مَوَاقِيتِ الْحَجِّ وَالْعُمْرَةِ، نمبر: 1181)
وجه : (۲) الحديث لثبوت وَمَنْ كَانَ بِمَكَّةَ فَمِيقَاتُهُ فِي الْحَجَ الْحَرَمُ \ حَدَّثَنِي جَابِرُ بْنُ عَبْدِ اللَّهِ رَضِيَ اللَّهُ عَنْهُمَا، أَنَّ النَّبِيَّ صَلَّى اللهُ عَلَيْهِ وَسَلَّمَ أَهَلَ ... قَالَتْ: يَا رَسُولَ اللَّهِ، أَتَنْطَلِقُونَ بِعُمْرَةٍ وَحَجَّةٍ وَأَنْطَلِقُ بِالْحَجِ؟ فَأَمَرَ عَبْدَ الرَّحْمَنِ بْنَ أَبِي بَكْرٍ أَنْ يَخْرُجَ مَعَهَا إِلَى التَّنْعِيمِ، فَاعْتَمَرَتْ بَعْدَ
الحج في ذي الحَجَّةِ. (بخاري بَابُ عُمْرَةِ التَّنْعِيمِ، نمبر : 1785/
اصول : میقات کے اندر اور حرم کے ارد گرد جو حصے ہیں انھیں حل کہتے ہیں۔
اصول: میقات سے قبل احرام باندھنا بالاتفاق جائز ہے۔ اصول : میقات کے اندر مقیم کے احرام باندھنے کی جگہ حل ہے یعنی وہ مقامات جہاں سے نکل رہے ہیں۔
Book of Hajj. It is allowed. And whoever is after the mawaqit, his time is the hill (outside Haram). And whoever is in Makkah, his miqat for hajj is the Haram, and for umrah the hill. Proof based on: (3) The statement of the Companion (Ibn Abbas) for proof: That if he brings forward ihram before these mawaqit, it is allowed. From Ibn Abbas: 'He used to turn them back to the mawaqit, those who entered Makkah without ihram' (Musannaf Ibn Abi Shaybah: no. 14182). Another aspect: (1) The hadith for proof of 'And whoever is after the mawaqit, his time is the hill': From Ibn Abbas, he said: 'The Prophet (peace be upon him) appointed for the people of Madinah Dhul-Hulayfah, for the people of Sham al-Juhfah, for the people of Najd Qarn al-Manazil, for the people of Yemen Yalamlam; they are for them and for those who come upon them from others who intend hajj and umrah. And whoever is within that, then from wherever he begins, including the people of Makkah from Makkah.' (Bukhari: Bab Muhal Ahl Makkah, no. 1524; Muslim: Bab Mawaqit al-Hajj, no. 1181) And another aspect: (2) The hadith for proof of 'And whoever is after the mawaqit, his time is the hill': 'So whoever is before them, his mahl is from his family, and likewise even the people of Makkah enter ihram from it.' (Bukhari: no. 1526; Muslim: no. 1181) Another aspect: (1) The hadith for proof of 'And whoever is in Makkah, his miqat for hajj is the Haram': 'So whoever is before them, his mahl is from his family, and likewise even the people of Makkah enter ihram from it.' (Bukhari: no. 1526; Muslim: no. 1181) Another aspect: (2) The hadith for proof of 'And whoever is in Makkah, his miqat for hajj is the Haram': Jabir ibn Abdullah narrated that the Prophet ... said: 'O Messenger of Allah, are you going for umrah and hajj while I go for hajj?' So he ordered Abdur-Rahman ibn Abi Bakr to go out with her to Tan'im, so she performed umrah after hajj in Dhul-Hijjah. (Bukhari: Bab Umrat al-Tan'im, no. 1785) Principles: The parts inside the miqat and around the Haram are called hill. Principle: Entering ihram before the miqat is unanimously allowed. Principle: The place of ihram for a resident within the miqat is the hill, meaning the places from which they are departing.
Source pages p. 236

Commentary
This passage from al-Quduri's Kitab al-Hajj lays out the rulings on the mawaqit (designated places and times) for entering ihram. The author first states the general rule: it is permissible to enter ihram before reaching the miqat, but the proper time for those who are beyond the mawaqit (i.e., traveling from afar) is the hill—the area outside the Haram. For a person residing in Makkah, the miqat for hajj is the Haram itself, while for umrah it is the hill. The commentary then provides multiple proofs from the hadith of Ibn Abbas, which list the mawaqit assigned by the Prophet (peace be upon him) for different regions. The hadith also clarifies that those living within the mawaqit (like Makkans) should enter ihram from their homes. The author also includes a hadith from Jabir about the permissibility of umrah after hajj for a Makkan woman, which supports the ruling that the miqat for umrah for a Makkan is the hill. Finally, the Urdu usool notes summarize: (1) the areas inside the miqat and around the Haram are called hill, (2) entering ihram before the miqat is unanimously allowed, and (3) a resident within the miqat enters ihram from the hill—i.e., the places from which they depart.

Key Terms
مِيقَات (mīqāt): The designated time or place for entering the state of ihram.
حِل (ḥill): The area outside the Haram of Makkah, including areas between miqat and haram.
حَرَم (ḥaram): The sacred precinct of Makkah.
إِحْرَام (iḥrām): The state of consecration for hajj or umrah, marked by specific dress and prohibitions.

Key Terms from Source Passage

Checkpoint
According to the Hanafi school, where should a person residing in Makkah enter ihram for hajj?
A) From the miqat of their hometown
B) From the Haram itself
C) From the hill (outside Haram)
D) From the nearest miqat

Key Takeaway
The miqat for ihram is a fixed boundary; entering before is permissible, but the sunnah is to do so at the designated point; residents within the miqat enter from their homes.

Hajj — Pilgrimage
beginner
6 min
Recommended Acts Before Ihram
Rulings with hadith proofs for pre-ihram sunan

Learning Objective
By the end of this lesson, you will be able to list the sunan before entering ihram, cite the hadith evidence for each, and explain the Hanafi preference for ghusl over wudu.

Core Idea
Before ihram, perform ghusl, wear two white garments, apply perfume, pray two rak'ahs, and recite the talbiyah.

Entering ihram is a sacred transition; the Prophet’s practice provides a clear precedent. This passage from al-Quduri enumerates the recommended acts to prepare for pilgrimage, each supported by authentic hadith.

Guided Path
1
Identify the five recommended acts
Read the matn and list: ghusl (or wudu), wearing two garments, applying perfume, praying two rak'ahs, and reciting talbiyah after the prayer.
Ghusl is preferred over wudu.
2
Match each act with its hadith proof
For each act, find the corresponding hadith cited: ghusl from Ibn Abbas (multiple narrations), perfume from A'ishah, two rak'ahs and talbiyah from Ibn Abbas and others.
The proofs are from Bukhari, Abu Dawud, etc.
3
Understand the Hanafi emphasis on ghusl
The matn explicitly says 'ghusl is better' (وَالْغُسْلُ أَفْضَلُ). Note that wudu suffices but ghusl is sunnah muakkadah.
This preference is supported by multiple ahadith.
4
Analyze the Shafi'i proof on perfume
The passage includes a Shafi'i evidence that the Prophet had perfume while in ihram. The Hanafi position maintains that perfume is applied before ihram, not during its state.
This is a legitimate ikhtilaf; the practical ruling is the same: perfume before ihram is allowed.
5
Apply the ruling in practice
When intending ihram, one should follow these sunan. Omitting them is not sinful but reduces the completeness of the sunnah.
These acts are mustahabb, not wajib.

Source Text
⚠ Extracted via Advanced OCR ∼97% accuracy, minor errors may remain — always verify against original Arabic books
كِتَابُ الْحَجّ ك وَإِذَا أَرَادَ الْإِحْرَامَ اغْتَسَلَ أَوْ تَوَضَّأَ وَالْغُسْلُ أَفْضَلُ وَلَبِسَ ثَوْبَيْنِ جَدِيدَيْنِ أَوْ غَسِيلَيْنِ وَمَسَّ طِيبًا إِنْ كَانَ لَهُ وَصَلَّى رَكْعَتَيْنِ وَيَقُولُ اللَّهُمَّ إِنِّي أُرِيدُ الْحَجَّ فَيَسِرْهُ لِي وَتَقَبَّلْهُ مِنِّي ثُمَّ يُلَي عَقِيبَ صَلَاتِهِ
وجه : (۱) الحديث لثبوت وَإِذَا أَرَادَ الْإِحْرَامَ اغْتَسَلَ أَوْ تَوَضَّأَ وَالْغُسْلُ أَفْضَلُ \ عَنْ عَبْدِ اللَّهِ بْنِ عَبَّاسٍ رَضِيَ اللَّهُ عَنْهُمَا، قَالَ: «انْطَلَقَ النَّبِيُّ صَلَّى اللَّهُ عَلَيْهِ وَسَلَّمَ مِنَ الْمَدِينَةِ بَعْدَ مَا تَرَجَّلَ، وَادَّهَنَ وَلَبِسَ إِزَارَهُ وَرِدَاءَهُ هُوَ وَأَصْحَابُهُ، فَلَمْ يَنْهَ عَنْ شَيْءٍ مِنَ الْأَرْدِيَةِ وَالْأُذُرِ (بخاري: بَابُ مَا يَلْبَسُ الْمُحْرِمُ مِنَ القِيَابِ وَالْأَرْدِيَةِ وَالْأُذُرِ، نمبر: 1545)
وجه (۲) الحديث لثبوت وَإِذَا أَرَادَ الْإِحْرَامَ اغْتَسَلَ أَوْ تَوَضَّأَ وَالْغُسْلُ أَفْضَلُ \ عَنِ ابْنِ عَبَّاسِ . قَالَ: «اغْتَسَلَ رَسُولُ اللَّهِ صَلَّى اللهُ عَلَيْهِ وَسَلَّمَ ثُمَّ لَبِسَ ثِيَابَهُ, فَلَمَّا أَتَى ذَا اخْلَيْفَةِ صَلَّى رَكْعَتَيْنِ ثُمَّ قَعَدَ عَلَى بَعِيرِهِ, فَلَمَّا اسْتَوَى بِهِ عَلَى الْبَيْدَاءِ أَحْرَمَ بِالْجَ» (سنن الدار قطني: كِتَابُ الْحَجّ، نمبر: 2432/ سنن للبيهقي: بَابُ الْغُسْلِ لِلْإِهْلَالِ نمبر: 8945/ الترمذي: بَابُ مَا جَاءَ فِي الاغْتِسَالِ عِنْدَ الإحرام/ نمبر (830)
وجه (۳) الحديث لثبوت وَإِذَا أَرَادَ الْإِحْرَامَ اغْتَسَلَ أَوْ تَوَضَّأَ وَالْغُسْلُ أَفْضَلُ \ عَنْ عَائِشَةَ رَضِيَ اللَّهُ عَنْهَا زَوْجِ النَّبِيِّ صَلَّى اللهُ عَلَيْهِ وَسَلَّمَ قَالَتْ: كُنْتُ أُطَيْبُ رَسُولَ اللَّهِ صَلَّى اللهُ عَلَيْهِ وَسَلَّمَ لإحْرَامِهِ حِينَ يُخرمُ، وَلِلَّهِ قَبْلَ أَنْ يَطُوفَ بِالْبَيْتِ» (بخاري بَابُ الطَّيبِ عِنْدَ الإِحْرَامِ، غير: 1539/ أبو داؤد: بَابُ الطِيبِ عِنْدَ الْإِحْرَامِ، نمبر: 1745)
وجه (1) دليل الشافعي الحديث لثبوت وَإِذَا أَرَادَ الْإِحْرَامَ اغْتَسَلَ أَوْ تَوَضَّأَ وَالْغُسْلُ أَفْضَلُ \ عَنْ عَائِشَةَ رَضِيَ اللَّهُ عَنْهَا، قَالَتْ: كَأَيّ أَنْظُرُ إِلَى وَبِيصِ الطّيبِ فِي مَفَارِقِ رَسُولِ اللَّهِ صَلَّى اللَّهُ عَلَيْهِ وَسَلَّمَ وَهُوَ مُحْرِمٌ» (بخاري : بَابُ الطَّيبِ عِنْدَ الإِحْرَامِ، نمبر : 1538/)
وجه (۲) الحديث لثبوت وَإِذَا أَرَادَ الْإِحْرَامَ اغْتَسَلَ أَوْ تَوَضَّأَ وَالْغُسْلُ أَفْضَلُ \ قُلْتُ لِعَبْدِ اللَّهِ بْنِ عَبَّاسٍ: . . . خَرَجَ رَسُولُ اللَّهِ صَلَّى اللهُ عَلَيْهِ وَسَلَّمَ حَاجًا فَلَمَّا صَلَّى فِي مَسْجِدِهِ بِذِي الحْلَيْفَةِ رَكْعَتَيْهِ أَوْجَبَ فِي مَجْلِسِهِ، فَأَهَلَّ بِالْجَ حِينَ فَرَغَ مِنْ رَكْعَتَيْهِ، (أبو داؤد: بَابٌ فِي وَقْتِ الْإِحْرَامِ، نمبر : 1770/ بخاري : بَابُ الإِهْلاَلِ مُسْتَقْبِلَ القِبْلَةِ، نمبر: 1554
اصول : احرام وہ خاص کپڑا جو خاص طریقے سے باندھا جاتا ہے ، وہ حج یا عمرہ کرنے والے کے لئے لازم ہے۔
Book of Hajj. And when one intends ihram, he should perform ghusl or wudu, and ghusl is better, and wear two new or washed garments, and apply perfume if he has it, and pray two rak'ahs, and say: O Allah, I intend Hajj, so make it easy for me and accept it from me. Then he should recite the talbiyah after his prayer. Proof based on: (1) The hadith for proof: From Abdullah ibn Abbas, may Allah be pleased with them, he said: 'The Prophet (peace be upon him) set out from Madinah after combing his hair, oiling it, and wearing his izaar and ridaa, he and his companions, and he did not forbid anything from the cloaks and loincloths.' (Bukhari: Bab ma yalbasu al-muhrim min al-qiyab..., no. 1545) (2) The hadith for proof: From Ibn Abbas, he said: 'The Messenger of Allah (peace be upon him) performed ghusl, then wore his clothes. When he came to Dhul-Hulayfah, he prayed two rak'ahs, then sat on his camel. When he stood up on al-Bayda', he entered ihram for hajj.' (Daraqutni: Hajj no. 2432; Bayhaqi: Bab al-Ghusl li al-Ihlal no. 8945; Tirmidhi: Bab ma ja'a fi al-ightisal 'inda al-ihram no. 830) (3) The hadith for proof: From A'ishah, the wife of the Prophet (peace be upon him), she said: 'I used to perfume the Messenger of Allah for his ihram when he entered ihram, and for his ihram before he circumambulated the House.' (Bukhari: Bab al-tib 'inda al-ihram, no. 1539; Abu Dawud: Bab al-tib 'inda al-ihram no. 1745) (1) Proof of al-Shafi'i: the hadith for proof: From A'ishah, she said: 'I can still see the glistening of the perfume in the parting of the Messenger of Allah while he was in ihram.' (Bukhari: no. 1538) (2) The hadith for proof: I said to Abdullah ibn Abbas: '... The Messenger of Allah set out as a pilgrim, and when he prayed two rak'ahs in his mosque at Dhul-Hulayfah, he made it obligatory in his sitting, and he began the talbiyah for hajj when he finished his two rak'ahs.' (Abu Dawud: Bab fi waqt al-ihram no. 1770; Bukhari: Bab al-ihlal mustaqbil al-qibla no. 1554) Principle: Ihram is the specific cloth tied in a specific manner; it is necessary for the one performing hajj or umrah.
Source pages p. 237

Commentary
This passage from al-Quduri outlines the sunan (recommended acts) to be performed before entering ihram. The matn lists: performing ghusl (or wudu, with ghusl preferred), wearing two new or washed garments, applying perfume if available, praying two rak'ahs, and reciting the talbiyah (لبيك اللهم حجاً) immediately after the prayer. The commentary provides multiple hadith proofs for each of these acts. The hadith of Ibn Abbas shows the Prophet combed and oiled his hair and wore the izaar and ridaa. The hadith of Ibn Abbas also narrates that the Prophet performed ghusl, dressed, prayed two rak'ahs, and then entered ihram at Dhul-Hulayfah. A'ishah's hadith establishes the use of perfume before ihram. Another hadith clarifies that the talbiyah should be recited after the two rak'ahs. The final Urdu note defines ihram as the specific garments tied in a particular manner, which is necessary for hajj and umrah.

Key Terms
غُسْل (ghusl): Full body washing; recommended before ihram and considered superior to wudu.
ثَوْبَان (thawbān): Two garments worn by the pilgrim, typically an izaar (lower wrap) and ridaa (upper wrap).
طِيب (ṭīb): Perfume or fragrant oil; applying it before ihram is recommended, but use during ihram is prohibited.
تَلْبِيَة (talbiyah): The phrase recited upon entering ihram: 'Labbayka Allahumma labbayka...'

Key Terms from Source Passage

Checkpoint
Which of the following is NOT recommended before ihram according to the text?
A) Performing ghusl
B) Wearing two new garments
C) Applying perfume
D) Fasting

Key Takeaway
Performing ghusl, wearing two garments, applying perfume, praying two rak'ahs, and reciting the talbiyah are sunnah acts before ihram, each supported by the Prophet's practice.

Hajj — Pilgrimage
beginner
8 min
The Recommended Acts Before Ihram and Their Proofs
Matn with multiple hadith proofs for the sunan of ihram

Learning Objective
By the end of this lesson, you will be able to list the six recommended acts (sunan) before ihram and cite the corresponding hadith proofs for each.

Core Idea
Before entering ihram, the Prophet set a pattern of ghusl, two garments, perfume, prayer, and talbiyah — all sunnah muakkadah rooted in authentic hadith.

This lesson covers the recommended acts (sunan) that a pilgrim should perform before entering the state of ihram, as compiled by Imam al-Quduri in his matn. These acts are derived from the Prophet's practice (Sunnah), and each has its own evidence. Understanding these sunan helps the pilgrim follow the prophetic model more completely, while recognizing that omission does not invalidate the ihram.

Guided Path
1
Identify the six recommended acts from the matn
Read the matn text and extract each action mentioned: ghusl (or wudu), wearing two new/washed garments, applying perfume, praying two rak'ahs, making the intention supplication, and pronouncing the talbiyah.
The matn also notes that ghusl is superior to wudu.
2
Locate the hadith proof for each act
The author provides three hadiths from Ibn Abbas and Aisha. Match each act to its proof: ghusl and two rak'ahs from Ibn Abbas (hadith 2), garments from Ibn Abbas (hadith 1), perfume from Aisha (hadith 3), and the sequence of prayer then talbiyah from additional narrations.
Hadith references are from Bukhari, Abu Dawud, and others.
3
Understand the Hanafi hukm level
These acts are classified as sunnah muakkadah (emphasized recommended) – not obligatory. The Prophet's actions indicate desirability, not necessity.
This is in contrast to fard/wajib – omitting these does not require compensation.
4
Note the intra-madhhab detail on ghusl and wudu
Both ghusl and wudu are permissible, but ghusl is better (afdal). This is based on the hadith where the Prophet performed ghusl before ihram.
The source does not mention obligatory nature; it remains sunnah.
5
Examine the cross-madhhab dispute on perfume before ihram
The Hanafi school permits applying perfume before ihram based on Aisha's hadith that she perfumed the Prophet. The Shafi'i school considers it makruh (disliked) because perfume remains during ihram. The Hanafi response is that the prohibition of perfume after ihram does not apply before.
This illustrates how different schools weigh conflicting evidences.

Source Text
⚠ Extracted via Advanced OCR ∼97% accuracy, minor errors may remain — always verify against original Arabic books
كِتَابُ الْحَجّ
وَإِذَا أَرَادَ الْإِحْرَامَ اغْتَسَلَ أَوْ تَوَضَّأَ وَالْغُسْلُ أَفْضَلُ وَلَبِسَ ثَوْبَيْنِ جَدِيدَيْنِ أَوْ غَسِيلَيْنِ وَمَسَّ طِيبًا إِنْ كَانَ لَهُ وَصَلَّى رَكْعَتَيْنِ وَيَقُولُ اللَّهُمَّ إِنِّي أُرِيدُ الْحَجَّ فَيَسِرْهُ لِي وَتَقَبَّلْهُ مِنِّي ثُمَّ يُلَي عَقِيبَ صَلَاتِهِ
وَجْهٌ (١) الْحَدِيثُ لِثُبُوتِ... عَنْ عَبْدِ اللَّهِ بْنِ عَبَّاسٍ رَضِيَ اللَّهُ عَنْهُمَا قَالَ: «انْطَلَقَ النَّبِيُّ صَلَّى اللَّهُ عَلَيْهِ وَسَلَّمَ مِنَ الْمَدِينَةِ بَعْدَ مَا تَرَجَّلَ، وَادَّهَنَ وَلَبِسَ إِزَارَهُ وَرِدَاءَهُ هُوَ وَأَصْحَابُهُ، فَلَمْ يَنْهَ عَنْ شَيْءٍ مِنَ الْأَرْدِيَةِ وَالْأُزُرِ» (بخاري: بَابُ مَا يَلْبَسُ الْمُحْرِمُ مِنَ الْقِيَابِ وَالْأَرْدِيَةِ وَالْأُزُرِ، نمر: 1545)
وَجْهٌ (٢) الْحَدِيثُ لِثُبُوتِ... عَنِ ابْنِ عَبَّاسٍ قَالَ: «اغْتَسَلَ رَسُولُ اللَّهِ صَلَّى اللهُ عَلَيْهِ وَسَلَّمَ ثُمَّ لَبِسَ ثِيَابَهُ، فَلَمَّا أَتَى ذَا الْحُلَيْفَةِ صَلَّى رَكْعَتَيْنِ ثُمَّ قَعَدَ عَلَى بَعِيرِهِ، فَلَمَّا اسْتَوَى بِهِ عَلَى الْبَيْدَاءِ أَحْرَمَ بِالْحَجِّ» (سنن الدارقطني: كِتَابُ الْحَجِّ، نمر: 2432/ سنن البيهقي: بَابُ الْغُسْلِ لِلْإِهْلَالِ، نمر: 8945/ الترمذي: بَابُ مَا جَاءَ فِي الِاغْتِسَالِ عِنْدَ الْإِحْرَامِ، نمر: 830)
وَجْهٌ (٣) الْحَدِيثُ لِثُبُوتِ... عَنْ عَائِشَةَ رَضِيَ اللَّهُ عَنْهَا زَوْجِ النَّبِيِّ صَلَّى اللهُ عَلَيْهِ وَسَلَّمَ قَالَتْ: «كُنْتُ أُطَيِّبُ رَسُولَ اللَّهِ صَلَّى اللهُ عَلَيْهِ وَسَلَّمَ لِإِحْرَامِهِ حِينَ يُحْرِمُ، وَلِحِلِّهِ قَبْلَ أَنْ يَطُوفَ بِالْبَيْتِ» (بخاري: بَابُ الطِّيبِ عِنْدَ الْإِحْرَامِ، نمر: 1539/ أبو داوود: بَابُ الطِّيبِ عِنْدَ الْإِحْرَامِ، نمر: 1745)
وَجْهٌ (١) دَلِيلُ الشَّافِعِيِّ الْحَدِيثُ لِثُبُوتِ... عَنْ عَائِشَةَ رَضِيَ اللَّهُ عَنْهَا قَالَتْ: «كَأَنِّي أَنْظُرُ إِلَى وَبِيصِ الطِّيبِ فِي مَفَارِقِ رَسُولِ اللَّهِ صَلَّى اللَّهُ عَلَيْهِ وَسَلَّمَ وَهُوَ مُحْرِمٌ» (بخاري: بَابُ الطِّيبِ عِنْدَ الْإِحْرَامِ، نمر: 1538)
وَجْهٌ (٢) الْحَدِيثُ لِثُبُوتِ... قُلْتُ لِعَبْدِ اللَّهِ بْنِ عَبَّاسٍ: ... خَرَجَ رَسُولُ اللَّهِ صَلَّى اللهُ عَلَيْهِ وَسَلَّمَ حَاجًّا فَلَمَّا صَلَّى فِي مَسْجِدِهِ بِذِي الْحُلَيْفَةِ رَكْعَتَيْهِ أَوْجَبَ فِي مَجْلِسِهِ، فَأَهَلَّ بِالْحَجِّ حِينَ فَرَغَ مِنْ رَكْعَتَيْهِ (أبو داوود: بَابٌ فِي وَقْتِ الْإِحْرَامِ، نمر: 1770/ بخاري: بَابُ الْإِهْلَالِ مُسْتَقْبِلَ الْقِبْلَةِ، نمر: 1554)
Book of Hajj. And when one intends to enter ihram, he should perform ghusl or wudu, and ghusl is better, and he should wear two new garments or washed ones, and apply perfume if he has it, and pray two rak'ahs, and say: 'O Allah, I intend Hajj, so make it easy for me and accept it from me.' Then he should pronounce the talbiyah immediately after his prayer. Aspect (1): The hadith for establishing... from Abdullah ibn Abbas... Aspect (2): The hadith for establishing... from Ibn Abbas... Aspect (3): The hadith for establishing... from Aisha... Aspect (1): The proof of al-Shafi'i... from Aisha... Aspect (2): The hadith for establishing... I said to Abdullah ibn Abbas...
Source pages p. 237

Commentary
This passage from al-Quduri's matn lists the recommended acts (sunan) before entering the state of ihram for Hajj. It is a ruling statement with multiple hadith proofs. The author presents the text of the matn, then provides evidence from the Sunnah. The rulings: (1) Ghusl is preferred over wudu, based on the hadith that the Prophet performed ghusl before ihram. (2) Wearing two new or washed garments—the hadith from Ibn Abbas shows the Prophet wore his izār and ridā'. (3) Applying perfume is recommended, as Aisha reports she perfumed the Prophet for ihram. (4) Praying two rak'ahs before ihram—the Prophet prayed at Dhul-Hulayfah. (5) Making the intention and supplication. (6) Pronouncing the talbiyah immediately after the prayer. The proofs are all from authentic hadith. Note the inclusion of a proof from al-Shafi'i's viewpoint on perfume, though the Hanafi position remains that perfume is allowed before ihram. The Urdu marginal note on page 237 defines ihram as special clothing.

Key Terms
إحرام (ihrām): The state of sacred consecration for Hajj or Umrah, initiated by the intention and talbiyah, and accompanied by specific prohibitions.
تلبيَة (talbiyah): The prescribed words recited upon entering ihram, beginning with 'Labbayka Allahumma labbayka...'
غُسْل (ghusl): Full body wash with water, recommended before ihram and considered superior to wudu.
وُضُوء (wudu): Ablution with water, an alternative to ghusl before ihram, though ghusl is better.
طِيب (tib): Perfume or fragrance; recommended to apply before ihram according to the Hanafi school.

Key Terms from Source Passage

According to al-Quduri, which of the following acts is considered superior before entering ihram?
A) Performing wudu only
B) Performing ghusl
C) Both ghusl and wudu are equal
D) Neither is required

Key Takeaway
The six sunan before ihram are all recommended (sunnah muakkadah), not obligatory, and each is supported by authentic hadith from the Prophet's practice.

Talbiyah, Intention, and Prohibitions in Ihram
Exposition of talbiyah and prohibitions in ihram

Learning Objective
By the end of this lesson, you will be able to state the wording of the talbiyah for ifrad, identify when ihram is entered, and explain the prohibitions of rafath, fusuq, and jidal in Hajj.

Core Idea
Ihram is entered by talbiyah with intention; from then on, rafath, fusuq, jidal, and hunting are strictly forbidden.

The source opens the Book of Hajj by establishing the core acts of entering ihram: intention through talbiyah. The mu'tamad wording of talbiyah is given, and the moment of ihram is defined. After entering ihram, certain prohibitions become binding: sexual relations, sin, disputation, and hunting. This lesson unpacks these rulings, their proofs from the Quran and Sunnah, and the Hanafi perspective on their obligatory nature.

Guided Path
1
Identify the talbiyah wording
Read the Arabic text of the talbiyah as given in the matn. Note that it is for ifrad (Hajj alone) but also used for tamattu' and qiran with slight modifications.
The wording is: 'Labbaik Allahumma labbaik, labbaik la sharika laka labbaik, inna al-hamda wan-ni'mata laka wal-mulka, la sharika laka.'
2
Determine when ihram is entered
The matn states: 'When he recites talbiyah, he has entered ihram.' The intention (niyyah) is made with the talbiyah, and the state begins immediately.
Hanafi: intention and talbiyah together are the rukn of ihram.
3
List the prohibitions
From the Quran (2:197) and Sunnah, the matn lists: rafath (sexual relations), fusuq (sin/obscenity), jidal (disputation), and hunting game (citing 5:96).
These are wajib to avoid; violation requires dam (penalty).
4
Understand the dalil for each prohibition
Rafath, fusuq, jidal: Quran 2:197. Hunting: Quran 5:96 and hadith of Abu Qatada. The imperative tone indicates prohibition.
Hanafi: these are zanni al-dalala but accepted due to consensus.
5
Note the Hanafi hukm level
Avoiding these prohibitions is wajib (obligatory), not fard. Omission (violation) necessitates dam, not invalidation of Hajj.
Wajib because based on ahad hadith; fard would require qat'i dalil.

Source Text
⚠ Extracted via Advanced OCR ∼97% accuracy, minor errors may remain — always verify against original Arabic books
كِتَابُ الْحَجِّ فَإِنْ كَانَ مُفْرِدًا بِالْحَجِّ نَوَى بِتَلْبِيَتِهِ الْحَجَّ، وَالتَّلْبِيَةُ: لَبَّيْكَ اللَّهُمَّ لَبَّيْكَ، لَبَّيْكَ لَا شَرِيكَ لَكَ لَبَّيْكَ، إِنَّ الْحَمْدَ وَالنِّعْمَةَ لَكَ وَالْمُلْكَ، لَا شَرِيكَ لَكَ. وَلَا يَنْبَغِي أَنْ يُحِلَّ بِشَيْءٍ مِنْ هَذِهِ الْكَلِمَاتِ، فَإِنْ زَادَ فِيهَا جَازَ. فَإِذَا لَبَّى فَقَدْ أَحْرَمَ، فَلْيَتَّقِ مَا نَهَى اللَّهُ عَنْهُ مِنَ الرَّفَثِ وَالْفُسُوقِ وَالْجِدَالِ فِي الْحَجِّ، وَلَا يَقْتُلُ صَيْدًا وَلَا يُشِيرُ إِلَيْهِ وَلَا يَدُلُّ عَلَيْهِ. وَإِذَا أَرَادَ الْإِحْرَامَ اغْتَسَلَ أَوْ تَوَضَّأَ، وَالْغُسْلُ أَفْضَلُ. وَلَا يَلْبَسُ قَمِيصًا وَلَا سَرَاوِيلَ وَلَا عِمَامَةً وَلَا قَلَنْسُوَةً وَلَا قَبَاءً وَلَا خُفَّيْنِ إِلَّا أَنْ لَا يَجِدَ النَّعْلَيْنِ فَلْيَقْطَعْهُمَا أَسْفَلَ الْكَعْبَيْنِ.
The Book of Hajj: If one is performing Hajj alone (ifrad), he intends Hajj through his talbiyah. The talbiyah is: 'Labbaik Allahumma labbaik, labbaik la sharika laka labbaik, inna al-hamda wan-ni'mata laka wal-mulka, la sharika laka.' It is not appropriate to omit any of these words; if he adds to them, it is permissible. When he recites talbiyah, he has entered ihram. Let him fear what Allah has forbidden of sexual relations, sin, and disputation in Hajj, and let him not kill game, nor point to it, nor guide to it. When he intends ihram, he should perform ghusl or wudu, and ghusl is better. He should not wear a shirt, trousers, turban, cap, cloak, or khuffs (leather socks) unless he cannot find sandals; then let him cut them below the ankles.
Source pages p. 238

Commentary
This is a ruling statement with proofs from the Hanafi school's Al-Quduri text, accompanied by hadith evidence. The passage covers several ihram rulings: (1) The wording of the talbiyah for the mufrid (one performing Hajj only) and that adding to it is permissible. (2) Upon reciting talbiyah, one enters ihram and must refrain from rafath (sexual relations/intercourse), fusuq (sin, i.e., obscenity), and jidal (disputation) as per Quran 2:197. (3) The prohibition of hunting game, pointing to it, or guiding others to it, based on Quran 5:96. (4) The recommendation of ghusl before ihram, with wudu also sufficient but ghusl superior, following the Prophet's practice. (5) The prohibition of sewn garments such as shirts, trousers, turbans, caps, cloaks, and khuffs for men, except that one without sandals may wear khuffs cut below the ankles. These are from the Sunnah, with detailed hadith references. The Urdu note adds that ghusl before ihram is superior because the Prophet performed it, and that caps and turbans are prohibited in ihram.

Key Terms
التَّلْبِيَةُ (at-talbiyah): The phrase recited upon entering ihram, 'Labbaik Allahumma labbaik...'
الإِحْرَامُ (al-ihram): The sacred state entered by intention and talbiyah for Hajj/Umrah
الرَّفَثُ (ar-rafath): Sexual intercourse and its preliminaries
الْفُسُوقُ (al-fusuq): Sin, specifically obscene speech or disobedience
الْجِدَالُ (al-jidal): Quarreling or disputation, especially in matters of Hajj

Key Terms from Source Passage

Checkpoint
What is the legal ruling (hukm) for a pilgrim who commits jidal (disputation) in ihram?
A) Hajj becomes invalid and must be repeated.
B) Hajj is valid but a dam (penalty) is required.
C) No penalty, as it is merely makruh.
D) The pilgrim must stop and perform sajdah al-sahw.

Key Takeaway
Talbiyah with intention enters one into ihram, after which rafath, fusuq, jidal, and hunting are wajib to avoid; violations require dam.

Prohibited Garments in Ihram and the Exception for Khuffs
Exposition of prohibited garments and ghusl before ihram

Learning Objective
By the end of this lesson, you will be able to list the garments prohibited for a muhrim, explain the ruling on ghusl before ihram, and apply the exception allowing khuffs cut below the ankles if sandals are unavailable.

Core Idea
A muhrim may not wear sewn garments; if sandals are unavailable, khuffs may be worn but must be cut below the ankles.

After establishing the prohibitions related to conduct, the text moves to dress: the muhrim must avoid sewn garments that are form-fitting or cover the body parts typically covered by ordinary clothes. The Prophet ﷺ explicitly forbade shirts, trousers, turbans, cloaks, and khuffs. Ghusl before ihram is recommended. For the khuff exception, the matn provides a specific condition: only if sandals are not found, and then the khuffs must be cut below the ankles. This lesson examines the wisdom behind the dress code and the precise application of the exception.

Guided Path
1
List the prohibited garments
Read the text: 'la yalbasu qamisan wa la sarawila wa la 'imamata wa la qalansuwata wa la qaba'a wa la khuffayni' – shirt, trousers, turban, cap, cloak, and khuffs are prohibited.
For men only; women may wear sewn garments but not gloves or niqab.
2
Understand the wisdom behind the prohibition
These garments are sewn to fit the body, which contradicts the state of humility and equality in ihram. The muhrim should wear the izar and rida (unsewn wrap).
The prohibition aims to prevent pride and remind of the Hereafter.
3
Learn the ghusl recommendation
The matn says: 'idha arada al-ihrama ightasala aw tawaddaa, wal-ghuslu afdal' – ghusl is better but wudu is sufficient. This is based on the Prophet's practice.
Ghusl is sunnah mu'akkadah, not wajib.
4
Study the khuffs exception and its condition
If one cannot find sandals (na'layn), he may wear khuffs but must cut them below the ankles. The cutting removes the form-fitting nature and makes them resemble sandals.
The cut must be below the ankle bone (ka'b), as per Hanafi interpretation.

Source Text
⚠ Extracted via Advanced OCR ∼97% accuracy, minor errors may remain — always verify against original Arabic books
كِتَابُ الْحَجِّ فَإِنْ كَانَ مُفْرِدًا بِالْحَجِّ نَوَى بِتَلْبِيَتِهِ الْحَجَّ، وَالتَّلْبِيَةُ: لَبَّيْكَ اللَّهُمَّ لَبَّيْكَ، لَبَّيْكَ لَا شَرِيكَ لَكَ لَبَّيْكَ، إِنَّ الْحَمْدَ وَالنِّعْمَةَ لَكَ وَالْمُلْكَ، لَا شَرِيكَ لَكَ. وَلَا يَنْبَغِي أَنْ يُحِلَّ بِشَيْءٍ مِنْ هَذِهِ الْكَلِمَاتِ، فَإِنْ زَادَ فِيهَا جَازَ. فَإِذَا لَبَّى فَقَدْ أَحْرَمَ، فَلْيَتَّقِ مَا نَهَى اللَّهُ عَنْهُ مِنَ الرَّفَثِ وَالْفُسُوقِ وَالْجِدَالِ فِي الْحَجِّ، وَلَا يَقْتُلُ صَيْدًا وَلَا يُشِيرُ إِلَيْهِ وَلَا يَدُلُّ عَلَيْهِ. وَإِذَا أَرَادَ الْإِحْرَامَ اغْتَسَلَ أَوْ تَوَضَّأَ، وَالْغُسْلُ أَفْضَلُ. وَلَا يَلْبَسُ قَمِيصًا وَلَا سَرَاوِيلَ وَلَا عِمَامَةً وَلَا قَلَنْسُوَةً وَلَا قَبَاءً وَلَا خُفَّيْنِ إِلَّا أَنْ لَا يَجِدَ النَّعْلَيْنِ فَلْيَقْطَعْهُمَا أَسْفَلَ الْكَعْبَيْنِ.
The Book of Hajj: If one is performing Hajj alone (ifrad), he intends Hajj through his talbiyah. The talbiyah is: 'Labbaik Allahumma labbaik, labbaik la sharika laka labbaik, inna al-hamda wan-ni'mata laka wal-mulka, la sharika laka.' It is not appropriate to omit any of these words; if he adds to them, it is permissible. When he recites talbiyah, he has entered ihram. Let him fear what Allah has forbidden of sexual relations, sin, and disputation in Hajj, and let him not kill game, nor point to it, nor guide to it. When he intends ihram, he should perform ghusl or wudu, and ghusl is better. He should not wear a shirt, trousers, turban, cap, cloak, or khuffs (leather socks) unless he cannot find sandals; then let him cut them below the ankles.

(2) Upon reciting talbiyah, one enters ihram and must refrain from rafath (sexual relations/intercourse), fusuq (sin, i.e., obscenity), and jidal (disputation) as per Quran 2:197. (3) The prohibition of hunting game, pointing to it, or guiding others to it, based on Quran 5:96. Key Takeaway
Sewn garments are prohibited for men in ihram; only if sandals are unavailable may khuffs be worn, provided they are cut below the ankles.
