Prohibitions of Covering Head, Perfume, and Shaving in Ihram
Rulings with proofs for three ihram prohibitions: head covering, perfume, shaving.

Learning Objective
By the end of this lesson, you will be able to state the three prohibitions for a muhrim, identify the proof for each, and explain the distinction between necessary and unnecessary violations with their consequences.

Core Idea
Three acts are haram in ihram: covering head/face, using perfume, shaving hair – each has a clear proof and fidya exception for necessity.

This lesson examines three key prohibitions for the muhrim/muhrimah: covering the head or face, applying perfume, and shaving or cutting hair. Each prohibition is supported by textual evidence from the Quran and Sunnah, and the Hanafi school provides detailed rulings on the consequences of violation.

Guided Path
1
Identify the prohibitions
Read the passage and list the three categories: covering head/face, using perfume, and shaving/cutting hair. Note that these apply to both men and women with specific details.
Men are prohibited from covering the head; women are prohibited from covering the face with niqab.
2
Examine proof for covering head/face
Review the hadith of Ibn Umar (prohibition of niqab and gloves) and the hadith of Aisha (temporary covering when non-mahram pass). Understand that the general prohibition is for permanent covering, but temporary covering is permitted for necessity.
The hadith of Aisha shows the specific practice of the Prophet's wives.
3
Examine proof for perfume
Consider the hadith of Ya'la ibn Umayyah (removing cloak with perfume) and the hadith of Ibn Umar (prohibition of garments dyed with saffron). Note that any scented product is prohibited for the muhrim.
Khaluq is specifically mentioned because it was a common perfume.
4
Examine proof for shaving/cutting
Read the Quranic verse (2:196) prohibiting shaving the head before the sacrifice, and the statement of al-Hasan and Ata regarding cutting nails. Understand that the prohibition extends to all hair and nails.
The verse explicitly allows shaving for illness but requires fidya.
5
Apply the ruling
For each prohibition, determine the consequence if violated: without necessity, it is haram and requires fidya; with necessity (illness, extreme heat), it is permitted but fidya is still required. Fidya is either fasting three days, feeding six poor, or sacrificing a sheep.
The Hanafi school distinguishes between intentional violation (sinful) and necessary violation (permissible with compensation).

Source Text
⚠ Extracted via Advanced OCR ∼97% accuracy, minor errors may remain — always verify against original Arabic books
وَلَا يُغَطِّي رَأْسَهُ وَلا وَجْهَهُ ١٣ وَلا يَمَسُّ طِيبًا وَلَا يَحْلِقُ رَأْسَهُ وَلَا شَعْرَ بَدَنِهِ وَلَا يَقُصُّ مِنْ اللِّحْيَةِ الْوَجْهُ: (١) الحديث لثبوت وَلَا يُغَطِي رَأْسَهُ وَلَاوَجْهَهُ عَنِ ابْنِ عُمَرَ، عَنِ النَّبِيِّ صَلَّى اللَّهُ عَلَيْهِ وَسَلَّمَ قَالَ: «الْمُحْرِمَةُ لَا تَنْتَقِبُ وَلَا تَلْبَسُ الْقُفَّازَيْنِ» أبو داؤد: بَابُ مَا يَلْبَسُ الْمُحْرِمُ : 1826) وجه: (٢) الحديث لثبوت وَلَا يُغَطِي رَأْسَهُ وَلَا وَجْهَهُ \ عَنْ عَائِشَةَ، قَالَتْ: «كَانَ الرَّكْبَانُ يَمُرُّونَ بِنَا وَنَحْنُ مَعَ رَسُولِ اللَّهِ صَلَّى اللهُ عَلَيْهِ وَسَلَّمَ مُحْرِمَاتٌ، فَإِذَا حَاذَوْا بِنَا سَدَلَتْ إِحْدَانَا جِلْبَابَهَا مِنْ رَأْسِهَا عَلَى وَجْهِهَا فَإِذَا جَاوَزُونَا كَشَفْنَاهُ أبو داؤد: بَابُ مَا يَلْبَسُ الْمُحْرِمُ، نمبر: 1833) ۱۲ وجه (۱) الحديث لثبوت وَلَا يَمَسُّ طِيبًا \ أَخْبَرَنِي صَفْوَانُ بْنُ يَعْلَى، عَنْ أَبِيهِ رَضِيَ اللَّهُ عَنْهُ، قَالَ: كُنَّا مَعَ رَسُولِ اللهِ صَلَّى اللهُ عَلَيْهِ وَسَلَّمَ، فَأَتَاهُ رَجُلٌ عَلَيْهِ جُبَّةٌ بِمَا أَثَرٌ مِنْ خَلُوقِ، فَقَالَ يَا رَسُولَ اللَّهِ، إِنِّي أَحْرَمْتُ بِعُمْرَةٍ، فَكَيْفَ أَفْعَلُ؟ . . . فَقَالَ: «انْزِغْ عَنْكَ جُبَّتَكَ، وَاغْسِلْ أَثَرَ الخلُوقِ الَّذِي بِكَ (مسلم) بَابُ مَا يُبَاحُ لِلْمُحْرِم بِحَجَ أَوْ عُمْرَةِ، وَمَا لَا يُبَاحُ وَبَيَانِ تَحْرِيمِ الطَّيبِ عَلَيْهِ : 1180/ بخاري: بَابُ غَسْلِ الخَلُوقِ ثَلَاثَ مَرَّاتٍ مِنَ الشَّيَابِ، نمبر : 1536) وجه : (۲) الحديث لثبوت وَلَا يَمَسُّ طِيبًا \ عَنْ عَبْدِ اللَّهِ بْنِ عُمَرَ رَضِيَ اللَّهُ عَنْهُمَا، أَنَّ رَجُلًا قَالَ: يَا رَسُولَ اللَّهِ، مَا يَلْبَسُ الْمُحْرِمُ مِنَ الشَّيَابِ؟ قَالَ رَسُولُ اللَّهِ صَلَّى اللَّهُ عَلَيْهِ وَسَلَّمَ: . . . وَلَا تَلْبَسُوا مِنَ الشَّيَابِ شَيْئًا مَسَّهُ الزَّعْفَرَانُ أَوْ وَرْسٌ» (بخاري بَابُ مَا لَا يَلْبَسُ الْمُحْرِمُ مِنَ القِيَابِ، نمبر: 1543/ مسلم : بَابُ مَا يُبَاحُ لِلْمُحْرِمِ بِحَجِّ أَوْ عُمْرَةٍ، وَمَا لَا يُبَاحُ، نمبر: 1177) وجه: (1) الأية لثبوت وَلَا يَحْلِقُ رَأْسَهُ وَلَا شَعْرَ بَدَنِهِ ﴿وَلَا تَحْلِقُوا رُءُوسَكُمْ حَتَّى يَبْلُغَ الْهَدَى يَحِلَّةٌ فَمَن كَانَ مِنكُم مَّرِيضًا أَوْ بِهِ أَذًى مِّن رَّأْسِهِ، فَفِدْيَةٌ مِّن صِيَامٍ أَوْ صَدَقَةٍ أَوْ نُسُكِ) (سورة البقرة، 2 : أيت (196) وجه:(۲) قول التابعى لثبوت وَلَا يَحْلِقُ رَأْسَهُ وَلَا شَعْرَ بَدَنِهِ \ عَنِ الْحَسَنِ، وَعَطَاءِ، قَالَ: «إِذَا انكَسَرَ ظُفْرُهُ مِنْ حَيْثُ الكَسَرَ، وَلَيْسَ عَلَيْهِ شَيْءٌ، فَإِنْ قَلَّمَهُ مِنْ قَبْلِ أَنْ يَنْكَسِرَ، فَعَلَيْهِ دَمٌ» (مصنف ابن أبي شيبة فِي الْمُحْرِمِ يَقُصُّ ظُفُرَهُ، نمبر : 12758) لغات : تَعْطِيَةُ : ڈھانکنا طيبا خوشبو شعر بال يَقْصُ : کاشا، لحيَتِهِ : داڑھی۔
And he should not cover his head nor his face. And he should not touch perfume. And he should not shave his head nor the hair of his body, and he should not cut from his beard. Proof (1): Hadith confirming 'he should not cover his head and face': from Ibn Umar, from the Prophet (peace be upon him): 'The muhrimah should not wear a face veil nor gloves.' (Abu Dawud: chapter of what the muhrim wears, 1826). Proof (2): Hadith confirming 'he should not cover his head and face': from Aisha, she said: 'Riders used to pass by us while we were with the Messenger of Allah (peace be upon him) as muhrimat. When they were parallel to us, one of us would let down her jilbab from her head over her face, and when they had passed, we would uncover it.' (Abu Dawud no. 1833). Proof (2: actually 1) Hadith confirming 'he should not touch perfume': Safwan ibn Ya'la narrated from his father: We were with the Messenger of Allah (peace be upon him), and a man came to him wearing a cloak with traces of khaluq (perfume). He said: 'O Messenger of Allah, I have entered ihram for Umrah, what should I do?' He said: 'Take off your cloak and wash the traces of khaluq from you.' (Muslim no. 1180, Bukhari no. 1536). Proof (2): Hadith confirming 'he should not touch perfume': from Abdullah ibn Umar: A man said: O Messenger of Allah, what may the muhrim wear? He said: '...and do not wear any garment that has been touched by saffron or yellow dye.' (Bukhari no. 1543, Muslim no. 1177). Proof (1): Verse confirming 'he should not shave his head nor body hair': {And do not shave your heads until the sacrificial animal reaches its place. But if any of you is ill or has an ailment in his scalp, then a compensation of fasting or charity or sacrifice.} (Surah al-Baqarah 2:196). Proof (2): Statement of a tabi'i confirming 'he should not shave his head nor body hair': from al-Hasan and Ata': 'If his nail breaks where it broke, there is no penalty on him; but if he cuts it before it breaks, he owes a dam (blood).' (Musannaf Ibn Abi Shayba no. 12758). Lexicon: taghtiya: covering; tib: perfume; sha'r: hair; yaqussu: cuts; lihyah: beard.
Source pages p. 240

Commentary
This passage continues the prohibitions for the muhrim. It covers three prohibitions: covering the head and face (for men covering the head, for women covering the face), using perfume, and shaving or cutting hair/nails. Each prohibition is supported by proofs. For covering: the hadith of Ibn Umar prohibits the muhrimah from wearing a niqab (face veil) and gloves, indicating that the face and hands should not be covered. The hadith of Aisha shows that women may cover their faces when non-mahram men pass, but only temporarily. For perfume: the hadith of Ya'la ibn Umayyah shows that the muhrim must remove perfume and wash it off. The prohibition includes any scented substance. For shaving/cutting: the Quranic verse (2:196) explicitly prohibits shaving the head before the sacrifice, and mentions fidya for necessity. The statement from al-Hasan and Ata' extends the prohibition to cutting nails: if a nail breaks, there is no penalty unless it is cut deliberately. The Urdu gloss explains the terms. The Hanafi school applies these prohibitions to both men and women, with specific exceptions: women may cover their faces when strangers approach, but not with a niqab permanently. The fidya for shaving is required only if done intentionally for need; otherwise, it is sinful.

Key Terms
فِدْيَة (fidya): Compensation for violating the prohibitions of ihram, consisting of fasting, charity, or sacrifice.
خَلُوق (khaluq): A kind of perfume made of saffron and other substances, typically yellow in color.
نِقَاب (niqab): A face veil that covers the face, leaving only the eyes visible.

Key Terms from Source Passage

Checkpoint
A muhrim accidentally shaves his head due to severe heat. What is required according to the Hanafi school?
A) Nothing, it was necessary.
B) He must sacrifice a sheep (dam).
C) He must repeat his ihram.
D) He must fast three days.

Key Takeaway
Three acts are haram in ihram: covering head/face, perfume, shaving – each with clear proof and fidya exception for necessity.

Sunan Acts from Entry to Tawaf
Sunan acts from entering Makkah to completing tawaf

Learning Objective
By the end of this lesson, you will be able to list the sunan muakkadah acts of a pilgrim from entering Makkah through completing tawaf and explain why each is sunnah.

Core Idea
Seven circuits outside the Hatim with idtiba' and istilam — these sunan complete the tawaf.

This passage from the matn of Al-Quduri presents the recommended practices (sunan) for a pilgrim upon reaching the Sacred Mosque. It covers the prohibition of washing with certain herbs, the emphasis on talbiyah, the order of actions at the Black Stone, the requirement to perform idtiba', and the precise route of tawaf outside the Hatim. Understanding these details ensures that the pilgrim performs the tawaf as closely to the Sunnah as possible.

Guided Path
1
Identify the acting subject
The passage addresses a pilgrim (hajj) who has entered Makkah and is about to perform tawaf. All rulings here are for that person.
2
Recognize the prohibition
Note that washing the head or beard with khitmi is forbidden for a muhrim. This is a minor prohibition (makruh tanzihi) because khitmi acts like a perfume.
3
Extract the times for talbiyah
List the occasions when talbiyah is emphasized: after prayers, on high ground, in valleys, when meeting riders, and at dawn. This shows the sunnah is to recite it frequently.
4
Follow the order at the Black Stone
Sequence: face the Stone, say takbir and tahlil, raise hands, then touch it (istilam) if possible without harming others. This is sunnah.
5
Outline the tawaf procedure
Before starting, perform idtiba' (bare right shoulder). Then begin tawaf from the Black Stone side, moving to the right, making exactly seven circuits all outside the Hatim. This completes the sunan of tawaf.
The Hatim is part of the Kaaba; tawaf inside it is invalid.

Source Text
⚠ Extracted via Advanced OCR ∼97% accuracy, minor errors may remain — always verify against original Arabic books
كِتَابُ الْحَجّ ١٨ وَلَا يَغْسِلُ رَأْسَهُ وَلَا حِيَتَهُ بِالْخِطْمِي وَيُكْثِرُ مِنْ التَّلْبِيَةِ عَقِيبَ الصَّلَوَاتِ وَكُلَّمَا عَلَا شَرَفًا أَوْ هَبَطَ وَادِيًا أَوْ لَقِيَ رَكْبَانًا وَبِالْأَسْحَارِ فَإِذَا دَخَلَ مَكَّةَ ابْتَدَأَ بِالْمَسْجِدِ الْحَرَامِ فَإِذَا عَايَنَ الْبَيْتَ هَلَّلَ وَكَبَّرَ ثُمَّ ابْتَدَأَ بِالْحَجَرِ الْأَسْوَدِ فَاسْتَقْبَلَهُ وَكَبَّرَ وَهَلَّلَ وَرَفَعَ يَدَيْهِ وَاسْتَلَمَهُ إِنْ اسْتَطَاعَ مِنْ غَيْرِ أَنْ يُؤْذِيَ مُسْلِمًا ثُمَّ يَأْخُذُ عَنْ يَمِينِهِ مِمَّا يَلِي الْبَابَ وَقَدْ اضْطَبَعَ قَبْلَ ذَلِكَ فَيَطُوفُ بِالْبَيْتِ سَبْعَةَ أَشْوَاطٍ وَيَجْعَلُ طَوَافَهُ مِنْ وَرَاءِ الْحَظِيمِ. أصول: طواف میں سات شوط مسنون ہیں یعنی سات چکر لگائے اور طواف میں اضطباع کرے.
The Book of Hajj, Section 18: He should not wash his head or his beard with khitmi. He should say the talbiyah abundantly after prayers, whenever he ascends a height, descends into a valley, meets a riding party, and at dawn. When he enters Makkah, he starts with the Sacred Mosque. When he sees the House, he says 'La ilaha illallah' and 'Allahu Akbar'. Then he starts with the Black Stone, faces it, says 'Allahu Akbar' and 'La ilaha illallah', raises his hands, and touches it if he can, without harming any Muslim. Then he takes to his right, near the door, having previously placed his garment under his right armpit (idtiba'), and performs seven circuits around the House, making his tawaf from behind the Hatim. Principles: In tawaf, seven circuits are sunnah, meaning seven rounds, and one performs idtiba' in the tawaf.
Source pages p. 242

Commentary
This passage from Al-Quduri outlines the sunan (recommended acts) for a pilgrim upon entering Makkah and performing the tawaf al-qudoom (arrival tawaf). The matn begins by prohibiting the use of khitmi (a plant used for washing) on the head and beard for the muhrim, as it is considered a perfume-like substance. It then emphasizes frequent recitation of the talbiyah, especially after prayers, at elevated spots, in valleys, when meeting other travelers, and at dawn. Upon reaching Makkah, the pilgrim should first go to the Sacred Mosque and upon sighting the Kaaba, begin with takbir and tahlil. The next act is to approach the Black Stone (Hajar al-Aswad), face it, raise the hands, and perform istilam (touching) if possible without harming others. Then, the pilgrim should move to the right towards the door, having already performed idtiba' (baring the right shoulder by placing the upper garment under the right armpit and over the left shoulder). The tawaf consists of exactly seven circuits, all performed outside the Hatim (the semicircular area on the north side of the Kaaba, which is considered part of the House). The Urdu note confirms these as sunnah and emphasizes the requirement of idtiba'.

Key Terms
اضطباع (idṭibāʿ): Placing the upper garment under the right armpit and over the left shoulder, leaving the right shoulder bare during tawaf.
حظيم (Ḥaṭīm): The semicircular area adjacent to the Kaaba, considered part of the original House built by Ibrahim. Tawaf must be performed outside it.
تلبيبة (talbiyah): Reciting 'Labbayk Allahumma labbayk, labbayka la sharika laka labbayk...' as a declaration of intent and obedience during Hajj.

Key Terms from Source Passage

Checkpoint
According to the Hanafi school, how many circuits must the pilgrim perform in tawaf?
A) Three
B) Seven
C) Four
D) Ten

Key Takeaway
The pilgrim should enter Makkah with dhikr, touch the Black Stone, perform idtiba', and complete seven circuits entirely outside the Hatim; these are sunnah muakkadah.

Hajj — Pilgrimage
intermediate

Sunan of Tawaf: Ramal, Istilam, and Two Rak'ahs
Detailed sunan of tawaf with hadith proofs.

Learning Objective
By the end of this lesson, you will be able to state the three sunan actions within tawaf (ramal, istilam, praying two rak'ahs) and cite the hadith proofs for each, identifying the Hanafi position on which corners of the Kaaba are touched.

Core Idea
Ramal shows strength, istilam honors the Black Stone and Yemeni corner, and the two rak'ahs are a constant sunna after every tawaf.

The first three circuits of tawaf have a distinctive brisk walk called ramal, revealed to refute the disbelievers' claim of weakness. Each circuit includes touching the Black Stone (and only the Yemeni corner), and upon completion, two rak'ahs are prayed near Maqam Ibrahim. Let us examine the proofs.

Guided Path
1
Identify the three sunan actions
Read the matn: ramal in first three circuits, istilam of the Stone, and praying two rak'ahs after tawaf. Note the order.
Ramal is for men only.
2
Trace the ramal proof
From the hadith of Ibn Abbas: the Prophet ordered ramal to show strength to the polytheists. This was a specific occasion but became a sunna.
3
Trace the istilam proof
From Ibn Umar: the Prophet never left touching the Yemeni corner and the Black Stone. Also, the hadith of Abdur Rahman shows touching the entire side from door to Hatim after conquest.
Hanafis limit istilam to these two corners.
4
Trace the two rak'ahs proof
From Ibn Umar: the Prophet prayed two rak'ahs behind the Maqam after tawaf. The verse also instructs taking the Maqam as a place of prayer.
The Hanafis interpret the verse as sunna, not obligation.
5
Conclude the Hanafi ruling
All three are sunna mu'akkada. The usul principle confirms ramal is sunna, and the other sunan are confirmed by the Prophet's continuous practice.

Source Text
⚠ Extracted via Advanced OCR ∼97% accuracy, minor errors may remain — always verify against original Arabic books
كِتَابُ الْحَجِّ ٢٥ وَيَرْمُلُ فِي الْأَشْوَاطِ الثَّلَاثِ الْأُوَلِ وَيَمْشِي فِيمَا بَقِيَ عَلَى هَيْئَتِهِ ٢٦ وَيَسْتَلِمُ الْحَجَرَ الْأَسْوَدَ كُلَّمَا مَرَّ بِهِ إِنِ اسْتَطَاعَ ٢٧ وَيَخْتَتِمُ بِالِاسْتِلَامِ ٢٨ ثُمَّ يَأْتِي الْمَقَامَ فَيُصَلِّي عِنْدَهُ رَكْعَتَيْنِ أَوْ حَيْثُ تَيَسَّرَ مِنَ الْمَسْجِدِ

٢٥ وَجْهٌ: (١) الْحَدِيثُ لِثُبُوتِ وَيَرْمُلُ فِي الْأَشْوَاطِ الثَّلَاثِ الْأُوَلِ عَنِ ابْنِ عَبَّاسٍ رَضِيَ اللَّهُ عَنْهُمَا قَالَ: قَدِمَ رَسُولُ اللَّهِ صَلَّى اللهُ عَلَيْهِ وَسَلَّمَ وَأَصْحَابُهُ، فَقَالَ الْمُشْرِكُونَ: إِنَّهُ يَقْدَمُ عَلَيْكُمْ وَقَدْ وَهَنَهُمْ حُمَّى يَثْرِبَ، فَأَمَرَهُمُ النَّبِيُّ صَلَّى اللهُ عَلَيْهِ وَسَلَّمَ أَنْ يَرْمُلُوا الْأَشْوَاطَ الثَّلَاثَةَ، وَأَنْ يَمْشُوا مَا بَيْنَ الرُّكْنَيْنِ، (بخاري بَابٌ: كَيْفَ كَانَ بَدْءُ الرَّمَلِ: ١٦٠٢/ أَبُو دَاوُدَ: بَابٌ فِي الرَّمَلِ: ١٨٨٦) وَجْهٌ: (١) الْحَدِيثُ لِثُبُوتِ وَرَفَعَ يَدَيْهِ وَاسْتَلَمَهُ إِنِ اسْتَطَاعَ عَنِ ابْنِ عَبَّاسٍ رَضِيَ اللَّهُ عَنْهُمَا، قَالَ: «طَافَ النَّبِيُّ صَلَّى اللهُ عَلَيْهِ وَسَلَّمَ بِالْبَيْتِ عَلَى بَعِيرٍ، كُلَّمَا أَتَى الرُّكْنَ أَشَارَ إِلَيْهِ بِشَيْءٍ كَانَ عِنْدَهُ وَكَبَّرَ» (بخاري بَابُ التَّكْبِيرِ عِنْدَ الرُّكْنِ، نمر: ١٦١٣) وَجْهٌ: (١) الْحَدِيثُ لِثُبُوتِ وَرَفَعَ يَدَيْهِ وَاسْتَلَمَهُ إِنِ اسْتَطَاعَ عَنِ ابْنِ عُمَرَ، قَالَ: كَانَ رَسُولُ اللَّهِ صَلَّى اللهُ عَلَيْهِ وَسَلَّمَ لَا يَدَعُ أَنْ يَسْتَلِمَ الرُّكْنَ الْيَمَانِي وَالْحَجَرَ فِي كُلِّ طَوْفَةٍ». قَالَ: وَكَانَ عَبْدُ اللَّهِ بْنُ عُمَرَ يَفْعَلُهُ (أبو داؤد: بَابُ اسْتِلَامِ الْأَرْكَانِ نمر ١٨٧٦/ بخاري، نمر: ١٦١١) ٢٧ وَجْهٌ: (١) الْحَدِيثُ لِثُبُوتِ وَيَخْتَتِمُ بِالِاسْتِلَامِ عَنْ عَبْدِ الرَّحْمَنِ بْنِ صَفْوَانَ، قَالَ: «لَمَّا فَتَحَ رَسُولُ اللهِ صلى الله عليه وسلم مَكَّةَ قُلْتُ: لَأَلْبَسَنَّ ثِيَابِي وَكَانَتْ دَارِي عَلَى الطَّرِيقِ، فَلَأَنْظُرَنَّ كَيْفَ يَصْنَعُ رَسُولُ اللهِ صلى الله عليه وسلم فَانْطَلَقْتُ فَرَأَيْتُ النَّبِيَّ صلى الله عليه وسلم قَدْ خَرَجَ مِنَ الْكَعْبَةِ هُوَ وَأَصْحَابُهُ قَدِ اسْتَلَمُوا الْبَيْتَ مِنَ الْبَابِ إِلَى الْحَطِيمِ وَقَدْ وَضَعُوا خُدُودَهُمْ عَلَى الْبَيْتِ، وَرَسُولُ اللهِ صلى الله عليه وسلم وَسْطَهُمْ» (سنن للبيهقي: بَابُ الْمُلْتَزَمِ، نمر: ٩٣٣١) ٢٨ وَجْهٌ: (١) الْحَدِيثُ لِثُبُوتِ ثُمَّ يَأْتِي الْمَقَامَ فَيُصَلِّي عِنْدَهُ رَكْعَتَيْنِ قَالَ: سَمِعْتُ ابْنَ عُمَرَ رَضِيَ اللَّهُ عَنْهُمَا يَقُولُ: «قَدِمَ النَّبِيُّ صَلَّى اللهُ عَلَيْهِ وَسَلَّمَ فَطَافَ بِالْبَيْتِ سَبْعًا، وَصَلَّى خَلْفَ الْمَقَامِ رَكْعَتَيْنِ، ثُمَّ خَرَجَ إِلَى الصَّفَا» (بخاري بَابُ مَنْ صَلَّى رَكْعَتَيِ الطَّوَافِ خَلْفَ الْمَقَامِ: ١٦٢٧)

أُصُولٌ: طَوَافِ كَے اَوَائِلِ تِينْ شَوْطٍ مَیں رَمَلْ كَرْنَا مَسْنُونٌ هَے، یَعْنِي اَکَٹْر كَرْ چَلْے، اور آخِری چَارْ شَوْطٍ مَیں اپنی حَالَتْ پَر سُکُون و قَار كَیساتھ كَرے۔

كِتَابُ الْحَجِّ وَلَ وَهَذَا الطَّوَافُ طَوَافُ الْقُدُومِ وَهُوَ سُنَّةٌ وَلَيْسَ بِوَاجِبٍ وَلَيْسَ عَلَى أَهْلِ مَكَّةَ طَوَافُ الْقُدُومِ ٣٠ ثُمَّ يَخْرُجُ إِلَى الصَّفَا فَيَصْعَدُ عَلَيْهَا وَيَسْتَقْبِلُ الْبَيْتَ وَيُكَبِّرُ وَيُهَلِّلُ وَيُصَلِّي عَلَى النَّبِيِّ صَلَّى اللَّهُ عَلَيْهِ وَسَلَّمَ وَيَدْعُو اللَّهَ بِحَاجَتِهِ

وَجْهٌ: (٢) الْآيَةُ لِثُبُوتِ ثُمَّ يَأْتِي الْمَقَامَ فَيُصَلِّي عِنْدَهُ رَكْعَتَيْنِ {وَاتَّخِذُوا مِنْ مَقَامِ إِبْرَاهِيمَ مُصَلًّى} (سورة البقرة، ٢ أية نمر: ١٢٥)

وَجْهٌ: (٣) قَوْلُ التَّابِعِيِّ لِثُبُوتِ ثُمَّ يَأْتِي الْمَقَامَ فَيُصَلِّي عِنْدَهُ رَكْعَتَيْنِ قُلْتُ لِلزُهْرِيِّ: إِنَّ عَطَاءً يَقُولُ: تُجْزِتُهُ الْمَكْتُوبَةُ مِنْ رَكْعَتَيِ الطَّوَافِ؟ فَقَالَ: السُّنَّةُ أَفْضَلُ «لَمْ يَطُفِ النَّبِيُّ صَلَّى اللَّهُ عَلَيْهِ وَسَلَّمَ سُبُوعًا قَطُّ إِلَّا صَلَّى رَكْعَتَيْنِ» (بخاري: بَابٌ: لِسُبُوعِهِ رَكْعَتَيْنِ، نمر: ١٦٢٣)

وَلَ وَجْهٌ: (١) الْحَدِيثُ لِثُبُوتِ وَهَذَا الطَّوَافُ طَوَافُ الْقُدُومِ وَهُوَ سُنَّةٌ عَنْ وَبَرَةَ، قَالَ: كُنْتُ جَالِسًا عِنْدَ ابْنِ عُمَرَ فَجَاءَهُ رَجُلٌ فَقَالَ: أَيَصْلُحُ لِي أَنْ أَطُوفَ بِالْبَيْتِ قَبْلَ أَنْ آتِيَ الْمَوْقِفَ، فَقَالَ: نَعَمْ، فَقَالَ: فَإِنَّ ابْنَ عَبَّاسٍ يَقُولُ: لَا تَطُفْ بِالْبَيْتِ حَتَّى تَأْتِيَ الْمَوْقِفَ، فَقَالَ ابْنُ عُمَرَ: «فَقَدْ حَجَّ رَسُولُ اللَّهِ صَلَّى اللَّهُ عَلَيْهِ وَسَلَّمَ فَطَافَ بِالْبَيْتِ قَبْلَ أَنْ يَأْتِيَ الْمَوْقِفَ» فَبِقَوْلِ رَسُولِ اللهِ صَلَّى اللهُ عَلَيْهِ وَسَلَّمَ أَحَقُّ أَنْ تَأْخُذَ أَوْ بِقَوْلِ ابْنِ عَبَّاسٍ إِنْ كُنْتَ صَادِقًا (مسلم: بَابُ مَا يَلْزَمُ مَنْ أَحْرَمَ بِالْحَجِّ ثُمَّ قَدِمَ مَكَّةَ مِنَ الطَّوَافِ وَالسَّعْيِ نمر: ١٢٣٣)

٣٠ وَجْهٌ: (١) الْحَدِيثُ لِثُبُوتِ ثُمَّ يَخْرُجُ إِلَى الصَّفَا فَيَصْعَدُ عَلَيْهَا قَالَ: دَخَلْنَا عَلَى جَابِرِ بْنِ عَبْدِ اللَّهِ... ثُمَّ خَرَجَ مِنَ الْبَابِ إِلَى الصَّفَا فَلَمَّا دَنَا مِنَ الصَّفَا قَرَأَ: {إِنَّ الصَّفَا وَالْمَرْوَةَ مِنْ شَعَائِرِ اللهِ} [البقرة: ١٥٨] «أَبْدَأُ بِمَا بَدَأَ اللهُ بِهِ» فَبَدَأَ بِالصَّفَا فَرَقِيَ عَلَيْهِ، حَتَّى رَأَى الْبَيْتَ فَاسْتَقْبَلَ الْقِبْلَةَ، فَوَحَّدَ اللَّهَ وَكَبَّرَهُ، وَقَالَ: «لَا إِلَهَ إِلَّا اللهُ وَحْدَهُ لَا شَرِيكَ لَهُ، لَهُ الْمُلْكُ وَلَهُ الْحَمْدُ وَهُوَ عَلَى كُلِّ شَيْءٍ قَدِيرٌ، لَا إِلَهَ إِلَّا اللهُ وَحْدَهُ، أَنْجَزَ وَعْدَهُ، وَنَصَرَ عَبْدَهُ، وَهَزَمَ الْأَحْزَابَ وَحْدَهُ» ثُمَّ دَعَا بَيْنَ ذَلِكَ، قَالَ: مِثْلَ هَذَا ثَلَاثَ مَرَّاتٍ، ثُمَّ نَزَلَ إِلَى الْمَرْوَةِ، (مسلم: بَابُ حَجَّةِ النَّبِيِّ صَلَّى اللَّهُ عَلَيْهِ وَسَلَّمَ،:١٢١٨/أبوداؤد: بَابُ صِفَةِ حَجَّةِ النَّبِيِّ صَلَّى اللَّهُ عَلَيْهِ وَسَلَّمَ: ١٩٠٥)

أُصُولٌ: بَيْتُ اللَّهِ كَے چَارْ رُكْنٍ هَیں: ۱ رُكْنُ الْحَجَرِ الْأَسْوَدِ ۲ رُكْنُ الْيَمَانِي ۳ رُكْنُ الشَّامِي ٤ رُكْنُ الْعِرَاقِي۔ أُصُولٌ: بَيْتُ اللَّهِ كَے حَجَرِ الْأَسْوَدِ اور رُكْنِ يَمَانِي كُو چُومْنَا يَا اسْتِلَامُ كَرْنَا مَسْنُونَ هَے، اور باقی دو كَا اسْتِلَامُ نَہ كرے۔
The Book of Hajj. 25. And he performs ramal in the first three circuits and walks in what remains in his normal manner. 26. And he touches the Black Stone whenever he passes by it if he is able. 27. And he concludes with touching (istilam). 28. Then he comes to the Maqam and prays two rak'ahs near it or wherever is easy in the mosque. 25. Proof: (1) The hadith for establishing 'and he performs ramal in the first three circuits' from Ibn Abbas (may Allah be pleased with them both) who said: The Messenger of Allah (peace be upon him) and his companions arrived, and the polytheists said: 'Indeed he is coming to you while the fever of Yathrib has weakened them.' So the Prophet (peace be upon him) ordered them to perform ramal in the three circuits and to walk between the two corners. (Bukhari: Chapter: How ramal began, no. 1602 / Abu Dawud: Chapter on ramal, no. 1886). Proof: (1) The hadith for establishing 'and he raises his hands and touches it if he is able' from Ibn Abbas (may Allah be pleased with them both) who said: 'The Prophet (peace be upon him) performed tawaf of the House on a camel, whenever he came to the corner he pointed to it with something he had and said Allahu Akbar.' (Bukhari: Chapter of Takbir at the corner, no. 1613). Proof: (1) The hadith for establishing 'and he raises his hands and touches it if he is able' from Ibn Umar who said: 'The Messenger of Allah (peace be upon him) would not leave touching the Yemeni corner and the Stone in every circuit.' He said: 'And Abdullah ibn Umar used to do it.' (Abu Dawud: Chapter of touching the corners, no. 1876 / Bukhari, no. 1611). 27. Proof: (1) The hadith for establishing 'and he concludes with touching' from Abdur Rahman ibn Safwan who said: 'When the Messenger of Allah (peace be upon him) conquered Makkah, I said: I will put on my clothes—and my house was on the road—and I will watch how the Messenger of Allah (peace be upon him) acts. So I went and I saw the Prophet (peace be upon him) came out of the Kaaba, he and his companions, they had touched the House from the door to the Hatim and placed their cheeks on the House, and the Messenger of Allah (peace be upon him) was in their midst.' (Sunan al-Bayhaqi: Chapter of the Multazam, no. 9331). 28. Proof: (1) The hadith for establishing 'then he comes to the Maqam and prays two rak'ahs near it' — he said: I heard Ibn Umar (may Allah be pleased with them both) saying: 'The Prophet (peace be upon him) arrived and performed tawaf of the House seven times, and prayed two rak'ahs behind the Maqam, then went out to Safa.' (Bukhari: Chapter of whoever prays the two rak'ahs of tawaf behind the Maqam, no. 1627). Principle: Performing ramal in the first three circuits of tawaf is sunna, i.e., to walk briskly, and in the remaining four circuits to walk with tranquility and dignity. The Book of Hajj: And this tawaf is Tawaf al-Qudum, and it is sunna and not obligatory, and the people of Makkah are not required to perform Tawaf al-Qudum. 30. Then he goes out to Safa and ascends upon it, faces the House, says Allahu Akbar, says La ilaha illa Allah, sends salawat upon the Prophet (peace be upon him), and supplicates Allah for his need. Proof: (2) The verse for establishing 'then he comes to the Maqam and prays two rak'ahs near it': {And take from the Maqam of Ibrahim a place of prayer} (Surah al-Baqarah, 2, verse 125). Proof: (3) The saying of the Tabi'i for establishing 'then he comes to the Maqam and prays two rak'ahs near it' — I said to al-Zuhri: 'Indeed Ata says: The obligatory prayer suffices him from the two rak'ahs of tawaf?' He said: 'The sunna is better. The Prophet (peace be upon him) never performed any tawaf without praying two rak'ahs.' (Bukhari: Chapter: For his tawaf, two rak'ahs, no. 1623). And he said — Proof: (1) The hadith for establishing 'and this tawaf is Tawaf al-Qudum and it is sunna' from Wabarah who said: I was sitting with Ibn Umar when a man came to him and said: 'Is it permissible for me to perform tawaf of the House before I go to the standing place (Arafat)?' He said: 'Yes.' He said: 'Indeed Ibn Abbas says: Do not perform tawaf of the House until you go to the standing place.' Ibn Umar said: 'The Messenger of Allah (peace be upon him) performed Hajj and performed tawaf of the House before he went to the standing place. So is the saying of the Messenger of Allah (peace be upon him) more deserving to take or the saying of Ibn Abbas, if you are truthful?' (Muslim: Chapter of what is incumbent on one who enters ihram for Hajj then arrives in Makkah regarding tawaf and sa'i, no. 1233). 30. Proof: (1) The hadith for establishing 'then he goes out to Safa and ascends upon it' — he said: We entered upon Jabir ibn Abdillah... then he (the Prophet) came out of the door to Safa, and when he approached Safa he recited: {Indeed Safa and Marwa are from the symbols of Allah} [Al-Baqarah: 158] 'I begin with what Allah began with.' So he began with Safa and ascended upon it until he saw the House, then faced the Qibla, and declared the oneness of Allah and magnified Him, and said: 'There is no god but Allah alone, with no partner, His is the dominion and His is the praise, and He is over all things competent. There is no god but Allah alone, He fulfilled His promise, and helped His servant, and defeated the confederates alone.' Then he supplicated in between that. He said: The like of this three times, then he descended to Marwa. (Muslim: Chapter of the Prophet's Hajj, no. 1218 / Abu Dawud: Chapter of the description of the Prophet's Hajj, no. 1905). Principles: The House of Allah has four corners: 1. The Black Stone corner, 2. The Yemeni corner, 3. The Syrian corner, 4. The Iraqi corner. Principles: It is sunna to kiss or touch the Black Stone and the Yemeni corner of the House of Allah, and not to touch the remaining two.
Source pages p. 244

Commentary
This passage is a commentary on the rulings of Tawaf al-Qudum and Sa'i, presented as an expansion of the base matn (likely Al-Quduri) with hadith proofs and usul principles. The matn begins by detailing the sunan actions within the circumambulation (tawaf) performed upon arrival in Makkah (Tawaf al-Qudum). The first instruction is to perform ramal — walking with short, brisk steps with shoulder movement — in the first three circuits, and to walk normally in the remaining four. This is proven by the hadith from Ibn Abbas that the Prophet ordered ramal to show strength to the disbelievers. The matn then instructs touching the Black Stone (istilam) each time one passes by it, if possible, and to conclude the tawaf with istilam. The hadith from Ibn Umar confirms the Prophet's practice of touching the Yemeni corner and the Black Stone every circuit, and the hadith from Abdur Rahman ibn Safwan describes the Companions touching the House from the door to the Hatim after the conquest. After completing the seven circuits, the pilgrim prays two rak'ahs near Maqam Ibrahim (or anywhere in the mosque), proven by the hadith of Ibn Umar and the verse from Surah al-Baqarah. The saying of al-Zuhri emphasizes that the sunna is to pray these two rak'ahs specifically, not to substitute them with an obligatory prayer. The commentary then clarifies the legal nature of this tawaf: it is called Tawaf al-Qudum, it is sunna (not obligatory), and the residents of Makkah are not required to perform it. This is supported by the hadith where Ibn Umar refutes Ibn Abbas's view that tawaf before Arafat is impermissible, citing the Prophet's own practice. Finally, the passage describes the sa'i: after tawaf, the pilgrim goes to Safa, ascends it, faces the Kaaba, glorifies Allah, sends salawat, and makes supplication. The long hadith of Jabir details the Prophet's actions at Safa, including the specific dhikr repeated three times, then descending to Marwa. The concluding usul principle states that the Kaaba has four corners: Black Stone, Yemeni, Syrian, and Iraqi. It is sunna to kiss or touch only the Black Stone and the Yemeni corner, not the other two. This is a key point of Hanafi fiqh, as other schools may have different practices. The passage thus provides a comprehensive sunna-based guide for the opening rituals of the pilgrim arriving in Makkah.

Key Terms
الرَّمَلُ (ar-ramal): Walking briskly with short steps and shoulder movement in the first three circuits of tawaf, a sunna act.
الِاسْتِلَامُ (al-istilam): Touching the Black Stone or Yemeni corner with the hand or kissing it if possible during tawaf.
مَقَامُ إِبْرَاهِيمَ (maqāmu ibrāhīm): The station of Ibrahim, a stone near the Kaaba where Ibrahim stood during construction; near it the two rak'ahs of tawaf are prayed.

Key Terms from Source Passage

Checkpoint
According to the Hanafi school, which of the following is a sunna act within tawaf?
A) Walking slowly in all circuits
B) Touching the Syrian corner
C) Praying two rak'ahs after tawaf
D) Running between Safa and Marwa

Key Takeaway
Ramal, istilam of two corners, and the two rak'ahs are established sunnas of tawaf with strong hadith evidence.

Hajj — Pilgrimage
beginner
8 min
The Ruling of Tawaf al-Qudum
Ruling on the legal status of Tawaf al-Qudum.

Learning Objective
By the end of this lesson, you will be able to state the Hanafi ruling that Tawaf al-Qudum is sunna (not wajib) and apply the exemption for residents of Makkah, citing the hadith evidence.

Core Idea
Tawaf al-Qudum is a confirmed sunna, not an obligation, and residents of Makkah are exempt from it.

Upon arriving in Makkah, a non-resident pilgrim is encouraged to perform a tawaf called Tawaf al-Qudum. The Hanafi school explicitly states it is sunna, not wajib, and that residents of Makkah do not perform it. Let's examine the proof from the hadith of Wabarah and the response to a contrary view.

Guided Path
1
Read the ruling statement
The matn says: 'This tawaf is Tawaf al-Qudum, and it is sunna, not obligatory, and it is not upon the people of Makkah.'
Note the clear distinction between sunna and wajib.
2
Examine the hadith proof
The hadith of Wabarah: a man asked Ibn Umar whether tawaf before Arafat is permissible. Ibn Umar affirmed, citing the Prophet's action, and refuted Ibn Abbas's opinion.
This proves the permissibility and sunna status, not obligation.
3
Understand the exemption for Makkans
Residents of Makkah do not perform Tawaf al-Qudum because they have not arrived from afar; it is a greeting for the Haram.
This is a unique ruling; other schools might not have this exemption.
4
Contrast with the contrary view
Ibn Abbas held that tawaf should be postponed until after Arafat. Ibn Umar rebutted with the Prophet's practice. The Hanafi school follows Ibn Umar.
This shows the hierarchical priority of Prophet's action over a Sahabi's opinion.

Source Text
⚠ Extracted via Advanced OCR ∼97% accuracy, minor errors may remain — always verify against original Arabic books
كِتَابُ الْحَجِّ ٢٥ وَيَرْمُلُ فِي الْأَشْوَاطِ الثَّلَاثِ الْأُوَلِ وَيَمْشِي فِيمَا بَقِيَ عَلَى هَيْئَتِهِ ٢٦ وَيَسْتَلِمُ الْحَجَرَ الْأَسْوَدَ كُلَّمَا مَرَّ بِهِ إِنِ اسْتَطَاعَ ٢٧ وَيَخْتَتِمُ بِالِاسْتِلَامِ ٢٨ ثُمَّ يَأْتِي الْمَقَامَ فَيُصَلِّي عِنْدَهُ رَكْعَتَيْنِ أَوْ حَيْثُ تَيَسَّرَ مِنَ الْمَسْجِدِ

٢٥ وَجْهٌ: (١) الْحَدِيثُ لِثُبُوتِ وَيَرْمُلُ فِي الْأَشْوَاطِ الثَّلَاثِ الْأُوَلِ عَنِ ابْنِ عَبَّاسٍ رَضِيَ اللَّهُ عَنْهُمَا قَالَ: قَدِمَ رَسُولُ اللَّهِ صَلَّى اللهُ عَلَيْهِ وَسَلَّمَ وَأَصْحَابُهُ، فَقَالَ الْمُشْرِكُونَ: إِنَّهُ يَقْدَمُ عَلَيْكُمْ وَقَدْ وَهَنَهُمْ حُمَّى يَثْرِبَ، فَأَمَرَهُمُ النَّبِيُّ صَلَّى اللهُ عَلَيْهِ وَسَلَّمَ أَنْ يَرْمُلُوا الْأَشْوَاطَ الثَّلَاثَةَ، وَأَنْ يَمْشُوا مَا بَيْنَ الرُّكْنَيْنِ، (بخاري بَابٌ: كَيْفَ كَانَ بَدْءُ الرَّمَلِ: ١٦٠٢/ أَبُو دَاوُدَ: بَابٌ فِي الرَّمَلِ: ١٨٨٦) وَجْهٌ: (١) الْحَدِيثُ لِثُبُوتِ وَرَفَعَ يَدَيْهِ وَاسْتَلَمَهُ إِنِ اسْتَطَاعَ عَنِ ابْنِ عَبَّاسٍ رَضِيَ اللَّهُ عَنْهُمَا، قَالَ: «طَافَ النَّبِيُّ صَلَّى اللهُ عَلَيْهِ وَسَلَّمَ بِالْبَيْتِ عَلَى بَعِيرٍ، كُلَّمَا أَتَى الرُّكْنَ أَشَارَ إِلَيْهِ بِشَيْءٍ كَانَ عِنْدَهُ وَكَبَّرَ» (بخاري بَابُ التَّكْبِيرِ عِنْدَ الرُّكْنِ، نمر: ١٦١٣) وَجْهٌ: (١) الْحَدِيثُ لِثُبُوتِ وَرَفَعَ يَدَيْهِ وَاسْتَلَمَهُ إِنِ اسْتَطَاعَ عَنِ ابْنِ عُمَرَ، قَالَ: كَانَ رَسُولُ اللَّهِ صَلَّى اللهُ عَلَيْهِ وَسَلَّمَ لَا يَدَعُ أَنْ يَسْتَلِمَ الرُّكْنَ الْيَمَانِي وَالْحَجَرَ فِي كُلِّ طَوْفَةٍ». قَالَ: وَكَانَ عَبْدُ اللَّهِ بْنُ عُمَرَ يَفْعَلُهُ (أبو داؤد: بَابُ اسْتِلَامِ الْأَرْكَانِ نمر ١٨٧٦/ بخاري، نمر: ١٦١١) ٢٧ وَجْهٌ: (١) الْحَدِيثُ لِثُبُوتِ وَيَخْتَتِمُ بِالِاسْتِلَامِ عَنْ عَبْدِ الرَّحْمَنِ بْنِ صَفْوَانَ، قَالَ: «لَمَّا فَتَحَ رَسُولُ اللهِ صلى الله عليه وسلم مَكَّةَ قُلْتُ: لَأَلْبَسَنَّ ثِيَابِي وَكَانَتْ دَارِي عَلَى الطَّرِيقِ، فَلَأَنْظُرَنَّ كَيْفَ يَصْنَعُ رَسُولُ اللهِ صلى الله عليه وسلم فَانْطَلَقْتُ فَرَأَيْتُ النَّبِيَّ صلى الله عليه وسلم قَدْ خَرَجَ مِنَ الْكَعْبَةِ هُوَ وَأَصْحَابُهُ قَدِ اسْتَلَمُوا الْبَيْتَ مِنَ الْبَابِ إِلَى الْحَطِيمِ وَقَدْ وَضَعُوا خُدُودَهُمْ عَلَى الْبَيْتِ، وَرَسُولُ اللهِ صلى الله عليه وسلم وَسْطَهُمْ» (سنن للبيهقي: بَابُ الْمُلْتَزَمِ، نمر: ٩٣٣١) ٢٨ وَجْهٌ: (١) الْحَدِيثُ لِثُبُوتِ ثُمَّ يَأْتِي الْمَقَامَ فَيُصَلِّي عِنْدَهُ رَكْعَتَيْنِ قَالَ: سَمِعْتُ ابْنَ عُمَرَ رَضِيَ اللَّهُ عَنْهُمَا يَقُولُ: «قَدِمَ النَّبِيُّ صَلَّى اللهُ عَلَيْهِ وَسَلَّمَ فَطَافَ بِالْبَيْتِ سَبْعًا، وَصَلَّى خَلْفَ الْمَقَامِ رَكْعَتَيْنِ، ثُمَّ خَرَجَ إِلَى الصَّفَا» (بخاري بَابُ مَنْ صَلَّى رَكْعَتَيِ الطَّوَافِ خَلْفَ الْمَقَامِ: ١٦٢٧)

أُصُولٌ: طَوَافِ كَے اَوَائِلِ تِينْ شَوْطٍ مَیں رَمَلْ كَرْنَا مَسْنُونٌ هَے، یَعْنِي اَکَٹْر كَرْ چَلْے، اور آخِری چَارْ شَوْطٍ مَیں اپنی حَالَتْ پَر سُکُون و قَار كَیساتھ كَرے۔

كِتَابُ الْحَجِّ وَلَ وَهَذَا الطَّوَافُ طَوَافُ الْقُدُومِ وَهُوَ سُنَّةٌ وَلَيْسَ بِوَاجِبٍ وَلَيْسَ عَلَى أَهْلِ مَكَّةَ طَوَافُ الْقُدُومِ ٣٠ ثُمَّ يَخْرُجُ إِلَى الصَّفَا فَيَصْعَدُ عَلَيْهَا وَيَسْتَقْبِلُ الْبَيْتَ وَيُكَبِّرُ وَيُهَلِّلُ وَيُصَلِّي عَلَى النَّبِيِّ صَلَّى اللَّهُ عَلَيْهِ وَسَلَّمَ وَيَدْعُو اللَّهَ بِحَاجَتِهِ

وَجْهٌ: (٢) الْآيَةُ لِثُبُوتِ ثُمَّ يَأْتِي الْمَقَامَ فَيُصَلِّي عِنْدَهُ رَكْعَتَيْنِ {وَاتَّخِذُوا مِنْ مَقَامِ إِبْرَاهِيمَ مُصَلًّى} (سورة البقرة، ٢ أية نمر: ١٢٥)

وَجْهٌ: (٣) قَوْلُ التَّابِعِيِّ لِثُبُوتِ ثُمَّ يَأْتِي الْمَقَامَ فَيُصَلِّي عِنْدَهُ رَكْعَتَيْنِ قُلْتُ لِلزُهْرِيِّ: إِنَّ عَطَاءً يَقُولُ: تُجْزِتُهُ الْمَكْتُوبَةُ مِنْ رَكْعَتَيِ الطَّوَافِ؟ فَقَالَ: السُّنَّةُ أَفْضَلُ «لَمْ يَطُفِ النَّبِيُّ صَلَّى اللَّهُ عَلَيْهِ وَسَلَّمَ سُبُوعًا قَطُّ إِلَّا صَلَّى رَكْعَتَيْنِ» (بخاري: بَابٌ: لِسُبُوعِهِ رَكْعَتَيْنِ، نمر: ١٦٢٣)

وَلَ وَجْهٌ: (١) الْحَدِيثُ لِثُبُوتِ وَهَذَا الطَّوَافُ طَوَافُ الْقُدُومِ وَهُوَ سُنَّةٌ عَنْ وَبَرَةَ، قَالَ: كُنْتُ جَالِسًا عِنْدَ ابْنِ عُمَرَ فَجَاءَهُ رَجُلٌ فَقَالَ: أَيَصْلُحُ لِي أَنْ أَطُوفَ بِالْبَيْتِ قَبْلَ أَنْ آتِيَ الْمَوْقِفَ، فَقَالَ: نَعَمْ، فَقَالَ: فَإِنَّ ابْنَ عَبَّاسٍ يَقُولُ: لَا تَطُفْ بِالْبَيْتِ حَتَّى تَأْتِيَ الْمَوْقِفَ، فَقَالَ ابْنُ عُمَرَ: «فَقَدْ حَجَّ رَسُولُ اللَّهِ صَلَّى اللَّهُ عَلَيْهِ وَسَلَّمَ فَطَافَ بِالْبَيْتِ قَبْلَ أَنْ يَأْتِيَ الْمَوْقِفَ» فَبِقَوْلِ رَسُولِ اللهِ صَلَّى اللهُ عَلَيْهِ وَسَلَّمَ أَحَقُّ أَنْ تَأْخُذَ أَوْ بِقَوْلِ ابْنِ عَبَّاسٍ إِنْ كُنْتَ صَادِقًا (مسلم: بَابُ مَا يَلْزَمُ مَنْ أَحْرَمَ بِالْحَجِّ ثُمَّ قَدِمَ مَكَّةَ مِنَ الطَّوَافِ وَالسَّعْيِ نمر: ١٢٣٣)

٣٠ وَجْهٌ: (١) الْحَدِيثُ لِثُبُوتِ ثُمَّ يَخْرُجُ إِلَى الصَّفَا فَيَصْعَدُ عَلَيْهَا قَالَ: دَخَلْنَا عَلَى جَابِرِ بْنِ عَبْدِ اللَّهِ... ثُمَّ خَرَجَ مِنَ الْبَابِ إِلَى الصَّفَا فَلَمَّا دَنَا مِنَ الصَّفَا قَرَأَ: {إِنَّ الصَّفَا وَالْمَرْوَةَ مِنْ شَعَائِرِ اللهِ} [البقرة: ١٥٨] «أَبْدَأُ بِمَا بَدَأَ اللهُ بِهِ» فَبَدَأَ بِالصَّفَا فَرَقِيَ عَلَيْهِ، حَتَّى رَأَى الْبَيْتَ فَاسْتَقْبَلَ الْقِبْلَةَ، فَوَحَّدَ اللَّهَ وَكَبَّرَهُ، وَقَالَ: «لَا إِلَهَ إِلَّا اللهُ وَحْدَهُ لَا شَرِيكَ لَهُ، لَهُ الْمُلْكُ وَلَهُ الْحَمْدُ وَهُوَ عَلَى كُلِّ شَيْءٍ قَدِيرٌ، لَا إِلَهَ إِلَّا اللهُ وَحْدَهُ، أَنْجَزَ وَعْدَهُ، وَنَصَرَ عَبْدَهُ، وَهَزَمَ الْأَحْزَابَ وَحْدَهُ» ثُمَّ دَعَا بَيْنَ ذَلِكَ، قَالَ: مِثْلَ هَذَا ثَلَاثَ مَرَّاتٍ، ثُمَّ نَزَلَ إِلَى الْمَرْوَةِ، (مسلم: بَابُ حَجَّةِ النَّبِيِّ صَلَّى اللَّهُ عَلَيْهِ وَسَلَّمَ،:١٢١٨/أبوداؤد: بَابُ صِفَةِ حَجَّةِ النَّبِيِّ صَلَّى اللَّهُ عَلَيْهِ وَسَلَّمَ: ١٩٠٥)

أُصُولٌ: بَيْتُ اللَّهِ كَے چَارْ رُكْنٍ هَیں: ۱ رُكْنُ الْحَجَرِ الْأَسْوَدِ ۲ رُكْنُ الْيَمَانِي ۳ رُكْنُ الشَّامِي ٤ رُكْنُ الْعِرَاقِي۔ أُصُولٌ: بَيْتُ اللَّهِ كَے حَجَرِ الْأَسْوَدِ اور رُكْنِ يَمَانِي كُو چُومْنَا يَا اسْتِلَامُ كَرْنَا مَسْنُونَ هَے، اور باقی دو كَا اسْتِلَامُ نَہ كرے۔
The Book of Hajj. 25. And he performs ramal in the first three circuits and walks in what remains in his normal manner. 26. And he touches the Black Stone whenever he passes by it if he is able. 27. And he concludes with touching (istilam). 28. Then he comes to the Maqam and prays two rak'ahs near it or wherever is easy in the mosque. 25. Proof: (1) The hadith for establishing 'and he performs ramal in the first three circuits' from Ibn Abbas (may Allah be pleased with them both) who said: The Messenger of Allah (peace be upon him) and his companions arrived, and the polytheists said: 'Indeed he is coming to you while the fever of Yathrib has weakened them.' So the Prophet (peace be upon him) ordered them to perform ramal in the three circuits and to walk between the two corners. (Bukhari: Chapter: How ramal began, no. 1602 / Abu Dawud: Chapter on ramal, no. 1886). Proof: (1) The hadith for establishing 'and he raises his hands and touches it if he is able' from Ibn Abbas (may Allah be pleased with them both) who said: 'The Prophet (peace be upon him) performed tawaf of the House on a camel, whenever he came to the corner he pointed to it with something he had and said Allahu Akbar.' (Bukhari: Chapter of Takbir at the corner, no. 1613). Proof: (1) The hadith for establishing 'and he raises his hands and touches it if he is able' from Ibn Umar who said: 'The Messenger of Allah (peace be upon him) would not leave touching the Yemeni corner and the Stone in every circuit.' He said: 'And Abdullah ibn Umar used to do it.' (Abu Dawud: Chapter of touching the corners, no. 1876 / Bukhari, no. 1611). 27. Proof: (1) The hadith for establishing 'and he concludes with touching' from Abdur Rahman ibn Safwan who said: 'When the Messenger of Allah (peace be upon him) conquered Makkah, I said: I will put on my clothes—and my house was on the road—and I will watch how the Messenger of Allah (peace be upon him) acts. So I went and I saw the Prophet (peace be upon him) came out of the Kaaba, he and his companions, they had touched the House from the door to the Hatim and placed their cheeks on the House, and the Messenger of Allah (peace be upon him) was in their midst.' (Sunan al-Bayhaqi: Chapter of the Multazam, no. 9331). 28. Proof: (1) The hadith for establishing 'then he comes to the Maqam and prays two rak'ahs near it' — he said: I heard Ibn Umar (may Allah be pleased with them both) saying: 'The Prophet (peace be upon him) arrived and performed tawaf of the House seven times, and prayed two rak'ahs behind the Maqam, then went out to Safa.' (Bukhari: Chapter of whoever prays the two rak'ahs of tawaf behind the Maqam, no. 1627). Principle: Performing ramal in the first three circuits of tawaf is sunna, i.e., to walk briskly, and in the remaining four circuits to walk with tranquility and dignity. The Book of Hajj: And this tawaf is Tawaf al-Qudum, and it is sunna and not obligatory, and the people of Makkah are not required to perform Tawaf al-Qudum. 30. Then he goes out to Safa and ascends upon it, faces the House, says Allahu Akbar, says La ilaha illa Allah, sends salawat upon the Prophet (peace be upon him), and supplicates Allah for his need. Proof: (2) The verse for establishing 'then he comes to the Maqam and prays two rak'ahs near it': {And take from the Maqam of Ibrahim a place of prayer} (Surah al-Baqarah, 2, verse 125). Proof: (3) The saying of the Tabi'i for establishing 'then he comes to the Maqam and prays two rak'ahs near it' — I said to al-Zuhri: 'Indeed Ata says: The obligatory prayer suffices him from the two rak'ahs of tawaf?' He said: 'The sunna is better. The Prophet (peace be upon him) never performed any tawaf without praying two rak'ahs.' (Bukhari: Chapter: For his tawaf, two rak'ahs, no. 1623). And he said — Proof: (1) The hadith for establishing 'and this tawaf is Tawaf al-Qudum and it is sunna' from Wabarah who said: I was sitting with Ibn Umar when a man came to him and said: 'Is it permissible for me to perform tawaf of the House before I go to the standing place (Arafat)?' He said: 'Yes.' He said: 'Indeed Ibn Abbas says: Do not perform tawaf of the House until you go to the standing place.' Ibn Umar said: 'The Messenger of Allah (peace be upon him) performed Hajj and performed tawaf of the House before he went to the standing place. So is the saying of the Messenger of Allah (peace be upon him) more deserving to take or the saying of Ibn Abbas, if you are truthful?' (Muslim: Chapter of what is incumbent on one who enters ihram for Hajj then arrives in Makkah regarding tawaf and sa'i, no. 1233). 30. Proof: (1) The hadith for establishing 'then he goes out to Safa and ascends upon it' — he said: We entered upon Jabir ibn Abdillah... then he (the Prophet) came out of the door to Safa, and when he approached Safa he recited: {Indeed Safa and Marwa are from the symbols of Allah} [Al-Baqarah: 158] 'I begin with what Allah began with.' So he began with Safa and ascended upon it until he saw the House, then faced the Qibla, and declared the oneness of Allah and magnified Him, and said: 'There is no god but Allah alone, with no partner, His is the dominion and His is the praise, and He is over all things competent. There is no god but Allah alone, He fulfilled His promise, and helped His servant, and defeated the confederates alone.' Then he supplicated in between that. He said: The like of this three times, then he descended to Marwa. (Muslim: Chapter of the Prophet's Hajj, no. 1218 / Abu Dawud: Chapter of the description of the Prophet's Hajj, no. 1905). Principles: The House of Allah has four corners: 1. The Black Stone corner, 2. The Yemeni corner, 3. The Syrian corner, 4. The Iraqi corner. Principles: It is sunna to kiss or touch the Black Stone and the Yemeni corner of the House of Allah, and not to touch the remaining two.
Source pages p. 244

Commentary
This passage is a commentary on the rulings of Tawaf al-Qudum and Sa'i, presented as an expansion of the base matn (likely Al-Quduri) with hadith proofs and usul principles. The matn begins by detailing the sunan actions within the circumambulation (tawaf) performed upon arrival in Makkah (Tawaf al-Qudum). The first instruction is to perform ramal — walking with short, brisk steps with shoulder movement — in the first three circuits, and to walk normally in the remaining four. This is proven by the hadith from Ibn Abbas that the Prophet ordered ramal to show strength to the disbelievers. The matn then instructs touching the Black Stone (istilam) each time one passes by it, if possible, and to conclude the tawaf with istilam. The hadith from Ibn Umar confirms the Prophet's practice of touching the Yemeni corner and the Black Stone every circuit, and the hadith from Abdur Rahman ibn Safwan describes the Companions touching the House from the door to the Hatim after the conquest. After completing the seven circuits, the pilgrim prays two rak'ahs near Maqam Ibrahim (or anywhere in the mosque), proven by the hadith of Ibn Umar and the verse from Surah al-Baqarah. The saying of al-Zuhri emphasizes that the sunna is to pray these two rak'ahs specifically, not to substitute them with an obligatory prayer. The commentary then clarifies the legal nature of this tawaf: it is called Tawaf al-Qudum, it is sunna (not obligatory), and the residents of Makkah are not required to perform it. This is supported by the hadith where Ibn Umar refutes Ibn Abbas's view that tawaf before Arafat is impermissible, citing the Prophet's own practice. Finally, the passage describes the sa'i: after tawaf, the pilgrim goes to Safa, ascends it, faces the Kaaba, glorifies Allah, sends salawat, and makes supplication. The long hadith of Jabir details the Prophet's actions at Safa, including the specific dhikr repeated three times, then descending to Marwa. The concluding usul principle states that the Kaaba has four corners: Black Stone, Yemeni, Syrian, and Iraqi. It is sunna to kiss or touch only the Black Stone and the Yemeni corner, not the other two. This is a key point of Hanafi fiqh, as other schools may have different practices. The passage thus provides a comprehensive sunna-based guide for the opening rituals of the pilgrim arriving in Makkah.

Key Terms
طَوَافُ الْقُدُومِ (tawāfu al-qudūm): The circumambulation performed upon arrival in Makkah by a non-resident pilgrim, which is sunna.

Key Terms from Source Passage

Checkpoint
According to the Hanafi school, who is required to perform Tawaf al-Qudum?
A) All pilgrims
B) Only residents of Makkah
C) Non-residents of Makkah
D) Only those performing Hajj Ifrad

Key Takeaway
Tawaf al-Qudum is a sunna for non-Makkans, and the hadith of Wabarah confirms its permissibility before Arafat.

Hajj — Pilgrimage
beginner
8 min
The Sa'i between Safa and Marwa: Procedure and Ruling
Procedure and ruling of sa'i with hadith details.

Learning Objective
By the end of this lesson, you will be able to describe the Hanafi procedure for sa'i, including the specific dhikr at Safa, and state that sa'i is a rukn of Hajj and Umrah.

Core Idea
Sa'i is a rukn; its procedure begins at Safa with tahlil, takbir, and supplication, repeating three times.

After completing tawaf and the two rak'ahs, the pilgrim proceeds to Safa to begin the sa'i. The matn describes the actions upon ascending Safa: facing the Kaaba, glorifying Allah, sending salawat, and supplicating. The hadith of Jabir provides the detailed practice of the Prophet.

Guided Path
1
Identify the act of sa'i
The matn says: 'Then he goes out to Safa and ascends upon it.' Sa'i is the walking between Safa and Marwa seven times.
Sa'i is a rukn according to Hanafi school.
2
List the sunan actions at Safa
Upon Safa: face the Kaaba, say Allahu Akbar, say La ilaha illa Allah, send salawat on the Prophet, and supplicate.
These are sunan, not fard.
3
Examine the hadith proof
The hadith of Jabir describes the Prophet's detailed practice: reciting the verse, beginning with Safa, ascending, facing Qibla, saying specific dhikr three times, then descending to Marwa.
This hadith is from Muslim and Abu Dawud.
4
Understand the ruling status
Though the matn does not explicitly state the ruling, the Hanafi school considers sa'i a rukn. The description here is about the sunan within it.
Omission of sa'i invalidates Hajj/Umrah.

Source Text
⚠ Extracted via Advanced OCR ∼97% accuracy, minor errors may remain — always verify against original Arabic books
كِتَابُ الْحَجِّ ٢٥ وَيَرْمُلُ فِي الْأَشْوَاطِ الثَّلَاثِ الْأُوَلِ وَيَمْشِي فِيمَا بَقِيَ عَلَى هَيْئَتِهِ ٢٦ وَيَسْتَلِمُ الْحَجَرَ الْأَسْوَدَ كُلَّمَا مَرَّ بِهِ إِنِ اسْتَطَاعَ ٢٧ وَيَخْتَتِمُ بِالِاسْتِلَامِ ٢٨ ثُمَّ يَأْتِي الْمَقَامَ فَيُصَلِّي عِنْدَهُ رَكْعَتَيْنِ أَوْ حَيْثُ تَيَسَّرَ مِنَ الْمَسْجِدِ

٢٥ وَجْهٌ: (١) الْحَدِيثُ لِثُبُوتِ وَيَرْمُلُ فِي الْأَشْوَاطِ الثَّلَاثِ الْأُوَلِ عَنِ ابْنِ عَبَّاسٍ رَضِيَ اللَّهُ عَنْهُمَا قَالَ: قَدِمَ رَسُولُ اللَّهِ صَلَّى اللهُ عَلَيْهِ وَسَلَّمَ وَأَصْحَابُهُ، فَقَالَ الْمُشْرِكُونَ: إِنَّهُ يَقْدَمُ عَلَيْكُمْ وَقَدْ وَهَنَهُمْ حُمَّى يَثْرِبَ، فَأَمَرَهُمُ النَّبِيُّ صَلَّى اللهُ عَلَيْهِ وَسَلَّمَ أَنْ يَرْمُلُوا الْأَشْوَاطَ الثَّلَاثَةَ، وَأَنْ يَمْشُوا مَا بَيْنَ الرُّكْنَيْنِ، (بخاري بَابٌ: كَيْفَ كَانَ بَدْءُ الرَّمَلِ: ١٦٠٢/ أَبُو دَاوُدَ: بَابٌ فِي الرَّمَلِ: ١٨٨٦) وَجْهٌ: (١) الْحَدِيثُ لِثُبُوتِ وَرَفَعَ يَدَيْهِ وَاسْتَلَمَهُ إِنِ اسْتَطَاعَ عَنِ ابْنِ عَبَّاسٍ رَضِيَ اللَّهُ عَنْهُمَا، قَالَ: «طَافَ النَّبِيُّ صَلَّى اللهُ عَلَيْهِ وَسَلَّمَ بِالْبَيْتِ عَلَى بَعِيرٍ، كُلَّمَا أَتَى الرُّكْنَ أَشَارَ إِلَيْهِ بِشَيْءٍ كَانَ عِنْدَهُ وَكَبَّرَ» (بخاري بَابُ التَّكْبِيرِ عِنْدَ الرُّكْنِ، نمر: ١٦١٣) وَجْهٌ: (١) الْحَدِيثُ لِثُبُوتِ وَرَفَعَ يَدَيْهِ وَاسْتَلَمَهُ إِنِ اسْتَطَاعَ عَنِ ابْنِ عُمَرَ، قَالَ: كَانَ رَسُولُ اللَّهِ صَلَّى اللهُ عَلَيْهِ وَسَلَّمَ لَا يَدَعُ أَنْ يَسْتَلِمَ الرُّكْنَ الْيَمَانِي وَالْحَجَرَ فِي كُلِّ طَوْفَةٍ». قَالَ: وَكَانَ عَبْدُ اللَّهِ بْنُ عُمَرَ يَفْعَلُهُ (أبو داؤد: بَابُ اسْتِلَامِ الْأَرْكَانِ نمر ١٨٧٦/ بخاري، نمر: ١٦١١) ٢٧ وَجْهٌ: (١) الْحَدِيثُ لِثُبُوتِ وَيَخْتَتِمُ بِالِاسْتِلَامِ عَنْ عَبْدِ الرَّحْمَنِ بْنِ صَفْوَانَ، قَالَ: «لَمَّا فَتَحَ رَسُولُ اللهِ صلى الله عليه وسلم مَكَّةَ قُلْتُ: لَأَلْبَسَنَّ ثِيَابِي وَكَانَتْ دَارِي عَلَى الطَّرِيقِ، فَلَأَنْظُرَنَّ كَيْفَ يَصْنَعُ رَسُولُ اللهِ صلى الله عليه وسلم فَانْطَلَقْتُ فَرَأَيْتُ النَّبِيَّ صلى الله عليه وسلم قَدْ خَرَجَ مِنَ الْكَعْبَةِ هُوَ وَأَصْحَابُهُ قَدِ اسْتَلَمُوا الْبَيْتَ مِنَ الْبَابِ إِلَى الْحَطِيمِ وَقَدْ وَضَعُوا خُدُودَهُمْ عَلَى الْبَيْتِ، وَرَسُولُ اللهِ صلى الله عليه وسلم وَسْطَهُمْ» (سنن للبيهقي: بَابُ الْمُلْتَزَمِ، نمر: ٩٣٣١) ٢٨ وَجْهٌ: (١) الْحَدِيثُ لِثُبُوتِ ثُمَّ يَأْتِي الْمَقَامَ فَيُصَلِّي عِنْدَهُ رَكْعَتَيْنِ قَالَ: سَمِعْتُ ابْنَ عُمَرَ رَضِيَ اللَّهُ عَنْهُمَا يَقُولُ: «قَدِمَ النَّبِيُّ صَلَّى اللهُ عَلَيْهِ وَسَلَّمَ فَطَافَ بِالْبَيْتِ سَبْعًا، وَصَلَّى خَلْفَ الْمَقَامِ رَكْعَتَيْنِ، ثُمَّ خَرَجَ إِلَى الصَّفَا» (بخاري بَابُ مَنْ صَلَّى رَكْعَتَيِ الطَّوَافِ خَلْفَ الْمَقَامِ: ١٦٢٧)

أُصُولٌ: طَوَافِ كَے اَوَائِلِ تِينْ شَوْطٍ مَیں رَمَلْ كَرْنَا مَسْنُونٌ هَے، یَعْنِي اَکَٹْر كَرْ چَلْے، اور آخِری چَارْ شَوْطٍ مَیں اپنی حَالَتْ پَر سُکُون و قَار كَیساتھ كَرے۔

كِتَابُ الْحَجِّ وَلَ وَهَذَا الطَّوَافُ طَوَافُ الْقُدُومِ وَهُوَ سُنَّةٌ وَلَيْسَ بِوَاجِبٍ وَلَيْسَ عَلَى أَهْلِ مَكَّةَ طَوَافُ الْقُدُومِ ٣٠ ثُمَّ يَخْرُجُ إِلَى الصَّفَا فَيَصْعَدُ عَلَيْهَا وَيَسْتَقْبِلُ الْبَيْتَ وَيُكَبِّرُ وَيُهَلِّلُ وَيُصَلِّي عَلَى النَّبِيِّ صَلَّى اللَّهُ عَلَيْهِ وَسَلَّمَ وَيَدْعُو اللَّهَ بِحَاجَتِهِ

وَجْهٌ: (٢) الْآيَةُ لِثُبُوتِ ثُمَّ يَأْتِي الْمَقَامَ فَيُصَلِّي عِنْدَهُ رَكْعَتَيْنِ {وَاتَّخِذُوا مِنْ مَقَامِ إِبْرَاهِيمَ مُصَلًّى} (سورة البقرة، ٢ أية نمر: ١٢٥)

وَجْهٌ: (٣) قَوْلُ التَّابِعِيِّ لِثُبُوتِ ثُمَّ يَأْتِي الْمَقَامَ فَيُصَلِّي عِنْدَهُ رَكْعَتَيْنِ قُلْتُ لِلزُهْرِيِّ: إِنَّ عَطَاءً يَقُولُ: تُجْزِتُهُ الْمَكْتُوبَةُ مِنْ رَكْعَتَيِ الطَّوَافِ؟ فَقَالَ: السُّنَّةُ أَفْضَلُ «لَمْ يَطُفِ النَّبِيُّ صَلَّى اللَّهُ عَلَيْهِ وَسَلَّمَ سُبُوعًا قَطُّ إِلَّا صَلَّى رَكْعَتَيْنِ» (بخاري: بَابٌ: لِسُبُوعِهِ رَكْعَتَيْنِ، نمر: ١٦٢٣)

وَلَ وَجْهٌ: (١) الْحَدِيثُ لِثُبُوتِ وَهَذَا الطَّوَافُ طَوَافُ الْقُدُومِ وَهُوَ سُنَّةٌ عَنْ وَبَرَةَ، قَالَ: كُنْتُ جَالِسًا عِنْدَ ابْنِ عُمَرَ فَجَاءَهُ رَجُلٌ فَقَالَ: أَيَصْلُحُ لِي أَنْ أَطُوفَ بِالْبَيْتِ قَبْلَ أَنْ آتِيَ الْمَوْقِفَ، فَقَالَ: نَعَمْ، فَقَالَ: فَإِنَّ ابْنَ عَبَّاسٍ يَقُولُ: لَا تَطُفْ بِالْبَيْتِ حَتَّى تَأْتِيَ الْمَوْقِفَ، فَقَالَ ابْنُ عُمَرَ: «فَقَدْ حَجَّ رَسُولُ اللَّهِ صَلَّى اللَّهُ عَلَيْهِ وَسَلَّمَ فَطَافَ بِالْبَيْتِ قَبْلَ أَنْ يَأْتِيَ الْمَوْقِفَ» فَبِقَوْلِ رَسُولِ اللهِ صَلَّى اللهُ عَلَيْهِ وَسَلَّمَ أَحَقُّ أَنْ تَأْخُذَ أَوْ بِقَوْلِ ابْنِ عَبَّاسٍ إِنْ كُنْتَ صَادِقًا (مسلم: بَابُ مَا يَلْزَمُ مَنْ أَحْرَمَ بِالْحَجِّ ثُمَّ قَدِمَ مَكَّةَ مِنَ الطَّوَافِ وَالسَّعْيِ نمر: ١٢٣٣)

٣٠ وَجْهٌ: (١) الْحَدِيثُ لِثُبُوتِ ثُمَّ يَخْرُجُ إِلَى الصَّفَا فَيَصْعَدُ عَلَيْهَا قَالَ: دَخَلْنَا عَلَى جَابِرِ بْنِ عَبْدِ اللَّهِ... ثُمَّ خَرَجَ مِنَ الْبَابِ إِلَى الصَّفَا فَلَمَّا دَنَا مِنَ الصَّفَا قَرَأَ: {إِنَّ الصَّفَا وَالْمَرْوَةَ مِنْ شَعَائِرِ اللهِ} [البقرة: ١٥٨] «أَبْدَأُ بِمَا بَدَأَ اللهُ بِهِ» فَبَدَأَ بِالصَّفَا فَرَقِيَ عَلَيْهِ، حَتَّى رَأَى الْبَيْتَ فَاسْتَقْبَلَ الْقِبْلَةَ، فَوَحَّدَ اللَّهَ وَكَبَّرَهُ، وَقَالَ: «لَا إِلَهَ إِلَّا اللهُ وَحْدَهُ لَا شَرِيكَ لَهُ، لَهُ الْمُلْكُ وَلَهُ الْحَمْدُ وَهُوَ عَلَى كُلِّ شَيْءٍ قَدِيرٌ، لَا إِلَهَ إِلَّا اللهُ وَحْدَهُ، أَنْجَزَ وَعْدَهُ، وَنَصَرَ عَبْدَهُ، وَهَزَمَ الْأَحْزَابَ وَحْدَهُ» ثُمَّ دَعَا بَيْنَ ذَلِكَ، قَالَ: مِثْلَ هَذَا ثَلَاثَ مَرَّاتٍ، ثُمَّ نَزَلَ إِلَى الْمَرْوَةِ، (مسلم: بَابُ حَجَّةِ النَّبِيِّ صَلَّى اللَّهُ عَلَيْهِ وَسَلَّمَ،:١٢١٨/أبوداؤد: بَابُ صِفَةِ حَجَّةِ النَّبِيِّ صَلَّى اللَّهُ عَلَيْهِ وَسَلَّمَ: ١٩٠٥)

أُصُولٌ: بَيْتُ اللَّهِ كَے چَارْ رُكْنٍ هَیں: ۱ رُكْنُ الْحَجَرِ الْأَسْوَدِ ۲ رُكْنُ الْيَمَانِي ۳ رُكْنُ الشَّامِي ٤ رُكْنُ الْعِرَاقِي۔ أُصُولٌ: بَيْتُ اللَّهِ كَے حَجَرِ الْأَسْوَدِ اور رُكْنِ يَمَانِي كُو چُومْنَا يَا اسْتِلَامُ كَرْنَا مَسْنُونَ هَے، اور باقی دو كَا اسْتِلَامُ نَہ كرے۔
The Book of Hajj. 25. And he performs ramal in the first three circuits and walks in what remains in his normal manner. 26. And he touches the Black Stone whenever he passes by it if he is able. 27. And he concludes with touching (istilam). 28. Then he comes to the Maqam and prays two rak'ahs near it or wherever is easy in the mosque. 25. Proof: (1) The hadith for establishing 'and he performs ramal in the first three circuits' from Ibn Abbas (may Allah be pleased with them both) who said: The Messenger of Allah (peace be upon him) and his companions arrived, and the polytheists said: 'Indeed he is coming to you while the fever of Yathrib has weakened them.' So the Prophet (peace be upon him) ordered them to perform ramal in the three circuits and to walk between the two corners. (Bukhari: Chapter: How ramal began, no. 1602 / Abu Dawud: Chapter on ramal, no. 1886). Proof: (1) The hadith for establishing 'and he raises his hands and touches it if he is able' from Ibn Abbas (may Allah be pleased with them both) who said: 'The Prophet (peace be upon him) performed tawaf of the House on a camel, whenever he came to the corner he pointed to it with something he had and said Allahu Akbar.' (Bukhari: Chapter of Takbir at the corner, no. 1613). Proof: (1) The hadith for establishing 'and he raises his hands and touches it if he is able' from Ibn Umar who said: 'The Messenger of Allah (peace be upon him) would not leave touching the Yemeni corner and the Stone in every circuit.' He said: 'And Abdullah ibn Umar used to do it.' (Abu Dawud: Chapter of touching the corners, no. 1876 / Bukhari, no. 1611). 27. Proof: (1) The hadith for establishing 'and he concludes with touching' from Abdur Rahman ibn Safwan who said: 'When the Messenger of Allah (peace be upon him) conquered Makkah, I said: I will put on my clothes—and my house was on the road—and I will watch how the Messenger of Allah (peace be upon him) acts. So I went and I saw the Prophet (peace be upon him) came out of the Kaaba, he and his companions, they had touched the House from the door to the Hatim and placed their cheeks on the House, and the Messenger of Allah (peace be upon him) was in their midst.' (Sunan al-Bayhaqi: Chapter of the Multazam, no. 9331). 28. Proof: (1) The hadith for establishing 'then he comes to the Maqam and prays two rak'ahs near it' — he said: I heard Ibn Umar (may Allah be pleased with them both) saying: 'The Prophet (peace be upon him) arrived and performed tawaf of the House seven times, and prayed two rak'ahs behind the Maqam, then went out to Safa.' (Bukhari: Chapter of whoever prays the two rak'ahs of tawaf behind the Maqam, no. 1627). Principle: Performing ramal in the first three circuits of tawaf is sunna, i.e., to walk briskly, and in the remaining four circuits to walk with tranquility and dignity. The Book of Hajj: And this tawaf is Tawaf al-Qudum, and it is sunna and not obligatory, and the people of Makkah are not required to perform Tawaf al-Qudum. 30. Then he goes out to Safa and ascends upon it, faces the House, says Allahu Akbar, says La ilaha illa Allah, sends salawat upon the Prophet (peace be upon him), and supplicates Allah for his need. Proof: (2) The verse for establishing 'then he comes to the Maqam and prays two rak'ahs near it': {And take from the Maqam of Ibrahim a place of prayer} (Surah al-Baqarah, 2, verse 125). Proof: (3) The saying of the Tabi'i for establishing 'then he comes to the Maqam and prays two rak'ahs near it' — I said to al-Zuhri: 'Indeed Ata says: The obligatory prayer suffices him from the two rak'ahs of tawaf?' He said: 'The sunna is better. The Prophet (peace be upon him) never performed any tawaf without praying two rak'ahs.' (Bukhari: Chapter: For his tawaf, two rak'ahs, no. 1623). And he said — Proof: (1) The hadith for establishing 'and this tawaf is Tawaf al-Qudum and it is sunna' from Wabarah who said: I was sitting with Ibn Umar when a man came to him and said: 'Is it permissible for me to perform tawaf of the House before I go to the standing place (Arafat)?' He said: 'Yes.' He said: 'Indeed Ibn Abbas says: Do not perform tawaf of the House until you go to the standing place.' Ibn Umar said: 'The Messenger of Allah (peace be upon him) performed Hajj and performed tawaf of the House before he went to the standing place. So is the saying of the Messenger of Allah (peace be upon him) more deserving to take or the saying of Ibn Abbas, if you are truthful?' (Muslim: Chapter of what is incumbent on one who enters ihram for Hajj then arrives in Makkah regarding tawaf and sa'i, no. 1233). 30. Proof: (1) The hadith for establishing 'then he goes out to Safa and ascends upon it' — he said: We entered upon Jabir ibn Abdillah... then he (the Prophet) came out of the door to Safa, and when he approached Safa he recited: {Indeed Safa and Marwa are from the symbols of Allah} [Al-Baqarah: 158] 'I begin with what Allah began with.' So he began with Safa and ascended upon it until he saw the House, then faced the Qibla, and declared the oneness of Allah and magnified Him, and said: 'There is no god but Allah alone, with no partner, His is the dominion and His is the praise, and He is over all things competent. There is no god but Allah alone, He fulfilled His promise, and helped His servant, and defeated the confederates alone.' Then he supplicated in between that. He said: The like of this three times, then he descended to Marwa. (Muslim: Chapter of the Prophet's Hajj, no. 1218 / Abu Dawud: Chapter of the description of the Prophet's Hajj, no. 1905). Principles: The House of Allah has four corners: 1. The Black Stone corner, 2. The Yemeni corner, 3. The Syrian corner, 4. The Iraqi corner. Principles: It is sunna to kiss or touch the Black Stone and the Yemeni corner of the House of Allah, and not to touch the remaining two.
Source pages p. 244

Commentary
This passage is a commentary on the rulings of Tawaf al-Qudum and Sa'i, presented as an expansion of the base matn (likely Al-Quduri) with hadith proofs and usul principles. The matn begins by detailing the sunan actions within the circumambulation (tawaf) performed upon arrival in Makkah (Tawaf al-Qudum). The first instruction is to perform ramal — walking with short, brisk steps with shoulder movement — in the first three circuits, and to walk normally in the remaining four. This is proven by the hadith from Ibn Abbas that the Prophet ordered ramal to show strength to the disbelievers. The matn then instructs touching the Black Stone (istilam) each time one passes by it, if possible, and to conclude the tawaf with istilam. The hadith from Ibn Umar confirms the Prophet's practice of touching the Yemeni corner and the Black Stone every circuit, and the hadith from Abdur Rahman ibn Safwan describes the Companions touching the House from the door to the Hatim after the conquest. After completing the seven circuits, the pilgrim prays two rak'ahs near Maqam Ibrahim (or anywhere in the mosque), proven by the hadith of Ibn Umar and the verse from Surah al-Baqarah. The saying of al-Zuhri emphasizes that the sunna is to pray these two rak'ahs specifically, not to substitute them with an obligatory prayer. The commentary then clarifies the legal nature of this tawaf: it is called Tawaf al-Qudum, it is sunna (not obligatory), and the residents of Makkah are not required to perform it. This is supported by the hadith where Ibn Umar refutes Ibn Abbas's view that tawaf before Arafat is impermissible, citing the Prophet's own practice. Finally, the passage describes the sa'i: after tawaf, the pilgrim goes to Safa, ascends it, faces the Kaaba, glorifies Allah, sends salawat, and makes supplication. The long hadith of Jabir details the Prophet's actions at Safa, including the specific dhikr repeated three times, then descending to Marwa. The concluding usul principle states that the Kaaba has four corners: Black Stone, Yemeni, Syrian, and Iraqi. It is sunna to kiss or touch only the Black Stone and the Yemeni corner, not the other two. This is a key point of Hanafi fiqh, as other schools may have different practices. The passage thus provides a comprehensive sunna-based guide for the opening rituals of the pilgrim arriving in Makkah.

Key Terms
السَّعْيُ (as-sa‘y): The walking between Safa and Marwa seven times, a rukn of Hajj and Umrah.
الصَّفَا (aṣ-ṣafā): A small hill near the Kaaba where sa'i begins.
الْمَرْوَةُ (al-marwah): The other hill where sa'i ends and begins again.

Key Terms from Source Passage

Checkpoint
According to the Hanafi school, what is the ruling of sa'i (walking between Safa and Marwa)?
A) Sunnah mu'akkadah
B) Wajib
C) Rukn (fard)
D) Mustahab

Key Takeaway
Sa'i is a rukn; its sunna procedure includes ascending Safa, facing Qibla, reciting specific dhikr three times with supplication.

Hajj — Pilgrimage
intermediate
12 min
Tawaf al-Qudum and the Sunan at Safa and Maqam Ibrahim
Defines Tawaf al-Qudum as sunna and describes subsequent sunan actions at Safa and Maqam Ibrahim

Learning Objective
By the end of this lesson, you will be able to state the Hanafi ruling of Tawaf al-Qudum (sunna for non-Makkans) and describe the recommended actions at Safa and Maqam Ibrahim, citing the textual proofs.

Core Idea
Tawaf al-Qudum is sunna for non-Makkans; its proof lies in the Prophet's practice, not an imperative command.

This passage from Al-Quduri's Mukhtasar clarifies the ruling on Tawaf al-Qudum, the circumambulation performed upon arriving in Makkah for Hajj. It explicitly states that it is sunna, not wajib, and that it does not apply to residents of Makkah. The author then details the subsequent sunan acts at Safa and Maqam Ibrahim, and provides a rich collection of proofs from the Quran and Sunnah to support these rulings. Understanding these distinctions is crucial for correctly performing the Hajj rituals according to the Hanafi school.

Guided Path
1
Identify the act and its ruling
The passage begins by stating that Tawaf al-Qudum is sunna, not wajib. It also specifies that there is no Tawaf al-Qudum for the people of Makkah. Note the categorical distinction.
The term sunna here means recommended, not obligatory. The exception for Makkans is based on their constant presence.
2
Outline the sunan actions at Safa and Maqam
After tawaf, the pilgrim goes to Safa, ascends, faces the Kaaba, makes takbir, tahlil, sends salawat on the Prophet, and makes dua. Then he goes to Maqam Ibrahim and prays two rak'ats. These are all sunan actions established by the Prophet's practice.
The actions at Safa include the specific dhikr mentioned in the hadith of Jabir.
3
Locate the proofs (dalil) and explain wajh al-dalalah
The author cites four proofs: Quran 2:125, the hadith of Ibn Umar (showing the Prophet performed tawaf before Arafat), the hadith of Jabir (detailing actions at Safa), and the hadith of al-Zuhri (establishing the two rak'ats after tawaf as sunna). Explain how each proof supports the sunna ruling, e.g., the imperative in 'اتخذوا' indicates recommendation, and the Prophet's actions demonstrate practice.
The imperative is interpreted as a recommendation (nadb) in Hanafi usul due to the absence of a specific command indicating obligation.
4
Note the ikhtilaf and thamarah
Some scholars (e.g., Hanbalis) consider Tawaf al-Qudum wajib. The Hanafi school holds sunna. The practical difference: missing it is not sinful but reward is lost; those who deem it wajib require compensation (dam) if omitted.
The Hanafi position is based on the strong evidence of the Prophet's action, which is considered sunna muakkadah.

وَهَذَا الطَّوَافُ طَوَافُ الْقُدُومِ وَهُوَ سُنَّةٌ وَلَيْسَ بِوَاجِبٍ وَلَيْسَ عَلَى أَهْلِ مَكَّةَ طَوَافُ الْقُدُومِ. ثُمَّ يَخْرُجُ إِلَى الصَّفَا فَيَصْعَدُ عَلَيْهَا وَيَسْتَقْبِلُ الْبَيْتَ وَيُكَبِّرُ وَيُهَلِّلُ وَيُصَلِّي عَلَى النَّبِيِّ صَلَّى اللَّهُ عَلَيْهِ وَسَلَّمَ وَيَدْعُو اللَّهَ بِحَاجَتِهِ. ثُمَّ يَأْتِي الْمَقَامَ فَيُصَلِّي عِنْدَهُ رَكْعَتَيْنِ. وَالدَّلِيلُ: قَوْلُهُ تَعَالَى: {وَاتَّخِذُوا مِن مَّقَامِ إِبْرَاهِيمَ مُصَلًّى} [البقرة: 125]. وَحَدِيثُ ابْنِ عُمَرَ: عَنْ وَبَرَةَ قَالَ: كُنْتُ جَالِسًا عِنْدَ ابْنِ عُمَرَ فَجَاءَهُ رَجُلٌ فَقَالَ: أَيَصْلُحُ لِي أَنْ أَطُوفَ بِالْبَيْتِ قَبْلَ أَنْ آتِيَ الْمَوْقِفَ؟ فَقَالَ: نَعَمْ، فَقَالَ: فَإِنَّ ابْنَ عَبَّاسٍ يَقُولُ: لَا تَطُفْ بِالْبَيْتِ حَتَّى تَأْتِيَ الْمَوْقِفَ، فَقَالَ ابْنُ عُمَرَ: فَقَدْ حَجَّ رَسُولُ اللَّهِ صَلَّى اللَّهُ عَلَيْهِ وَسَلَّمَ فَطَافَ بِالْبَيْتِ قَبْلَ أَنْ يَأْتِيَ الْمَوْقِفَ، فَبِقَوْلِ رَسُولِ اللَّهِ صَلَّى اللَّهُ عَلَيْهِ وَسَلَّمَ أَحَقُّ أَنْ تَأْخُذَ أَوْ بِقَوْلِ ابْنِ عَبَّاسٍ إِنْ كُنْتَ صَادِقًا. (رَوَاهُ مُسْلِمٌ). وَحَدِيثُ جَابِرٍ: دَخَلْنَا عَلَى جَابِرِ بْنِ عَبْدِ اللَّهِ، ثُمَّ خَرَجَ مِنَ الْبَابِ إِلَى الصَّفَا فَلَمَّا دَنَا مِنَ الصَّفَا قَرَأَ: {إِنَّ الصَّفَا وَالْمَرْوَةَ مِنْ شَعَائِرِ اللَّهِ} [البقرة: 158] قَالَ: أَبْدَأُ بِمَا بَدَأَ اللَّهُ بِهِ، فَبَدَأَ بِالصَّفَا فَرَقِيَ عَلَيْهِ، حَتَّى رَأَى الْبَيْتَ فَاسْتَقْبَلَ الْقِبْلَةَ، فَوَجَّدَ اللَّهَ وَكَبَّرَهُ، وَقَالَ: لَا إِلَهَ إِلَّا اللَّهُ وَحْدَهُ لَا شَرِيكَ لَهُ، لَهُ الْمُلْكُ وَلَهُ الْحَمْدُ وَهُوَ عَلَى كُلِّ شَيْءٍ قَدِيرٌ، لَا إِلَهَ إِلَّا اللَّهُ وَحْدَهُ، أَنْجَزَ وَعْدَهُ، وَنَصَرَ عَبْدَهُ، وَهَزَمَ الْأَحْزَابَ وَحْدَهُ، ثُمَّ دَعَا بَيْنَ ذَلِكَ، قَالَ: مِثْلَ هَذَا ثَلَاثَ مَرَّاتٍ، ثُمَّ نَزَلَ إِلَى الْمَرْوَةِ. (رَوَاهُ مُسْلِمٌ وَأَبُو دَاوُدَ). وَحَدِيثُ الزُّهْرِيِّ: قُلْتُ لِلزُّهْرِيِّ: إِنَّ عَطَاءً يَقُولُ: تُجْزِئُهُ الْمَكْتُوبَةُ مِنْ رَكْعَتَيِ الطَّوَافِ؟ فَقَالَ: السُّنَّةُ أَفْضَلُ. وَلَمْ يَطُفِ النَّبِيُّ صَلَّى اللَّهُ عَلَيْهِ وَسَلَّمَ سُبُوعًا قَطُّ إِلَّا صَلَّى رَكْعَتَيْنِ. (رَوَاهُ الْبُخَارِيُّ).
And this tawaf is Tawaf al-Qudum, and it is sunna and not wajib, and there is no tawaf al-qudum upon the people of Makkah. Then he goes out to as-Safa and ascends upon it, faces the House, says Allahu Akbar, says La ilaha illallah, sends blessings upon the Prophet (ﷺ), and supplicates Allah for his need. Then he comes to al-Maqam and prays two rak'ats near it. The proof: The statement of Allah Most High: {And take from the standing place of Ibrahim a place of prayer} [al-Baqarah:125]. And the hadith of Ibn Umar: From Wabarah: I was sitting with Ibn Umar when a man came and said: Is it proper for me to circumambulate the House before I go to the standing place? He said: Yes. He said: But Ibn Abbas says: Do not circumambulate the House until you come to the standing place. Ibn Umar said: The Messenger of Allah (ﷺ) performed Hajj and circumambulated the House before coming to the standing place. So which is more deserving to take, the saying of the Messenger of Allah or the saying of Ibn Abbas, if you are truthful? (Muslim). And the hadith of Jabir: We entered upon Jabir ibn Abdullah... then he went out from the door to as-Safa, and when he approached as-Safa he recited: {Indeed as-Safa and al-Marwah are among the symbols of Allah} [al-Baqarah:158]. He said: I begin with what Allah began with, so he started with as-Safa and climbed upon it until he saw the House, then he faced the qiblah, proclaimed Allah's oneness and magnified Him, and said: There is no god but Allah alone, no partner, to Him belongs the kingdom and praise, and He is powerful over all things; there is no god but Allah alone, He fulfilled His promise, helped His servant, and defeated the confederates alone. Then he made supplication in between that. He said: like this three times, then he descended to al-Marwah. (Muslim and Abu Dawud). And the hadith of al-Zuhri: I said to al-Zuhri: Ata says: The obligatory prayer suffices him from the two rak'ats of tawaf? He said: The sunna is better. And the Prophet (ﷺ) never performed a circumambulation without praying two rak'ats. (Bukhari).
Source pages p. 245

Commentary
This passage begins by stating the ruling of Tawaf al-Qudum. It is sunna, not wajib, meaning recommended but not obligatory. Exception: people of Makkah are not required to perform it because they are already present. After tawaf, the pilgrim goes to as-Safa, ascends, faces the Kaaba, makes takbir, tahmid, sends salawat on the Prophet, and makes dua. Then he goes to Maqam Ibrahim and prays two rak'ats. The author provides proofs: the verse commanding to take Maqam Ibrahim as a place of prayer, the hadith of Ibn Umar showing the Prophet performed tawaf before going to Arafat, making it sunna, the hadith of Jabir detailing the actions at Safa, and the hadith of al-Zuhri emphasizing that the two rak'ats after tawaf are a confirmed sunna, not replaced by fard prayer. Thus, the actions are established by the Qur'an and the practice of the Prophet (ﷺ).

Key Terms
طَوَافُ الْقُدُومِ (Tawāf al-Qudūm): The circumambulation performed upon first arriving in Makkah during Hajj, before standing at Arafat.
الصَّفَا (aṣ-Ṣafā): A small hill near the Kaaba, one of the two points between which sa'y is performed.
الْمَقَامُ (al-Maqām): The Station of Ibrahim, near the Kaaba, where Ibrahim stood during the construction of the House.

Key Terms from Source Passage

Key Takeaway
Tawaf al-Qudum is a confirmed sunna for non-Makkans; the subsequent acts at Safa and Maqam Ibrahim are sunan supported by the Prophet's practice.

The Sa'y Between Safa and Marwah: Actions and Proof of Obligation
Describes the actions of sa'y and proves its obligation via three hadith and usul

Learning Objective
By the end of this lesson, you will be able to describe the actions of sa'y and explain why the Hanafi school classifies it as wajib using the three hadith proofs.

Core Idea
Sa'y is wajib: the Prophet's command and Aisha's clarification confirm its obligation, not optional.

The ritual of sa'y between Safa and Marwah is a central act of Hajj and Umrah. In this passage, the classical Hanafi text describes the precise manner of performing sa'y—walking normally in most parts but running between the two green markers—and then provides three hadith proofs that establish its obligation. Understanding these proofs is essential to grasp why the Hanafi school classifies sa'y as wajib rather than fard, and to respond to common misunderstandings about the Quranic verse.

Guided Path
1
Identify the Act and Its Ruling
The passage describes the actions of sa'y: descending from Safa, walking normally, then running between the two green markers in the valley (Batan al-Wadi) until reaching Marwah, and repeating the same actions. The ruling stated in the Urdu principle is that sa'y is wajib.
Note the distinction: walking normally outside the markers, running between them.
2
Locate the First Dalil (Hadith of Jabir)
The hadith of Jabir narrates that the Prophet (ﷺ) descended from Safa and ran after his feet left the sacred area of the mas'a until he completed his sa'y. This proves the action of running in the valley.
This hadith establishes the manner, not the obligation directly.
3
Locate the Second Dalil (Hadith of Aisha) and Its Wajh al-Dalalah
The hadith of Aisha clarifies the misinterpretation of Quran 2:158. The verse 'There is no harm upon him if he does not circumambulate them' was revealed regarding the Ansar who refrained from sa'y before Islam. Aisha explains that the verse means there is no harm in performing sa'y, not that it is optional. This negates the misconception that sa'y can be omitted.
Key point: the negation of sin (la junah) does not imply permission to omit; rather, it affirms the act.
4
Locate the Third Dalil (Hadith of Barrah) and Its Wajh al-Dalalah
The hadith of Barrah quotes the Prophet (ﷺ) saying, 'Perform sa'y, for Allah has prescribed sa'y upon you.' The imperative verb 'اسعوا' (perform sa'y) indicates obligation (wujub) according to Hanafi usul, especially with the added statement that Allah has prescribed it.
This is the clearest proof of wujub.
5
Note the Ikhtilaf and Tarjih
Imam al-Shafi'i considers sa'y a fard (pillar) of Hajj/Umrah, meaning it invalidates the acts if omitted. The Hanafi position is wajib: omission does not invalidate but requires a dam (sacrifice). The text relies on the hadith evidence and does not engage in detailed tarjih, but the Hanafi position is mufta bihi.
The practical difference: if sa'y is omitted, Hajj is valid but a dam is due (Hanafi); if omitted, Hajj is invalid (Shafi'i).

Source Text
⚠ Extracted via Advanced OCR ∼97% accuracy, minor errors may remain — always verify against original Arabic books
وَيَنْحَطُّ نَحْوَ الْمَرْوَةِ وَيَمْشِي عَلَى هَيْئَتِهِ فَإِذَا بَلَغَ إِلَى بَطْنِ الْوَادِي سَعَى بَيْنَ الْمِيلَيْنِ الْأَخْضَرَيْنِ حَتَّى يَأْتِيَ الْمَرْوَةَ وَيَفْعَلُ كَمَا فَعَلَ عَلَى الصَّفَا. وَالدَّلِيلُ: حَدِيثُ جَابِرٍ: ثُمَّ نَزَلَ إِلَى الْمَرْوَةِ حَتَّى إِذَا انْفَصَلَتْ قَدَمَاهُ عَنْ حَرَمِ الْمَسْعَى سَعَى حَتَّى قَضَى سَعْيَهُ. (مُسْلِمٌ). وَحَدِيثُ عَائِشَةَ: قُلْتُ لِعَائِشَةَ: إِنِّي لَأَظُنُّ رَجُلًا لَوْ لَمْ يَطُفْ بَيْنَ الصَّفَا وَالْمَرْوَةِ مَا ضَرَّهُ. قَالَتْ: لِمَ؟ قُلْتُ: لِأَنَّ اللَّهَ تَعَالَى يَقُولُ: {فَلَا جُنَاحَ عَلَيْهِ أَنْ لَا يَطَّوَّفَ بِهِمَا} . فَقَالَتْ: لَوْ كَانَ كَمَا تَقُولُ لَكَانَ: فَلَا جُنَاحَ عَلَيْهِ أَنْ لَا يَطَّوَّفَ بِهِمَا، وَلَكِنَّ الْآيَةَ نَزَلَتْ فِي الْأَنْصَارِ كَانُوا لَا يُفِيضُونَ مِنْ مِنًى حَتَّى تُشْرِقَ الشَّمْسُ، فَنَزَلَتْ: {فَلَا جُنَاحَ عَلَيْهِ أَنْ يَطَّوَّفَ بِهِمَا} . (مُتَّفَقٌ عَلَيْهِ). وَحَدِيثُ بَرَّةَ بِنْتِ أَبِي تَجْرَاةَ قَالَتْ: رَأَيْتُ رَسُولَ اللَّهِ صَلَّى اللَّهُ عَلَيْهِ وَسَلَّمَ حِينَ انْتَهَى إِلَى الْمَسْعَى قَالَ: اسْعَوْا فَإِنَّ اللَّهَ كَتَبَ عَلَيْكُمُ السَّعْيَ. (رَوَاهُ ابْنُ مَاجَهْ). أَصُولُ: صَفَاءُ وَمَرْوَةَ كَي دَرْمِيَانَ سَعِي كَرْنَا وَاجِبْ هَي وَمِيلَيْنِ أَخْضَرَيْنِ مَيْنْ تَيْزْ قَدْمُو سَي چَلَّي.
And he descends towards al-Marwah, walking in his normal manner. When he reaches the bottom of the valley, he runs between the two green markers until he comes to al-Marwah, and he does as he did on as-Safa. And the proof: The hadith of Jabir: Then he descended to al-Marwah until when his feet left the sacred area of the mas'a, he ran until he completed his sa'y. (Muslim). And the hadith of Aisha: I said to Aisha: I think a man would not be harmed if he did not circumambulate between as-Safa and al-Marwah. She said: Why? I said: Because Allah says: 'There is no harm upon him if he does not circumambulate them.' She said: If it were as you say, it would be: 'There is no harm upon him if he does NOT circumambulate them', but the verse was revealed about the Ansar who would not depart from Mina until the sun rose high, so it was revealed: 'There is no harm upon him that he circumambulates them.' (Agreed upon). And the hadith of Barrah bint Abi Tajrah: She said: I saw the Messenger of Allah (ﷺ) when he reached the mas'a, he said: 'Perform sa'y, for Allah has prescribed sa'y upon you.' (Ibn Majah). Principle: Sa'y between Safa and Marwah is wajib, and one should walk quickly between the two green markers.
Source pages p. 246

Commentary
This passage describes the actions of sa'y (walking/ running) between Safa and Marwah. The pilgrim descends from Safa towards Marwah, walking normally until reaching the bottom of the valley (Batan al-Wadi), then runs between the two green markers (Milayn Akhḍarayn) until reaching Marwah, where he repeats the same actions as on Safa. The author provides three proofs for the obligation of sa'y: (1) The hadith of Jabir shows the Prophet (ﷺ) performed sa'y with running in the valley. (2) The hadith of Aisha clarifies that the verse 'no harm if he does not circumambulate them' was misunderstood; actually, the verse means there is no harm if one does circumambulate, not that it is optional. Aisha explains the correct context, proving sa'y is obligatory. (3) The hadith of Barrah directly quotes the Prophet commanding sa'y and stating Allah has prescribed it. The Urdu principle (usul) confirms: Sa'y is wajib, and one should run (quickly) between the two green markers.

Key Terms
السَّعْيُ (as-Sa'y): The ritual walking/running between the hills of Safa and Marwah during Hajj and Umrah.
الْمِيلَيْنِ الْأَخْضَرَيْنِ (al-Mīlayn al-Akhḍarayn): Two green markers in the valley (Batan al-Wadi) between Safa and Marwah, between which the pilgrim runs during sa'y.
بَطْنُ الْوَادِي (Baṭn al-Wādī): The valley floor between Safa and Marwah where running (ramal) is prescribed.

Key Terms from Source Passage

Checkpoint
According to the Hanafi school, what is the ruling of sa'y between Safa and Marwah?
A) Fard (pillar) - invalid without it.
B) Wajib (obligatory) - valid without it but requires dam.
C) Sunnah muakkadah.
D) Mubah.

Key Takeaway
Sa'y between Safa and Marwah is wajib in the Hanafi school, proven by the Prophet's command and Aisha's clarification, and omission requires a dam but does not invalidate the Hajj or Umrah.
