The Hanafi Ruling on Sa'i: Obligation and Method
Matn with proofs on sa'i's obligation and manner

Learning Objective
By the end of this lesson, you will be able to state the Hanafi ruling on sa'i, explain its proofs from the Quran and Sunnah, and distinguish it from the Shafi'i view.

Core Idea
Sa'i is wajib, not optional; the Quranic 'no sin' confirms its necessity through Aisha's clarification.

This lesson examines the Hanafi position on sa'i, the ritual walking between Safa and Marwah during Hajj and Umrah. The source text from Al-Quduri describes the manner and number of laps and provides proof that sa'i is wajib (obligatory). Understanding this ruling is essential because the distinction between wajib and fard affects the validity of the pilgrimage and the required compensation.

Guided Path
1
Identify the Act and Its Ruling
What act is being ruled upon? What is its hukm level according to the Hanafi school?
The text states sa'i is performed between Safa and Marwah. The Hanafi school classifies it as wajib.
2
Locate the Primary Dalil
Which proof does the text cite first? How does the Quranic verse (2:158) support the obligation?
The verse says 'no sin upon him who does not perform it,' but the context and practice indicate obligation.
3
Understand the Interpretation via Aisha's Hadith
How does the Companion's explanation clarify the verse? What is the key point in Aisha's response?
Aisha corrects the misconception by pointing out that if sa'i were optional, the verse would have said 'no sin in not doing it.'
4
Identify the Manner and Number of Laps
How many laps are required? What are the starting and ending points? What special action is done between the green milestones?
Seven laps, starting from Safa and ending at Marwah. Between the green milestones, the pilgrim runs (harwala).
5
Note the Ikhtilaf (Dispute) with the Shafi'i School
How does the Shafi'i school differ? What is the practical consequence of the difference?
Shafi'i considers sa'i a rukn (pillar). Hanafi says wajib. Consequence: omission in Hanafi requires dam; in Shafi'i, Hajj is invalid.

Source Text
⚠ Extracted via Advanced OCR ∼97% accuracy, minor errors may remain — always verify against original Arabic books
كِتَابُ الْحَجّ وَيَنْحَطُّ نَحْوَ الْمَرْوَةِ وَيَمْشِي عَلَى هَيْئَتِهِ فَإِذَا بَلَغَ إِلَى بَطْنِ الْوَادِي سَعَى بَيْنَ الْمِيلَيْنِ الْأَخْضَرَيْنِ حَتَّى يَأْتِي الْمَرْوَةَ وَيَفْعَلُ كَمَا فَعَلَ عَلَى الصَّفَا
وجه: (٢) الآية لثبوت ثُمَّ يَخْرُجُ إِلَى الصَّفَا فَيَصْعَدُ عَلَيْهَا إنَّ الصَّفَا وَالْمَرْوَةَ مِن شَعَابِرِ اللَّهِ فَمَنْ حَجَّ الْبَيْتَ أَوِ اعْتَمَرَ فَلَا جُنَاحَ عَلَيْهِ أَن يَطَّوَّفَ بِهِمَا (سورة البقرة، 2 آيت: 158) وجه (۳) الحديث لثبوت ثُمَّ يَخْرُجُ إلَى الصَّفَا فَيَصْعَدُ عَلَيْهَا حَدَّثَنَا جَابِرٌ «أَنَّ رَسُولَ اللَّهِ صَلَّى اللهُ عَلَيْهِ وَسَلَّمَ، رَقِيَ عَلَى الصَّفَا حَتَّى إِذَا نَظَرَ إِلَى الْبَيْتِ كَبَّرَ» (سنن النسائي: مَوْضِعُ الْقِيَامِ عَلَى الصَّفَا، نمبر : 2974) ٣١ وجه: (1) الحديث لثبوت وَيَنْحَطُّ نَحْوَ الْمَرْوَةِ وَيَمْشِي قَالَ: دَخَلْنَا عَلَى جَابِرِ بْنِ عَبْدِ اللَّهِ، . ثُمَّ خَرَجَ مِنَ الْبَابِ إِلَى الصَّفَا فَلَمَّا دَنَا مِنَ الصَّفَا قَرَأَ: {إِنَّ الصَّفَا وَالْمَرْوَةَ مِنْ شَعَائِرِ اللَّهِ} [البقرة: 158] «أَبْدَأُ بِمَا بَدَأَ اللهُ بِهِ فَبَدَأَ بِالصَّفَا فَرَقِيَ عَلَيْهِ، حَتَّى رَأَى الْبَيْتَ فَاسْتَقْبَلَ الْقِبْلَةَ، فَوَجَّدَ اللَّهَ وَكَبَّرَهُ، وَقَالَ: «لَا إِلَهَ إِلَّا اللهُ وَحْدَهُ لَا شَرِيكَ لَهُ، لَهُ الْمُلْكُ وَلَهُ الْحَمْدُ وَهُوَ عَلَى كُلِّ شَيْءٍ قَدِيرٌ، لَا إِلَهَ إِلَّا اللهُ وَحْدَهُ، أَنْجَزَ وَعْدَهُ، وَنَصَرَ عَبْدَهُ، وَهَزَمَ الْأَحْزَابَ وَحْدَهُ» ثُمَّ دَعَا بَيْنَ ذَلِكَ، قَالَ: مِثْلَ هَذَا ثَلَاثَ مَرَّاتٍ، ثُمَّ نَزَلَ إِلَى الْمَرْوَةِ، (مسلم: بَابُ حَجَّةِ النَّبِيِّ صَلَّى اللهُ عَلَيْهِ وَسَلَّمَ،: 1218/ أبو داؤد: بَابُ صِفَةِ حَجَّةِ النَّبِيِّ صَلَّى اللَّهُ عَلَيْهِ وَسَلَّمَ، نمبر: 1905) وجه:(۲)قول الصحابية لثبوت وَيَنْحَطُّ نَحْوَ الْمَرْوَةِ وَيَمْشِي عَلَى هِيئَتِهِ آعَنْ عُرْوَةَ، عَنْ عَائِشَةَ، قَالَ: قُلْتُ لَهَا: إِنّي لَأَظُنُّ رَجُلًا، لَوْ لَمْ يَطْفْ بَيْنَ الصَّفَا وَالْمَرْوَةِ، مَا ضَرَّهُ، قَالَتْ: «لم؟» قُلْتُ : لأَنَّ اللهَ تَعَالَى يَقُولُ: {إِنَّ الصَّفَا وَالْمَرْوَةَ مِنْ شَعَائِرِ اللهِ} [البقرة: 158] إلى آخر الآية، فَقَالَتْ : " مَا أَتَمَّ اللهُ حَجَّ امْرِئٍ وَلَا عُمْرَتَهُ لَم يَطْفْ بَيْنَ الصَّفَا وَالْمَرْوَةِ، وَلَوْ كَانَ كَمَا تَقُولُ لَكَانَ: فَلَا جُنَاحَ عَلَيْهِ أَنْ لَا يَطَّوَّفَ بِهِمَا، مسلم: بَابُ بَيَانِ أَنَّ السَّعْيَ بَيْنَ الصَّفَا وَالْمَرْوَةِ وَكُنٌ، غَير : 1277/ بخاري: بَابُ وُجُوبِ الصَّفَا وَالْمَرْوَةِ، وَجُعِلَ مِنْ شَعَائِرِ اللَّهِ، نمبر: 1643) وجه : (۳) الحديث لثبوت وَيَنْحَطُّ نَحْوَ الْمَرْوَةِ وَيَمْشِي عَلَى هِيئَتِهِ عَنْ بَرَّةَ بِنْتِ أَبِي تَجْرَاةَ, قَالَتْ : رَأَيْتُ رَسُولَ اللَّهِ صَلَّى اللَّهُ عَلَيْهِ وَسَلَّمَ حِينَ انْتَهَى إِلَى الْمَسْعَى قَالَ: «اسْعَوْا فَإِنَّ اللَّهَ كَتَبَ عَلَيْكُمُ السَّعْيَ» . فَرَأَيْتُهُ يَسْعَى حَتَّى بَدَتْ رُكْبَتَاهُ مِنِ انْكِشَافِ إِزَارِهِ (سنن الدار قطني: كتاب الحج، نمبر: 2583)
اصول : صفاء و مروہ کے درمیان سعی کرنا وجب ہے اور میلین اخضرین میں تیز قدموں سے چلے۔
وَهَذَا شَوْطٌ فَيَطُوفُ سَبْعَةَ أَشْوَاطٍ يَبْتَدِئُ بِالصَّفَا وَيَخْتِمُ بِالْمَرْوَةِ ثُمَّ يُقِيمُ بِمَكَّةَ حَرَامًا يَطُوفُ بِالْبَيْتِ كُلَّمَا بَدَا لَهُ وَيُصَلِّي لِكُلِّ أَسْبُوعِ رَكْعَتَيْنِ
۳۲ وجه : (۱) قول التابعى لثبوت وَهَذَا شَوْطٌ فَيَطُوفُ سَبْعَةَ أَشْوَاطٍ \ قَالَ: سَمِعْتُ عَبْدَ اللَّهِ بْنَ أَبِي أَوْفَى بِهَذَا الْحَدِيثِ زَادَ ثُمَّ أَتَى الصَّفَا وَالْمَرْوَةَ فَسَعَى بَيْنَهُمَا سَبْعًا ثُمَّ حَلَقَ رَأْسَهُ (أبو داؤد: بَابُ أَمْرِ الصَّفَا وَالْمَرْوَةِ، نمبر: 1903
وجه:(۲) الحديث لثبوت وَهَذَا شَوْطٌ فَيَطُوفُ سَبْعَةَ أَشْوَاطٍ \ فَقَالَ: ابْنُ عُمَرَ: " قَدِمَ رَسُولُ اللهِ صَلَّى اللهُ عَلَيْهِ وَسَلَّمَ فَطَافَ بِالْبَيْتِ سَبْعًا وَصَلَّى خَلْفَ الْمَقَامِ رَكْعَتَيْنِ, وَطَافَ بَيْنَ الصَّفَا وَالْمَرْوَةِ سَبْعًا وَ لَقَدْ كَانَ لَكُمْ فِي رَسُولِ اللهِ أَسْوَةٌ حَسَنَةٌ} (سنن للبيهقي: بَابُ وُجُوبِ الطَّوَافِ بَيْنَ الصَّفَا وَالْمَرْوَةِ وَأَنَّ غَيْرَهُ لَا يُجْزِي عَنْهُ، نمبر : 9363)
وجه (۳) قول التابعى لثبوت وَهَذَا شَوْطٌ فَيَطُوفُ سَبْعَةَ أَشْوَاطِ اعَنْ عَطَاءٍ قَالَ: سَأَلْتُ عَنْ رَجُلٍ سَعَى بَيْنَ الصَّفَا وَالْمَرْوَةِ أَرْبَعَ عَشْرَةَ مَرَّةً قَالَ: «يُعِيدُ» (مصنف ابن أبي شيبة: في الرَّجُلِ يَسْعَى بَيْنَ الصَّفَا وَالْمَرْوَةِ أَرْبَعَةَ عَشَرَ مَرَّةً، غبر : 15378)
٣٣ وجه : (۱) الحديث لثبوت ثُمَّ يُقِيمُ بِمَكَّةَ حَرَامًا يَطُوفُ بِالْبَيْتِ \ عَنْ طَاوُسٍ، عَنْ رَجُلٍ أَدْرَكَ النَّبِيَّ صلى الله عليه وسلم قَالَ: «الطَّوَافُ بِالْبَيْتِ صَلَاةٌ فَأَقِلُوا مِنَ الْكَلَامِ» (سنن النسائي: التَّكْبِيرُ فِي نَوَاحِي الْكَعْبَةِ، نمبر: 2923)
وجه: (٢) الحديث لثبوت ثُمَّ يُقِيمُ بِمَكَّةَ حَرَامًا يَطُوفُ بِالْبَيْتِ أَعَنْ ابْنِ عَبَّاسٍ، أَنَّ النَّبِيَّ صَلَّى اللهُ عَلَيْهِ وَسَلَّمَ قَالَ: «الطَّوَافُ حَوْلَ البَيْتِ مِثْلُ الصَّلَاةِ، إِلَّا أَنَّكُمْ تَتَكَلَّمُونَ فِيهِ، فَمَنْ تَكَلَّمَ فِيهِ فَلَا يَتَكَلَّمَنَّ إِلَّا بِخَيْرٍ» (الترمذي : بَابُ مَا جَاءَ فِي الكَلَامِ فِي الطَّوَافِ، نمبر: 960)
وجه (۳) الحديث لثبوت ثُمَّ يُقِيمُ بِمَكَّةَ حَرَامًا يَطُوفُ بِالْبَيْتِ عَنْ ابْنِ عَبَّاسِ قَالَ: قَالَ رَسُولُ اللَّهِ صَلَّى اللَّهُ عَلَيْهِ وَسَلَّمَ: «مَنْ طَافَ بِالْبَيْتِ خَمْسِينَ مَرَّةً خَرَجَ مِنْ ذُنُوبِهِ كَيَوْمِ وَلَدَتْهُ أُمُّهُ» (الترمذي: بَابُ مَا جَاءَ فِي الكَلَامِ فِي الطَّوَافِ، نمبر: 866)
Book of Hajj. And he descends towards al-Marwah and walks in his normal manner. When he reaches the bottom of the valley, he runs between the two green milestones until he comes to al-Marwah and does as he did on as-Safa. Proof 2: The verse for establishing (the ruling) ... Proof 3: The hadith for establishing ... Proof 1: The hadith for establishing ... Proof 2: The saying of the Companion for establishing ... Proof 3: The hadith for establishing ... Principle: Sa'i between Safa and Marwah is obligatory, and between the two green milestones he should walk with fast steps. And this is one lap, so he performs seven laps, starting from as-Safa and ending at al-Marwah. Then he stays in Makkah in ihram, performing tawaf of the House whenever he wishes, and for every seven tawaf circuits he prays two rak'ahs. Proof 1: The saying of the Tabi'i for establishing ... Source pages p. 246

Commentary
This passage from Al-Quduri outlines the rulings of sa'i (the ritual walking) between Safa and Marwah during Hajj or Umrah. The text first describes the manner: the pilgrim descends from Safa towards Marwah, walking normally until reaching the bottom of the valley (Batan al-Wadi). Between the two green milestones (al-mileyn al-akhdarayn), he runs (sa'a) with fast steps, a practice known as harwala, until reaching Marwah, where he repeats the actions performed on Safa (facing the Kaaba, making takbir, supplicating). The author then provides three proofs: (1) the Quranic verse (2:158) establishing Safa and Marwah as symbols of Allah, and the hadith of Jabir describing the Prophet's practice; (2) the hadith of Aisha confirming that sa'i is obligatory; (3) the hadith of Barrah bint Abi Tajrah witnessing the Prophet commanding sa'i. An Urdu note clarifies that sa'i is wajib (obligatory) and that the fast pace between the green milestones is required. The text then states that each crossing (from Safa to Marwah or vice versa) is one lap (shawt), and the total is seven laps, starting from Safa and ending at Marwah. After completing sa'i, the pilgrim remains in Makkah in ihram and may perform tawaf around the Kaaba as often as desired, praying two rak'ahs for each seven circuits (i.e., after each tawaf). Additional proofs are cited: the practice of Ibn Umar and hadith emphasizing the virtue of tawaf. The passage thus establishes the wajib nature of sa'i, its prescribed number of laps, and the recommended tawaf thereafter.

Key Terms
سعى (sa'y): The ritual walking between Safa and Marwah during Hajj or Umrah. The text describes it as seven laps, with normal walking and running between the green milestones.
الصفا والمروة (as-Safa wa al-Marwah): Two small hills near the Kaaba in Makkah between which the sa'i is performed. The text uses them as the starting and ending points.
الميلان الأخضران (al-mileyn al-akhdarayn): Two green milestones in the valley between Safa and Marwah that mark the area where the pilgrim runs (harwala).
شوط (shawt): One lap from Safa to Marwah or from Marwah to Safa. Seven complete shawts make up the sa'i.

Key Terms from Source Passage

Checkpoint
According to the Hanafi school, what is the ruling of sa'i between Safa and Marwah?
A) It is fard (pillar) and Hajj is invalid without it.
B) It is wajib (obligatory); if omitted, a sacrifice is required.
C) It is sunnah and recommended but not required.
D) It is permissible but not part of Hajj.

Key Takeaway
Sa'i between Safa and Marwah is wajib in Hajj and Umrah; its seven laps, starting at Safa and ending at Marwah, are established by Quran and Sunnah, and omitting it requires a compensatory sacrifice.

8 min
The Seven Rounds of Sa'i: Proof from Practice
Ruling with proof establishing seven rounds of sa'i

Learning Objective
By the end of this lesson, you will be able to state the precise number of rounds in sa'i and cite the three hadith proofs that establish it.

Core Idea
Sa'i between Safa and Marwah is exactly seven rounds, beginning at Safa and ending at Marwah.

The matn of Al-Quduri states the rule with clarity: the pilgrim performs seven rounds (ashwat) of sa'i. But how do we know this number is fixed? The author provides three proofs: two from the Prophet's own practice (fi'l) and one from the understanding of the early generations. This lesson unpacks each proof to show the strength of the Hanafi position on the obligatory nature of seven rounds.

Guided Path
1
Identify the ruling
Read the matn: 'This is a sa'i, so he performs seven rounds, beginning at Safa and ending at Marwah.' Note the precise number and the specified start and end points.
The number seven is not arbitrary; it is from Prophetic practice.
2
Examine the first proof (Abu Dawud)
The hadith from Abdullah ibn Abi Awfa reports that the Prophet performed sa'i seven times between Safa and Marwah before shaving his head. This is a direct observation of the Prophet's action (fi'l).
Fi'l of the Prophet, when consistently done, indicates obligation (wujub) in Hanafi usul.
3
Examine the second proof (al-Bayhaqi)
Ibn Umar's report also states seven rounds, and the verse 'Indeed you have a good example in the Messenger of Allah' is cited to emphasize following the Prophet's practice. This combines hadith with Quranic endorsement.
The Quranic verse (33:21) provides the basis for following the Prophet's actions.
4
Examine the third proof (Ata' ibn Abi Rabah)
Ata', a prominent tabi'i, ruled that if someone performs fourteen rounds, he must repeat the sa'i. This shows that exceeding seven invalidates the act, confirming that the prescribed number is exactly seven.
The ruling of a tabi'i carries weight as qawl al-sahabi in Hanafi fiqh.
5
Synthesize
All three proofs converge on one conclusion: sa'i is seven rounds. This is the established position of the Hanafi school, and the number is not subject to change.
The number seven is also agreed upon by all four schools, though the legal status (wajib vs rukn) differs.

32: This is a sa'i, so he performs seven rounds, beginning at Safa and ending at Marwah. 32 Proof: (1) Statement of the follower for establishing that this is a sa'i, so he performs seven rounds: He said: I heard Abdullah ibn Abi Awfa relating this hadith, adding: Then he came to Safa and Marwah and performed sa'i between them seven times, then shaved his head. (Abu Dawud: Book of Hajj, Chapter on the command of Safa and Marwah, no. 1903) (2) The hadith for establishing that this is a sa'i, so he performs seven rounds: Ibn Umar said: The Messenger of Allah (peace be upon him) arrived, performed tawaf around the Kaaba seven times, prayed two rak'ahs behind the Maqam, and performed sa'i between Safa and Marwah seven times. 'Indeed you have a good example in the Messenger of Allah.' (Sunan al-Bayhaqi: Bab Wujub al-Tawaf bayn al-Safa wa al-Marwah, no. 9363) (3) Statement of the follower for establishing that this is a sa'i, so he performs seven rounds: From Ata, he said: I asked about a man who performed sa'i between Safa and Marwah fourteen times. He said: 'He repeats.' (Musannaf Ibn Abi Shaybah: Fi al-rajul yas'a bayn al-Safa wa al-Marwah arba'ata ashar marrah, no. 15378)
Source pages p. 247

Commentary
This passage is a ruling with proof from the Prophet's practice. The matn (core text) states that the sa'i (ritual walking) between Safa and Marwah consists of exactly seven rounds, beginning at Safa and ending at Marwah. The author then provides three proofs (wajh). The first proof is a hadith from Abdullah ibn Abi Awfa, transmitted by Abu Dawud, showing that the Prophet performed sa'i seven times. The second proof is from Ibn Umar, recorded by al-Bayhaqi, emphasizing that the Prophet's example is to be followed. The third proof comes from a saying of Ata, the eminent tabi'i, who ruled that if someone does fourteen rounds, he must repeat the sa'i, indicating that any excess invalidates the act. These proofs collectively establish the number and sequence of sa'i as seven rounds, no less and no more. In the Hanafi school, sa'i is a wajib (obligatory) act of Hajj and Umrah, and these hadiths strongly support its fixed nature.

Key Terms
شَوْط (shawt): One round of sa'i between Safa and Marwah; the entire sa'i consists of seven ashwat.
سَعْي (sa'y): The ritual walking between Safa and Marwah during Hajj or Umrah.

Key Terms from Source Passage

Checkpoint
According to the third proof (from Ata'), what happens if a man performs sa'i fourteen times?
A) It is accepted because he doubled the rounds.
B) He must repeat the sa'i.
C) He must sacrifice an animal.
D) He must offer extra prayers.

Key Takeaway
Sa'i between Safa and Marwah is wajib and must be performed exactly seven rounds, beginning at Safa and ending at Marwah, as established by Prophetic practice and the understanding of the early generations.

Voluntary Tawaf in Makkah: Ruling and Encouragement
Ruling on voluntary tawaf and its prayer

Learning Objective
By the end of this lesson, you will be able to state the ruling on voluntary tawaf and the post-tawaf prayer, and explain the hadith evidence from the source.

Core Idea
Voluntary tawaf is sunnah; each seven rounds require two rak'ahs.

After completing sa'i, the pilgrim stays in Makkah in ihram. This lesson clarifies what acts are recommended during this period. The matn instructs performing tawaf whenever one wishes and praying two rak'ahs after each complete seven rounds. We will examine the three proofs cited from the Sunnah to understand the basis and reward of this practice.

Guided Path
1
Identify the act and its ruling
The matn instructs the pilgrim to stay in Makkah in ihram and perform tawaf whenever he wishes, and for every seven rounds (usbu') to pray two rak'ahs. This tawaf is voluntary (tatawwu'), not obligatory. Its ruling is sunnah mu'akkadah.
The prayer after tawaf is also sunnah, based on the Prophet's practice.
2
Recognize the first proof: Tawaf likened to prayer
The first hadith (from Tawus) states: 'Tawaf around the Kaaba is prayer, so speak little.' This analogy elevates tawaf's status and implies reverence, though speech is not prohibited.
This hadith is from Sunan al-Nasa'i; its chain is strong but ahad.
3
Analyze the second proof: Permissibility of good speech
The second hadith (from Ibn Abbas) adds: 'Tawaf is like prayer, except that you speak in it, so speak only good.' This clarifies that speech is allowed but restricted to good, reinforcing the sanctity of the act.
This hadith is from Tirmidhi; it qualifies the first hadith.
4
Understand the third proof: Reward for frequent tawaf
The third hadith (from Ibn Abbas) promises that fifty tawafs wipe away sins like the day of birth. This encourages repetition and shows the immense reward of voluntary tawaf.
The number fifty may be literal or symbolic; the key is encouragement.

Source Text
⚠ Extracted via Advanced OCR ∼97% accuracy, minor errors may remain — always verify against original Arabic books
٣٣ ثُمَّ يُقِيمُ بِمَكَّةَ حَرَامًا يَطُوفُ بِالْبَيْتِ كُلَّمَا بَدَا لَهُ وَيُصَلِّي لِكُلِّ أَسْبُوعِ رَكْعَتَيْنِ
٣٣ وجه : (۱) الحديث لثبوت ثُمَّ يُقِيمُ بِمَكَّةَ حَرَامًا يَطُوفُ بِالْبَيْتِ \ عَنْ طَاوُسٍ، عَنْ رَجُلٍ أَدْرَكَ النَّبِيَّ صلى الله عليه وسلم قَالَ: «الطَّوَافُ بِالْبَيْتِ صَلَاةٌ فَأَقِلُوا مِنَ الْكَلَامِ» (سنن النسائي: التَّكْبِيرُ فِي نَوَاحِي الْكَعْبَةِ، نمبر: 2923)
وجه: (٢) الحديث لثبوت ثُمَّ يُقِيمُ بِمَكَّةَ حَرَامًا يَطُوفُ بِالْبَيْتِ أَعَنْ ابْنِ عَبَّاسٍ، أَنَّ النَّبِيَّ صَلَّى اللهُ عَلَيْهِ وَسَلَّمَ قَالَ: «الطَّوَافُ حَوْلَ البَيْتِ مِثْلُ الصَّلَاةِ، إِلَّا أَنَّكُمْ تَتَكَلَّمُونَ فِيهِ، فَمَنْ تَكَلَّمَ فِيهِ فَلَا يَتَكَلَّمَنَّ إِلَّا بِخَيْرٍ» (الترمذي : بَابُ مَا جَاءَ فِي الكَلَامِ فِي الطَّوَافِ، نمبر: 960)
وجه (۳) الحديث لثبوت ثُمَّ يُقِيمُ بِمَكَّةَ حَرَامًا يَطُوفُ بِالْبَيْتِ عَنْ ابْنِ عَبَّاسِ قَالَ: قَالَ رَسُولُ اللَّهِ صَلَّى اللَّهُ عَلَيْهِ وَسَلَّمَ: «مَنْ طَافَ بِالْبَيْتِ خَمْسِينَ مَرَّةً خَرَجَ مِنْ ذُنُوبِهِ كَيَوْمِ وَلَدَتْهُ أُمُّهُ» (الترمذي: بَابُ مَا جَاءَ فِي الكَلَامِ فِي الطَّوَافِ، نمبر: 866)
33: Then he stays in Makkah in ihram, performing tawaf around the Kaaba whenever he wishes, and praying two rak'ahs for each seven rounds. 33 Proof: (1) The hadith for establishing 'then he stays in Makkah in ihram, performing tawaf around the Kaaba': From Tawus, from a man who met the Prophet (peace be upon him) who said: 'Tawaf around the Kaaba is prayer, so speak little.' (Sunan al-Nasa'i: no. 2923) (2) The hadith for establishing 'then he stays in Makkah in ihram, performing tawaf around the Kaaba': From Ibn Abbas, that the Prophet (peace be upon him) said: 'Tawaf around the Kaaba is like prayer, except that you speak in it. So whoever speaks in it, let him speak only good.' (Tirmidhi: no. 960) (3) The hadith for establishing 'then he stays in Makkah in ihram, performing tawaf around the Kaaba': From Ibn Abbas, said: The Messenger of Allah (peace be upon him) said: 'Whoever performs tawaf around the Kaaba fifty times will emerge from his sins like the day his mother bore him.' (Tirmidhi: no. 866)
Source pages p. 247

Commentary
This passage is a ruling on the pilgrim's actions after completing sa'i. The matn instructs that the pilgrim stays in Makkah in a state of ihram, performing tawaf (circumambulation) of the Kaaba whenever he wishes, and for every seven rounds of tawaf, he prays two rak'ahs. This tawaf is known as tawaf al-qudum or tawaf al-tatawwu' (voluntary tawaf). Three proofs are provided. First, a hadith from Tawus likens tawaf to prayer, implying reverence and minimizing speech. Second, a hadith from Ibn Abbas explicitly states tawaf is like prayer except speech is permitted, but only good speech. Third, another hadith from Ibn Abbas promises forgiveness for fifty tawafs. These hadiths encourage voluntary tawaf and establish its supererogatory nature. In the Hanafi school, this tawaf is sunnah (recommended). The prayer of two rak'ahs after each tawaf is also sunnah, based on the Prophet's practice.

Key Terms
طواف (tawaf): Circumambulation of the Kaaba; here voluntary tawaf performed during stay in Makkah.
أسبوع (usbu'): Seven rounds of tawaf; the unit of tawaf.

Key Terms from Source Passage

D) Four rak'ahs after complete tawaf

Key Takeaway
Voluntary tawaf during the stay in Makkah is a highly recommended sunnah, performed whenever one wishes, and each seven rounds should be followed by two rak'ahs.

Imam's Khutbah Before the Day of Tarwiyah: Ruling and Proof
Ruling on the imam's pre-Tarwiyah khutbah teaching Hajj rites

Learning Objective
By the end of this lesson, you will be able to state the ruling on the imam's khutbah before Tarwiyah (sunnah) and cite the hadith evidence from Ibn Umar that establishes it.

Core Idea
The imam's khutbah before Tarwiyah is sunnah, teaching pilgrims the rites — rooted in the Prophet's practice.

Hajj is a journey of devotion, and the imam plays a key role in guiding pilgrims. This lesson addresses the recommended khutbah delivered on the day before Yawm al-Tarwiyah (the 8th of Dhul Hijjah). In this sermon, the imam teaches the key rites: departure to Mina, standing at Arafat, and the ifadah. The Hanafi school rules this khutbah as sunnah, not wajib, based on the Prophet's continuous practice.

Guided Path
1
Identify the act and its timing
Locate the act described: the imam gives a khutbah on the day before Yawm al-Tarwiyah (i.e., the 7th of Dhul Hijjah). Note the content: teaching about Mina, Arafat, and ifadah.
2
Determine the ruling from the matn
The matn uses an imperative form 'khataba' which indicates a recommended act. In Hanafi usul, al-amr without qarina of obligation yields nadb (recommendation). Confirm the hukm level from the text's context.
No explicit wajib indicator appears.
3
Locate the dalil
The matn cites a hadith from Ibn Umar: the Prophet delivered a khutbah before Tarwiyah and informed people of their rites. Identify the hadith source (Sunan al-Bayhaqi and Sunan al-Nasa'i).
The hadith is ahad, establishing zanni thubut.
4
Analyze the dalil's evidence
The Prophet's action is a continuous practice (fi'l) that implies sunnah. In Hanafi usul, fi'l al-nabi al-mutabiq li al-ibadah indicates istihbab. Note that the hadith does not contain a command, so it does not reach wajib.
5
Conclude the hukm level
Combine the matn and dalil: the Hanafi ruling is sunnah (mustahabb). This is the mufta bihi position, agreed upon within the school.
The khutbah is not a pillar of Hajj; its omission does not affect validity.

Source Text
⚠ Extracted via Advanced OCR ∼97% accuracy, minor errors may remain — always verify against original Arabic books
فَإِذَا كَانَ قَبْلَ يَوْمِ التَّرْوِيَةِ بِيَوْمٍ خَطَبَ الْإِمَامُ النَّاسَ خُطْبَةً يُعَلِّمُ النَّاسَ فِيهَا الْخُرُوجَ إِلَى مِنْى وَالْوُقُوفَ بِعَرَفَاتِ وَالْإِفَاضَةَ
۳۴ وجه : (۱) الحديث لثبوت فَإِذَا كَانَ قَبْلَ يَوْمِ التَّرْوِيَةِ بِيَوْمٍ خَطَبَ الْإِمَامُ \ عَنِ ابْنِ عُمَرَ اللهُ عَنْهُ, قَالَ : " كَانَ رَسُولُ اللهِ صَلَّى اللهُ عَلَيْهِ وَسَلَّمَ إِذَا كَانَ قَبْلَ التَّرْوِيَةِ خَطَبَ النَّاسَ . فَأَخْبَرَهُمْ بِمَنَاسِكِهِمْ " (سنن للبيهقي: بَابُ الخُطَبِ الَّتِي يُسْتَحَبُّ لِلْإِمَامِ أَنْ يَأْتِيَ بِمَا فِي الْحَجَ. أَوَّلُهَا يَوْمَ السَّابع، نمبر : 9436/ سنن النسائي : الخُطْبَةُ قَبْلَ يَوْمِ التَّرْوِيَةِ، نمبر : 2993)
When it is the day before the day of Tarwiyah, the imam delivers a khutbah to the people in which he teaches them about the departure to Mina, standing at Arafat, and the ifadah. 34 Proof: (1) The hadith for establishing 'when it is the day before the day of Tarwiyah, the imam delivers a khutbah': From Ibn Umar (may Allah be pleased with him), he said: 'The Messenger of Allah (peace be upon him), when it was the day before Tarwiyah, he delivered a khutbah to the people and informed them of their rites.' (Sunan al-Bayhaqi: Bab al-khutab allati yustahabb li'l-imam an ya'ti biha fi al-hajj... no. 9436; Sunan al-Nasa'i: al-Khutbah qabl yawm al-tarwiyah, no. 2993)
Source pages p. 248

Commentary
This passage is a ruling on the imam's role in educating pilgrims. The matn instructs that the imam gives a khutbah (sermon) on the day before the 8th of Dhul Hijjah (yawm al-tarwiyah). In this khutbah, he teaches the people about the upcoming rites: leaving for Mina, standing at Arafat, and the ifadah (the rush from Arafat to Muzdalifah and then to Mina). The proof is a hadith from Ibn Umar that the Prophet did this. In the Hanafi school, this khutbah is sunnah (recommended) for the imam, not obligatory. It serves to remind and instruct the pilgrims.

Key Terms
خُطْبَة (khutbah): A sermon delivered by the imam during Hajj to teach the rites.
يَوْم التَّرْوِيَة (yawm al-tarwiyah): The 8th of Dhul Hijjah, when pilgrims go to Mina.

Departure to Mina and Arrival at Arafat
Ruling on the pilgrim's movement from Makkah to Mina and then to Arafat

Learning Objective
By the end of this lesson, you will be able to state the Hanafi ruling on the timing of departure from Mina to Arafat and identify the proof used.

Core Idea
The pilgrim stays in Mina from Fajr of Tarwiyah until Fajr of Arafat, then proceeds to Arafat – this is sunnah based on the Prophet's practice.

This passage gives a clear timeline for the pilgrim's movement from Makkah to Mina and then to Arafat. Understanding this schedule is essential for performing Hajj according to the Sunnah. The Hanafi school considers these timings as sunnah, not obligatory, and bases them on the detailed narration of the Prophet's Hajj.

Guided Path
1
Identify the act and its ruling
What is being ruled upon? The pilgrim's movement from Makkah to Mina on Yawm al-Tarwiyah, staying in Mina, then going to Arafat after Fajr on the day of Arafat. The ruling is that this sequence is recommended (sunnah).
2
Locate the dalil
What proof does the author cite? A hadith from Jabir ibn Abdullah describing the Prophet's Hajj, recorded in Muslim and Abu Dawud.
The hadith excerpt in the text appears to describe the sa'i between Safa and Marwah, but the full narration includes the entire sequence of the Prophet's Hajj.
3
Trace the wajh al-dalalah
How does the hadith prove the ruling? The Prophet's action of staying in Mina and proceeding to Arafat after Fajr establishes the recommended practice. Following the Prophet's example makes the action sunnah.
4
Note the hukm level
The ruling is sunnah, not fard or wajib. This is because the proof is a hadith ahad (zanni al-thubut) and the action is not commanded unequivocally.
Hanafi usul: a recommendation from the Prophet yields sunnah, not obligation.
5
Evaluate the proof's strength
The hadith is ahad (zanni al-thubut) and its indication (dalala) is also zanni, as it describes an action not a command. Thus the ruling remains sunnah, not more binding.

Source Text
⚠ Extracted via Advanced OCR ∼97% accuracy, minor errors may remain — always verify against original Arabic books
فَإِذَا صَلَّى الْفَجْرَ بِمَكَّةَ يَوْمَ التَّرْوِيَةِ خَرَجَ إِلَى مِنِّي فَأَقَامَ بِمَا حَتَّى يُصَلِّيَ الْفَجْرَ مِنْ يَوْمِ عَرَفَةَ ثُمَّ يَتَوَجَّهُ إِلَى عَرَفَاتٍ فَيُقِيمُ بِمَا
۳۵ وجه : (۱) الحديث لثبوت فَإِذَا صَلَّى الْفَجْرَ بِمَكَّةَ يَوْمَ التَّرْوِيَةِ \ قَالَ: دَخَلْنَا عَلَى جَابِرِ بْنِ عَبْدِ اللهِ . . . قَالَ : مِثْلَ هَذَا ثَلَاثَ مَرَّاتٍ ثُمَّ نَزَلَ إِلَى الْمَرْوَةِ، حَتَّى إِذَا انْصَبَّتْ قَدَمَاهُ فِي بَطْنِ الْوَادِي سَعَى، حَتَّى إِذَا صَعِدَتَا مَشَى، حَتَّى أَتَى الْمَرْوَةَ، فَفَعَلَ عَلَى الْمَرْوَةِ كَمَا فَعَلَ عَلَى الصَّفَا، (مسلم: بَابُ حَجَّةِ النَّبِيِّ صَلَّى اللهُ عَلَيْهِ وَسَلَّمَ، نمبر: 1218/ أبو داؤد: بَابُ صِفَةِ حَجَّةِ النَّبِيِّ صَلَّى اللهُ عَلَيْهِ وَسَلَّمَ، غبر : 1905)
When he prays Fajr in Makkah on the day of Tarwiyah, he goes out to Mina and stays there until he prays Fajr on the day of Arafat, then he heads to Arafat and stays there. 35 Proof: (1) The hadith for establishing 'when he prays Fajr in Makkah on the day of Tarwiyah': He said: We entered upon Jabir ibn Abdullah... he said: Like this three times, then he descended to Marwah, until when his feet sank in the bottom of the valley, he ran, until when they ascended, he walked, until he came to Marwah, and he did on Marwah as he did on Safa. (Muslim: Bab Hajjat al-Nabi, no. 1218; Abu Dawud: Bab Sifat Hajjat al-Nabi, no. 1905)
Source pages p. 248

Commentary
This passage is a ruling on the timeline of the pilgrim's movements. The matn specifies that after praying Fajr on the 8th of Dhul Hijjah (yawm al-tarwiyah) in Makkah, the pilgrim goes to Mina, stays there until Fajr of the 9th (yawm Arafat), then proceeds to Arafat and stays there until the afternoon. The proof provided is a hadith from Jabir, which in the full narration details the Prophet's Hajj; however, the excerpt given focuses on the sa'i part, possibly because the original context includes the entire sequence. In the Hanafi school, this schedule is sunnah (recommended) based on the Prophet's practice. The stay in Mina is a sunnah, and the timing of departure to Arafat after Fajr is also sunnah.

Key Terms
مِنَى (Mina): A valley near Makkah where pilgrims stay on the 8th, 11th, 12th, and 13th of Dhul Hijjah.
عَرَفَة (Arafah): The plain of Arafat where pilgrims stand on the 9th of Dhul Hijjah.

Combined Prayer at Arafat with Two Khutbahs
Ruling with proof on the combined prayer at Arafat

Learning Objective
By the end of this lesson, you will be able to state the Hanafi ruling for the combined Zuhr and Asr prayer at Arafat and describe the procedure and its proof from the Sunnah.

Core Idea
On Arafah, the imam combines Zuhr and Asr with one adhan, two iqamahs, and two khutbahs.

This lesson presents the sunnah procedure for the combined prayer at Arafat as established by the Prophet's practice. Understanding this ruling helps you appreciate the unique rituals of Hajj and distinguish between what is obligatory and what is recommended.

Guided Path
1
Identify the act and its ruling
The matn describes a specific prayer procedure on the day of Arafat: the imam leads Zuhr and Asr combined. Recognize that this is a sunnah (recommended) practice, not obligatory.
The Hanafi school classifies this as sunnah mu'akkadah for the imam.
2
Describe the procedure
Note the sequence: after the sun's decline (zawal), the imam delivers two khutbahs teaching pilgrims about the rites, then prays Zuhr and Asr with one adhan and two iqamahs.
The two iqamahs correspond to each prayer, but only one adhan is given.
3
Locate the proofs
The text cites two hadith: the long hadith of Jabir (Muslim) and the hadith of Ibn Umar (Abu Dawud). Both confirm the Prophet's action at Arafat.
These are ahad hadith, providing zanni evidence, but sufficient for a sunnah ruling.
4
Trace the basis of the ruling
The Prophet's action (fi'l) establishes the practice. In Hanafi usul, the Prophet's action generally indicates recommendation (sunnah) unless there is evidence of obligation.
The hadiths also show the location (Namirah) and the timing (after zawal).
5
Note the hukm level and significance
The combination is specific to Arafat and is a distinctive sunnah of the day. Pilgrims follow the imam and should not combine prayers individually.
This practice is mutually agreed upon (muttafaq alayh) among the schools.

Source Text
⚠ Extracted via Advanced OCR ∼97% accuracy, minor errors may remain — always verify against original Arabic books
فَإِذَا زَالَتْ الشَّمْسُ مِنْ يَوْمِ عَرَفَةَ صَلَّى الْإِمَامُ بِالنَّاسِ الظُّهْرَ وَالْعَصْرَ بِأَذَانٍ وَاحِدٍ وَإِقَامَتَيْنِ يَبْتَدِئُ فَيَخْطُبُ خُطْبَتَيْنِ يُعَلِّمُ النَّاسَ فِيهِمَا الصَّلَاةَ وَالْوُقُوفَ بِعَرَفَةَ وَالْمُزْدَلِفَةِ وَرَمْيَ الْجِمَارِ وَالتَّحَلُّلَ
وجه : (1) الحديث لثبوت فَإِذَا زَالَتْ الشَّمْسُ مِنْ يَوْمِ عَرَفَةَ صَلَّى الإِمَامُ بِالنَّاسِ \ دَخَلْنَا عَلَى جَابِرِ بْنِ عَبْدِ اللهِ، فَسَأَلَ عَنِ الْقَوْمِ حَتَّى انْتَهَى إِلَيَّ .... حَتَّى أَتَى عَرَفَةَ، فَوَجَدَ الْقُبَّةَ قَدْ ضُرِبَتْ لَهُ بِنَمِرَةَ، فَنَزَلَ بِمَا حَتَّى إِذَا زَاغَتِ الشَّمْسُ أَمَرَ بِالْقَصْوَاءِ، فَرُحِلَتْ لَهُ، فَأَتَى بَطْنَ الْوَادِي، فَخَطَبَ النَّاسَ وَقَالَ: «إِنَّ دِمَاءَكُمْ وَأَمْوَالَكُمْ حَرَامٌ عَلَيْكُمْ، (مسلم): بَابُ حَجَّةِ النَّبِيِّ صَلَّى اللَّهُ عَلَيْهِ وَسَلَّمَ، نمبر: 1218/ أبو داؤد: بَابُ صِفَةِ حَجَّةِ النَّبِيِّ صَلَّى اللَّهُ عَلَيْهِ وَسَلَّمَ، نمبر: 1905)
وجه (۲) الحديث لثبوت فَإِذَا زَالَتْ الشَّمْسُ مِنْ يَوْمِ عَرَفَةَ صَلَّى الْإِمَامُ بِالنَّاسِ \ عَنِ ابْنِ عُمَرَ، قَالَ: «غَدَا رَسُولُ اللَّهِ صَلَّى اللهُ عَلَيْهِ وَسَلَّمَ مِنْ مِنّى حِينَ صَلَّى الصُّبْحَ صَبِيحَةَ يَوْمِ عَرَفَةَ حَتَّى أَتَى عَرَفَةَ فَنَزَلَ بِنَمِرَةَ، وَهِيَ مَنْزِلُ الْإِمَامِ (أبو داؤد: بَابُ الْخُرُوجِ إِلَى عَرَفَةَ، نمبر: 1913)
اصول: یوم الترویہ : آٹھویں ذی الحجہ کو کہتے ہیں، یوم العرفہ ، نو، اور یوم النحر دس ذی الحجہ کو کہتے ہیں۔
When the sun declines on the day of Arafat, the imam leads the people in Zuhr and Asr with one adhan and two iqamahs. He begins by delivering two khutbahs in which he teaches the people about prayer, standing at Arafat, Muzdalifah, stoning the jamarat, and the tahallul (shaving/trimming). Proof (1): The hadith for establishing 'when the sun declines on the day of Arafat, the imam leads the people': We entered upon Jabir ibn Abdullah... until he came to Arafat, found a tent had been set up for him at Namirah, so he dismounted there. When the sun shifted, he ordered for the Qaswa (camel) and it was saddled for him. He came to the bottom of the valley and delivered a khutbah to the people saying: 'Your blood and your property are sacred to you...' (Muslim: Bab Hajjat al-Nabi, no. 1218; Abu Dawud: Bab Sifat Hajjat al-Nabi, no. 1905) Proof (2): The hadith for establishing 'when the sun declines on the day of Arafat, the imam leads the people': From Ibn Umar, he said: 'The Messenger of Allah (peace be upon him) set out from Mina after praying Fajr on the morning of the day of Arafat until he came to Arafat and dismounted at Namirah, which is the imam's lodging.' (Abu Dawud: Bab al-Khuruj ila Arafat, no. 1913) Principles: Yawm al-Tarwiyah is the 8th of Dhul Hijjah, Yawm al-Arafah is the 9th, and Yawm al-Nahr is the 10th.
Source pages p. 248

Commentary
This passage is a ruling on the combined prayer at Arafat. The matn states that after the sun declines (zawal) on the 9th of Dhul Hijjah, the imam leads the pilgrims in Zuhr and Asr prayers combined, with one adhan and two iqamahs. Before the prayer, he delivers two khutbahs teaching about prayer, standing at Arafat, Muzdalifah, stoning the jamarat, and the tahallul (final desacralization). Two proofs are provided: the long hadith of Jabir detailing the Prophet's Hajj, and the hadith of Ibn Umar showing the Prophet's stop at Namirah. The appended note clarifies the names of the days. In the Hanafi school, this combination and the khutbahs are sunnah (recommended) for the imam. The combination is specific to Arafat; the prayer is offered in the time of Zuhr with the intention of joining both prayers (jam' taqdim).

Key Terms
جَمْعُ تَقْدِيم (jam' taqdim): Combining Zuhr and Asr in the time of Zuhr at Arafat.
خُطْبَتَان (khutbatan): Two sermons delivered by the imam before the combined prayer at Arafat.

Key Terms from Source Passage

Checkpoint
How many adhans and iqamahs are used for the combined prayer at Arafat?
A) One adhan and one iqamah
B) One adhan and two iqamahs
C) Two adhans and two iqamahs
D) One adhan and no iqamah

Key Takeaway
The combined prayer at Arafat with two khutbahs is a confirmed sunnah derived from the Prophet's practice.

Combining Prayers for the Lone Pilgrim at Arafat
Intra-Hanafi dispute on combining prayers for lone pilgrim at Arafat

Learning Objective
By the end of this lesson, you will be able to state the intra-Hanafi dispute on combining prayers for a lone pilgrim at Arafat and identify the Quranic proof cited by Abu Hanifa.

Core Idea
A lone pilgrim at Arafat: Abu Hanifa says pray each in its time; Sahibayn allow combining.

This passage from al-Quduri presents an intra-Hanafi disagreement about the prayer of a pilgrim who prays alone at his camp at Arafat. While the imam of the congregation combines prayers at Arafat and Muzdalifah, what about the individual? The text gives the views of Abu Hanifa and his two disciples, along with a Quranic proof that underpins Abu Hanifa's position.

Guided Path
1
Identify the act and context
The act is the prayer of a pilgrim at Arafat who prays alone in his camp (rahlahu), not with the imam. The question is whether he may combine two prayers (Zuhr and Asr, or Maghrib and Isha) or must pray each in its own time.
The context is Hajj, specifically the time at Arafat.
2
State Abu Hanifa's ruling
Abu Hanifa holds that the lone pilgrim must pray each prayer in its own time. He does not have the excuse of staying with the imam, so combining is not permitted.
This is the stricter position.
3
State the Sahibayn's ruling
Abu Yusuf and Muhammad hold that the lone pilgrim may combine the prayers, analogizing to the congregation's practice under the imam.
This is the more lenient position and the mufta bihi.
4
Analyze the Quranic proof
Abu Hanifa cites Q4:103: 'Indeed, prayer has been upon the believers a timed prescription.' The word 'mawqutan' indicates fixed timings, so combining without a valid excuse violates this prescription.
The Sahibayn do not have a direct proof text cited here; they rely on analogy.
5
Understand the mufta bihi
Later Hanafi authorities prefer the Sahibayn's view because it is easier and follows the general practice of the Prophet at Arafat. The operative ruling for fatwa is that the lone pilgrim may combine.
This is an example of intra-madhhab tarjih.

Source Text
⚠ Extracted via Advanced OCR ∼97% accuracy, minor errors may remain — always verify against original Arabic books
وَمَنْ صَلَّى فِي رَحْلِهِ وَحْدَهُ صَلَّى كُلَّ وَاحِدَةٍ مِنْهُمَا فِي وَقْتِهَا عِنْدَ أَبِي حَنِيفَةَ وَقَالَ أَبُو يُوسُفَ وَمُحَمَّدٌ يَجْمَعُ بَيْنَهُمَا الْمُنْفَرِدُ ﴿إِنَّ الصَّلَوةَ كَانَتْ عَلَى الْمُؤْمِنِينَ كِتَبًا مَّوْقُوتَا﴾
And whoever prays in his camp alone, he prays each of them in its time according to Abu Hanifa. And Abu Yusuf and Muhammad said: the lone one combines them. Indeed, prayer has been upon the believers a timed prescription.
Source pages p. 249

Commentary
This passage presents an intra-Hanafi dispute. The matn states the ruling: if a pilgrim prays alone at his camp (not with the imam) at Arafat, Abu Hanifa holds that he must pray each of the two prayers (Zuhr and Asr, or Maghrib and Isha) in their own prescribed times, not combining them. The two disciples (Abu Yusuf and Muhammad) hold that the lone individual may combine them, just as the congregation does under the imam. The proof provided for Abu Hanifa's position is the Quranic verse: 'Indeed, prayer has been upon the believers a timed prescription' (4:103), indicating that each prayer has a fixed time that cannot be violated by combining without a valid excuse. The Sahibayn rely on the general practice of the Prophet at Arafat, though that is not cited here. The mufta bihi position in the later Hanafi school is the view of the Sahibayn, that the lone pilgrim may combine, as it is easier and in accordance with the Sunna of the Prophet. However, the text only gives Abu Hanifa's proof.

Key Terms
رَحْلِهِ (rahlahu): His camp or dwelling place during Hajj.
يَجْمَعُ بَيْنَهُمَا (yajma'u baynahuma): He combines two prayers (Zuhr and Asr, or Maghrib and Isha) at one time.

Key Terms from Source Passage

Checkpoint
According to Abu Hanifa, what must a pilgrim who prays alone at his camp at Arafat do?
A) Combine Zuhr and Asr together.
B) Pray each prayer in its own time.
C) Follow the imam's prayer even if alone.
D) Skip the prayer until Muzdalifah.

Key Takeaway
The lone pilgrim at Arafat may combine prayers according to the mufta bihi (Sahibayn's view), while Abu Hanifa's view requires separate prayers based on Quranic timing.

The Valid Standing Area at Arafat
Defines the valid area for standing at Arafat, excluding Batn 'Urana, with hadith proof

Learning Objective
By the end of this lesson, you will be able to state the valid area for standing (wuquf) at Arafat according to the Hanafi school and identify the dalil for the exception of Batn 'Urana.

Core Idea
All of Arafat is valid for wuquf — except Batn 'Urana, which is excluded by consensus.

One of the essential acts (arkan) of Hajj is the standing (wuquf) at Arafat on the 9th of Dhul-Hijjah. However, not every spot in the vicinity of Arafat qualifies. This lesson examines a concise ruling from al-Quduri: the entire Arafat is a standing place except a specific valley called Batn 'Urana. We will see the textual proof from the Prophet (peace be upon him) that establishes this boundary.

Guided Path
1
Identify the act and its ruling
The act is the standing (wuquf) at Arafat, which is a rukn of Hajj. The ruling states that the entire area of Arafat is a valid standing place except Batn 'Urana.
Batn 'Urana is a valley between Arafat and Muzdalifah.
2
Locate the dalil
The author cites a hadith from Ali ibn Abi Talib: the Prophet stood at Arafat and said, 'This is Arafat, and it is the standing place, and all of Arafat is a standing place.'
The hadith is narrated by Tirmidhi.
3
Trace the wajh al-dalalah
The explicit phrase 'all of Arafat is a standing place' indicates generality. The exception of Batn 'Urana is established through other narrations and consensus.
Scholars agree that Batn 'Urana is not part of Arafat.
4
Note the ikhtilaf
There is no significant disagreement among the schools on this point; all agree on the exclusion of Batn 'Urana.
The position is muttafaq alayh (agreed upon).

Source Text
⚠ Extracted via Advanced OCR ∼97% accuracy, minor errors may remain — always verify against original Arabic books
ثُمَّ يَتَوَجَّهُ إِلَى الْمَوْقِفِ فَيَقِفُ بِقُرْبِ الْجَبَلِ وَعَرَفَاتٌ كُلُّهَا مَوْقِفٌ إِلَّا بَطْنَ عُرَنَةَ عَنْ عَلِيِّ بْنِ أَبِي طَالِبٍ قَالَ: وَقَفَ رَسُولُ اللَّهِ صَلَّى اللهُ عَلَيْهِ وَسَلَّمَ بِعَرَفَةَ، فَقَالَ: «هَذِهِ عَرَفَةُ، وَهُوَ الْمَوْقِفُ، وَعَرَفَةً كُلُّهَا مَوْقِفٌ» ، ثُمَّ أَفَاضَ حِينَ غَرَبَتِ الشَّمْسُ
Then he heads to the standing place and stands near the mountain, and all of Arafat is a standing place except Batn 'Urana. From Ali ibn Abi Talib, he said: The Messenger of Allah stood at Arafat and said: 'This is Arafat, and it is the standing place, and all of Arafat is a standing place.' Then he departed when the sun set.
Source pages p. 249

Commentary
This passage gives a ruling about the valid area for the wuquf (standing) at Arafat. After the sun passes zenith on the 9th of Dhul Hijjah, the pilgrim should proceed to the standing place (mawqif) and stand near the mountain (Jabal al-Rahmah). However, the entire plain of Arafat is valid for standing, except the valley of 'Urana (Batn 'Urana), which lies between Arafat and Muzdalifah. The proof is a hadith from Ali ibn Abi Talib that the Prophet stood at Arafat and declared the entire area a standing place, then departed at sunset. This hadith establishes that standing anywhere in Arafat is sufficient, except 'Urana, which is not part of Arafat. Standing in 'Urana does not fulfill the obligation.

Key Terms
مَوْقِف (mawqif): The specific place at Arafat where pilgrims stand on the 9th of Dhul Hijjah.
بَطْنَ عُرَنَةَ (batna 'uranah): A valley near Arafat that is not part of Arafat; standing there does not count.

Key Terms from Source Passage

Checkpoint
Which part of Arafat is not valid for standing on the Day of Arafat?
A) Near the mountain.
B) Batn 'Urana.
C) The entire plain.
D) The area close to Muzdalifah.

Key Takeaway
For wuquf at Arafat to be valid, the pilgrim must stand anywhere within the boundaries of Arafat, excluding Batn 'Urana.

Imam's Sunnah Actions at Arafat
Ruling with proof on imam's sunnah at Arafat

Learning Objective
By the end of this lesson, you will be able to state the three sunnah actions of the imam at Arafat and cite the hadith proof for standing on a mount.

Core Idea
Standing on a mount at Arafat is a confirmed sunnah for the imam, not an obligation.

During the great standing at Arafat, the imam (leader of Hajj) has a special role: he should stand on his riding animal, supplicate, and teach the people the rites. This lesson unpacks these recommended actions and their scriptural basis from the hadith of Umm al-Fadl.

Guided Path
1
Identify the recommended actions
Read the passage and list the three things the imam should do while standing at Arafat.
The actions are: standing on a mount, supplication, teaching the rites.
2
Locate the proof
Find the hadith cited in the passage. Note its source (Umm al-Fadl) and what it explicitly shows the Prophet doing.
The hadith shows the Prophet standing on his camel at Arafat when he drank milk.
3
Determine the hukm level
Analyse whether these actions are fard, wajib, sunnah, or mubah. Use the Hanafi classification: the Prophet's action used as evidence indicates recommended (sunnah muakkadah).
It is sunnah muakkadah, not obligatory. The imam may also stand on the ground if needed.

Source Text
⚠ Extracted via Advanced OCR ∼97% accuracy, minor errors may remain — always verify against original Arabic books
وَيَنْبَغِي لِلْإِمَامِ أَنْ يَقِفَ بِعَرَفَةَ عَلَى رَاحِلَتِهِ وَيَدْعُو وَيُعَلِّمُ النَّاسَ الْمَنَاسِكَ عَنْ أُمِّ الفَضْلِ بِنْتِ الْحَارِثِ، أَنَّ نَاسًا اخْتَلَفُوا عِنْدَهَا يَوْمَ عَرَفَةَ فِي صَوْمِ النَّبِيِّ صَلَّى اللهُ عَلَيْهِ وَسَلَّمَ فَقَالَ بَعْضُهُمْ: هُوَ صَائِمٌ، وَقَالَ بَعْضُهُمْ لَيْسَ بِصَائِمٍ، فَأَرْسَلْتُ إِلَيْهِ بِقَدَحٍ لَبَنِ وَهُوَ وَاقِفٌ عَلَى بَعِيرِهِ، فَشَرِبَهُ
And it is befitting for the imam to stand at Arafat on his mount, supplicate, and teach the people the rites. From Umm al-Fadl bint al-Harith: People disputed before her on the Day of Arafat about the Prophet's fasting; some said he was fasting, others said he was not. She sent him a cup of milk while he was standing on his camel, and he drank it.
Source pages p. 249

Commentary
This passage outlines the sunnah actions for the imam (leader of Hajj) during the standing at Arafat. The imam should stand on his riding animal, engage in supplication, and instruct the people in the rituals of Hajj. The hadith of Umm al-Fadl is cited as proof that the Prophet stood on his camel at Arafat, as she sent him milk and he drank while mounted. This indicates that it is recommended (mustahabb) for the imam to stand on a mount, as the Prophet did. The teaching aspect is derived from other ahadith where the Prophet taught the Companions. The imam's role is to guide and educate.

Key Terms
رَاحِلَتِهِ (raahilatihi): His riding animal (camel, horse, etc.)
يُعَلِّمُ النَّاسَ الْمَنَاسِكَ (yu'allimu al-nasa al-manasika): He teaches the people the rituals of Hajj (what to do and when).

Key Terms from Source Passage

Checkpoint
What is recommended for the imam during his standing at Arafat?
A) Fast on the Day of Arafat.
B) Stand on his mount and teach the people.
C) Stay silent and not supplicate.
D) Remain on foot to be humble.

Key Takeaway
The imam's sunnah at Arafat includes standing on a mount, supplicating, and teaching—actions derived from the Prophet's practice and aimed at guiding the pilgrims.

Recommended Acts Before Departing to Muzdalifah
Lists recommended acts before departing to Muzdalifah

Learning Objective
By the end of this lesson, you will be able to state the recommended acts (mustahabbat) before departing Arafat to Muzdalifah and identify the Quranic evidence for the departure.

Core Idea
Ghusl, intense dua, departure after sunset, and camping near Quzah are recommended but not obligatory.

On the Day of Arafat, the pilgrim engages in several supererogatory acts before the evening departure to Muzdalifah. The classical Hanafi text outlines these mustahabbat to enhance the spiritual experience. This lesson walks through each recommended act and the supporting dalil.

Guided Path
1
List the recommended acts
Identify the four mustahabbat mentioned: ghusl before standing, intense supplication, departure after sunset, and descending near the mountain Quzah.
2
Identify the hukm level
All acts are mustahabb (sunnah muakkadah). Omission does not invalidate the hajj nor require compensation.
The text uses 'yustahabb' indicating recommendation.
3
Locate the Quranic proof
The verse 2:198 commands remembrance at Muzdalifah after departing Arafat, supporting the departure after sunset.
The verse is cited as proof for the departure, not for the other acts.
4
Understand the time and manner of departure
Departure occurs after sunset; the imam and people move calmly ('ala hay'atihim) to Muzdalifah.
Calmness is recommended, not haste.
5
Note the recommended camping site
Upon reaching Muzdalifah, it is recommended to camp near the mountain with the milestone (al-maqidah) called Quzah.
This is the site of the Mash'ar al-Haram.

Source Text
⚠ Extracted via Advanced OCR ∼97% accuracy, minor errors may remain — always verify against original Arabic books
وَيُسْتَحَبُّ لَهُ أَنْ يَغْتَسِلَ قَبْلَ الْوُقُوفِ وَيَجْتَهِدُ فِي الدُّعَاءِ فَإِذَا غَرَبَتْ الشَّمْسُ أَفَاضَ الْإِمَامُ وَالنَّاسُ مَعَهُ عَلَى هَيْئَتِهِمْ حَتَّى يَأْتُوا الْمُزْدَلِفَةَ وَالْمُسْتَحَبُّ أَنْ يَنزِلُوا بِقُرْبِ الجَبَلِ الَّذِي عَلَيْهِ الْمَقِيدَةُ يُقَالُ لَهُ قُرَحُ ﴿فَإِذَا أَفَضْتُم مِّنْ عَرَفَتٍ فَاذْكُرُوا اللَّهَ عِندَ الْمَشْعَرِ الْحَرَامِ﴾
And it is recommended for him to perform ghusl before the standing, and to strive in supplication. When the sun sets, the imam and the people with him depart in their state until they come to Muzdalifah. And it is recommended that they descend near the mountain on which is the milestone called Quzah. Then when you depart from Arafat, remember Allah at the Mash'ar al-Haram.
Source pages p. 250

Commentary
This passage covers several recommended acts (mustahabbat) for the Day of Arafat and the night of Muzdalifah. Firstly, the pilgrim should perform ghusl before the wuquf (standing) at Arafat. Secondly, he should exert himself in supplication during the standing. Thirdly, after sunset on the 9th, the imam and the people should depart from Arafat to Muzdalifah while maintaining their state (calmly). Fourthly, upon reaching Muzdalifah, it is recommended to camp near the mountain called Quzah, which has a milestone. The verse cited (2:198) is a proof for departing Arafat and remembering Allah at Muzdalifah. The ghusl before standing is proven by the practice of the Prophet as narrated by Jabir (not quoted here but in the commentary).

Key Terms
الْمَقِيدَةُ (al-maqidah): A milestone or marker on a mountain at Muzdalifah.
قُرَحُ (qurah): Another name for Quzah, the mountain at Muzdalifah.

Key Terms from Source Passage

Checkpoint
What is recommended before the standing at Arafat?
A) Perform ghusl.
B) Fast.
C) Give charity.
D) Shave the head.

Key Takeaway
The recommended acts before Muzdalifah enhance the hajj; they are mustahabb, not wajib.

Imam's Combined Prayer at Muzdalifah and the Ruling on Praying Alone on the Way
States imam's combined prayer at Muzdalifah with one adhan and iqamah, and a dispute on validity of praying Maghrib on the way alone

Learning Objective
By the end of this lesson, you will be able to state the Hanafi ruling on combining Maghrib and Isha at Muzdalifah, and apply the intra-Hanafi dispute to determine the validity of praying Maghrib alone on the way.

Core Idea
Praying Maghrib alone before reaching Muzdalifah is invalid according to Abu Hanifa and Muhammad.

During Hajj, the imam leads Maghrib and Isha combined at Muzdalifah with one adhan and one iqamah, following the Prophet's practice. But what if a pilgrim prays Maghrib on the way? This lesson explores a key intra-Hanafi dispute between Abu Hanifa and Muhammad on one side and Abu Yusuf on the other regarding the validity of that prayer.

Guided Path
1
Identify the two rulings in the passage
First, the imam's action: combining Maghrib and Isha at Muzdalifah with one adhan and one iqamah. Second, the individual's action: praying Maghrib alone on the way does not suffice according to Abu Hanifa and Muhammad.
The first ruling is established practice; the second is a disputed point within the Hanafi school.
2
Understand the dalil for the imam's combining
The hadith of Ibn Umar shows the Prophet combined with one iqamah. This is the primary evidence for the imam's action.
The adhan is optional; the iqamah is sufficient.
3
Analyze the dispute on praying alone on the way
The passage states that according to Abu Hanifa and Muhammad, praying Maghrib alone on the way does not suffice (lam yujzihi). This implies a difference with Abu Yusuf, who likely considers it valid.
The full dispute is not detailed, but the mufta bihi follows Abu Hanifa and Muhammad.
4
Examine the hadith evidence for the second ruling
Usama's hadith shows the Prophet did not pray Maghrib on the way; he delayed until Muzdalifah. This supports the view that praying alone on the way is incorrect.
The hadith is incomplete in the text but the key point is the delay.
5
Determine the mufta bihi position
Later Hanafi scholars uphold the view of Abu Hanifa and Muhammad: the prayer does not suffice and must be repeated at Muzdalifah.
This is the operative ruling for fatwa.

Source Text
⚠ Extracted via Advanced OCR ∼97% accuracy, minor errors may remain — always verify against original Arabic books
وَيُصَلِّي الْإِمَامُ بِالنَّاسِ الْمَغْرِبَ وَالْعِشَاءَ بِأَذَانٍ وَإِقَامَةٍ وَاحِدَةٍ وَمَنْ صَلَّى الْمَغْرِبَ فِي الطَّرِيقِ وَحْدَهُ لَمْ يُجْزِهِ عِنْدَ أَبِي حَنِيفَةَ وَمُحَمَّدٍ عَنِ ابْنِ عُمَرَ، قَالَ: جَمَعَ رَسُولُ اللَّهِ صَلَّى اللهُ عَلَيْهِ وَسَلَّمَ بَيْنَ الْمَغْرِبِ وَالْعِشَاءِ بِجَمْعٍ، صَلَّى الْمَغْرِبَ ثَلَاثًا وَالْعِشَاءَ رَكْعَتَيْنِ بِإِقَامَةِ وَاحِدَةٍ عَنْ أُسَامَةَ بْنِ زَيْدٍ رَضِيَ اللَّهُ عَنْهُمَا، أَنَّهُ سَمِعَهُ يَقُولُ: دَفَعَ رَسُولُ اللَّهِ صَلَّى اللهُ عَلَيْهِ وَسَلَّمَ مِنْ عَرَفَةَ، فَنَزَلَ الشَّعْبَ، فَبَالَ
And the imam prays with the people Maghrib and Isha with one adhan and one iqamah. And whoever prays Maghrib on the way alone, it does not suffice him according to Abu Hanifa and Muhammad. From Ibn Umar: The Messenger of Allah combined Maghrib and Isha at Jam' (Muzdalifah), praying Maghrib three and Isha two with one iqamah. From Usama ibn Zaid: He heard him say: The Messenger of Allah departed from Arafat, then descended into the valley and urinated...
Source pages p. 250

Commentary
This passage contains two rulings. First, the imam at Muzdalifah should lead the prayers for Maghrib and Isha combined (jama') with one adhan and one iqamah. This is based on the hadith of Ibn Umar, which explicitly states the Prophet did so. Second, if someone prays Maghrib on the way (during the journey from Arafat to Muzdalifah) alone, it is not valid (la yujzi'uhu) according to Abu Hanifa and Muhammad. This implies that Abu Yusuf may differ, though the text does not state his view fully. The proof for the second ruling is from Usama's hadith, which shows the Prophet delayed Maghrib until Muzdalifah, indicating the obligation to pray with the congregation. The mufta bihi position is that of Abu Hanifa and Muhammad, that praying alone on the way is insufficient; one must pray with the imam at Muzdalifah. The hadith from Usama is incomplete here, but it continues to show that the Prophet prayed at Muzdalifah.

Key Terms
لَمْ يُجْزِهِ (lam yujzihi): It does not suffice him; the prayer is invalid and must be repeated.
بِأَذَانٍ وَإِقَامَةٍ وَاحِدَةٍ (bi-adhanin wa iqamatin wahidatin): With one adhan and one iqamah for two prayers combined.

Key Terms from Source Passage

Checkpoint
According to Abu Hanifa and Muhammad, what is the ruling for someone who prays Maghrib alone on the way to Muzdalifah?
A) It is valid and he need not repeat.
B) It is invalid and he must repeat it at Muzdalifah.
C) It is better to pray on the way.
D) He should combine it with Isha on the way.

Key Takeaway
Praying Maghrib on the way to Muzdalifah is invalid and must be repeated at Muzdalifah with the imam.

Recommended Actions at Arafat and Muzdalifah: Ghusl, Supplication, and Combined Prayer
Rulings with hadith evidence on recommended ghusl, supplication, and combined prayer.

Learning Objective
By the end of this lesson, you will be able to state the recommended actions (mustahabbat) before and after the wuquf of Arafat including ghusl and supplication, and explain the Hanafi ruling on combining Maghrib and Isha at Muzdalifah with one adhan and one iqamah, citing the supporting hadith.

Core Idea
Ghusl before Arafat is sunnah; combining Maghrib and Isha at Muzdalifah with one iqamah is the Sunnah of the Prophet.

This passage from al-Quduri presents the recommended practices for the pilgrim after leaving Arafat and arriving at Muzdalifah. It emphasizes the importance of ghusl before the standing, diligent supplication, and a specific manner of proceeding. The central legal point is the combined prayer at Muzdalifah, where the imam leads Maghrib (3 rak'ahs) and Isha (2 rak'ahs, shortened) with a single adhan and iqamah, supported by multiple hadith narrations.

Guided Path
1
Identify the act and its ruling
Determine what actions are being ruled upon and their hukm level. The passage mentions ghusl before the standing (mustahabb), striving in supplication (mustahabb), and the combined prayer (sunnah muakkadah).
The term 'yustahabbu' indicates recommendation (sunnah), not obligation.
2
Locate the dalil
Identify the specific proofs cited for each ruling. For ghusl, the verse of dhikr at the Sacred Monument and the hadith of Jabir are used. For the combined prayer, the hadith of Ibn Umar (one iqamah) and the hadith of Jabir (two iqamahs) are presented.
The commentator cites a second narration showing a variant.
3
Trace the wajh al-dalalah
Explain how the evidence proves the ruling. In Hanafi usul, the Prophet's action (fi'l) indicates istihbab (recommendation), not wujub. Thus, the combined prayer is sunnah, not wajib.
The verse is also cited as a general encouragement for dhikr at the Sacred Monument.
4
Note the ikhtilaf
Recognize the difference between the two narrations regarding the number of iqamahs. One hadith mentions one iqamah, the other mentions two. This is a point of intra-Hanafi and cross-madhhab ikhtilaf.
The Shafi'i school follows the narration with two iqamahs.
5
Evaluate the tarjih
Determine which narration is relied upon in the Hanafi school. The commentator adopts the narration of one iqamah as the mufta bihi, because it is the practice of the Prophet on his farewell Hajj as reported by Ibn Umar.
Tarjih (preference) is based on the strength of the chain and consistency with established practice.

Source Text
⚠ Extracted via Advanced OCR ∼97% accuracy, minor errors may remain — always verify against original Arabic books
كِتَابُ الْحَجّ ٢٠ وَيُسْتَحَبُّ لَهُ أَنْ يَغْتَسِلَ قَبْلَ الْوُقُوفِ وَيَجْتَهِدُ فِي الدُّعَاءِ فَإِذَا غَرَبَتْ الشَّمْسُ أَفَاضَ الْإِمَامُ وَالنَّاسُ مَعَهُ عَلَى هَيْئَتِهِمْ حَتَّى يَأْتُوا الْمُزْدَلِفَةَ وَالْمُسْتَحَبُّ أَنْ يَنزِلُوا بِقُرْبِ الجَبَلِ الَّذِي عَلَيْهِ الْمَقِيدَةُ يُقَالُ لَهُ قُرَحُ الَّ وَيُصَلِّي الْإِمَامُ بِالنَّاسِ الْمَغْرِبَ وَالْعِشَاءَ بِأَذَانٍ وَإِقَامَةٍ وَاحِدَةٍ ٢٢ وجه: (1) الآية لثبوت وَيُسْتَحَبُّ لَهُ أَنْ يَغْتَسِلَ قَبْلَ الْوُقُوفِ الْوَفَإِذَا أَفَضْتُم مِّنْ عَرَفَتٍ فَاذْكُرُوا اللَّهَ عِندَ الْمَشْعَرِ الْحَرَامِ ﴾ (سورة البقرة، 2 أيت نمبر: 198) وجه : (٢) الحديث لثبوت وَيُسْتَحَبُّ لَهُ أَنْ يَغْتَسِلَ قَبْلَ الْوُقُوفِ ادَخَلْنَا عَلَى جَابِرِ بْنِ عَبْدِ اللَّهِ، ثُمَّ رَكِبَ الْقَصْوَاءَ، حَتَّى أَتَى الْمَشْعَرَ الْحَرَامَ، فَاسْتَقْبَلَ الْقِبْلَةَ، فَدَعَاهُ وَكَبَّرَهُ وَهَلَّلَهُ وَوَحْدَهُ، فَلَمْ يَزَلْ وَاقِفًا حَتَّى أَسْفَرَ جِدًّا، فَدَفَعَ قَبْلَ أَنْ تَطْلُعَ الشَّمْسُ (مسلم: بَابُ حَجَّةِ النَّبِيِّ صَلَّى اللهُ عَلَيْهِ وَسَلَّمَ، نمبر : 1218/ أبو داؤد: بَابُ صِفَةِ حَجَّةِ النَّبِيِّ صَلَّى اللَّهُ عَلَيْهِ وَسَلَّمَ: 1905) وجه:(۳) الحديث لثبوت وَيُسْتَحَبُّ لَهُ أَنْ يَغْتَسِلَ قَبْلَ الْوُقُوفِ اعَنْ عَلِي، قَالَ: فَلَمَّا أَصْبَحَ يَعْنِي النَّبِيَّ صَلَّى اللهُ عَلَيْهِ وَسَلَّمَ وَوَقَفَ عَلَى قُزَحَ فَقَالَ: «هَذَا قُرَحْ وَهُوَ الْمَوْقِفُ، وَجَمْعٌ كُلُّهَا مَوْقِفٌ، (أبو داؤد: بَابُ الصَّلَاةِ بِجَمْعِ، نمبر: 1935) ال وجه : (۱) الحديث لثبوت وَيُصَلِّي الْإِمَامُ بِالنَّاسِ الْمَغْرِبَ وَالْعِشَاءَ اعَنِ ابْنِ عُمَرَ، قَالَ: جَمَعَ رَسُولُ اللَّهِ صَلَّى اللهُ عَلَيْهِ وَسَلَّمَ بَيْنَ الْمَغْرِبِ وَالْعِشَاءِ بِجَمْعٍ، صَلَّى الْمَغْرِبَ ثَلَاثًا وَالْعِشَاءَ رَكْعَتَيْنِ بِإِقَامَةِ وَاحِدَةٍ» (مسلم: بَابُ الْإِفَاضَةِ مِنْ عَرَفَاتِ إِلَى الْمُزْدَلِفَةِ وَاسْتِحْبَابِ صَلَاتَي الْمَغْرِبِ وَالْعِشَاءِ جَمِيعًا بِالْمُزْدَلِفَةِ فِي هَذِهِ اللَّيْلَةِ، نمبر : 1288) وجه : (۲) الحديث لثبوت وَيُصَلِّي الْإِمَامُ بِالنَّاسِ الْمَغْرِبَ وَالْعِشَاءَ احَتَّى أَتَى الْمُزْدَلِفَةَ، فَصَلَّى بِمَا الْمَغْرِبَ وَالْعِشَاءَ بِأَذَانِ وَاحِدٍ وَإِقَامَتَيْنِ، وَلَمْ يُسَبِّحْ بَيْنَهُمَا شَيْئًا (مسلم: بَابُ حَجَّةِ النَّبِيِّ صَلَّى اللهُ عَلَيْهِ وَسَلَّمَ، نمبر: 1218)
The Book of Hajj. And it is recommended for him to perform ghusl before the standing, and he should strive in supplication. When the sun sets, the imam and the people with him proceed in their state until they come to Muzdalifah. And it is recommended that they descend near the mountain upon which is the monument called Quzah. And the imam prays with the people Maghrib and Isha with one adhan and one iqamah. Evidence (1): The verse for establishing that it is recommended for him to perform ghusl before the standing: 'When you depart from Arafat, remember Allah at the Sacred Monument' (Surah al-Baqarah, 2:198). Evidence (2): The hadith for establishing that it is recommended for him to perform ghusl before the standing: We entered upon Jabir ibn Abdullah, then he rode al-Qaswa until he reached the Sacred Monument, faced the qiblah, and supplicated, saying Allahu akbar, la ilaha illallah, and remained standing until it was very bright, then departed before sunrise (Muslim: Chapter of the Prophet's Hajj, no. 1218; Abu Dawud: Chapter of the Description of the Prophet's Hajj, no. 1905). Evidence (3): The hadith for establishing that it is recommended for him to perform ghusl before the standing: From Ali, he said: When morning came, the Prophet (peace be upon him) stood at Quzah and said: 'This is Quzah, and it is the standing place, and all of Muzdalifah is a standing place' (Abu Dawud: Chapter of Prayer at Muzdalifah, no. 1935). Evidence (1): The hadith for establishing that the imam prays with the people Maghrib and Isha: From Ibn Umar, he said: The Messenger of Allah (peace be upon him) combined Maghrib and Isha at Muzdalifah, praying Maghrib as three rak'ahs and Isha as two rak'ahs with one iqamah (Muslim: Chapter of Departure from Arafat to Muzdalifah and Recommendation of Praying Maghrib and Isha Together at Muzdalifah that Night, no. 1288). Evidence (2): The hadith for establishing that the imam prays with the people Maghrib and Isha: Until he came to Muzdalifah, and he prayed at it Maghrib and Isha with one adhan and two iqamahs, and he did not pray anything between them (Muslim: Chapter of the Prophet's Hajj, no. 1218).
Source pages p. 250

Commentary
This passage is a ruling with proof, presenting the recommended actions at Arafat and Muzdalifah. The matn (base text) states that it is mustahabb to perform ghusl before the wuquf at Arafat, to strive in du'a, and when the sun sets, the imam and the people proceed in a dignified manner to Muzdalifah. The recommended place to descend is near Mount Quzah. At Muzdalifah, the imam leads Maghrib and Isha combined with one adhan and one iqamah. The commentator then provides hadith evidence: For ghusl, the verse of dhikr at the Sacred Monument is cited, along with the hadith of Jabir describing the Prophet's standing. Another hadith from Ali states that all Muzdalifah is a standing place. For the combined prayer, Ibn Umar's narration confirms praying Maghrib (3 rakahs) and Isha (2 rakahs, as traveler shortens) with one iqamah. However, a second narration mentions one adhan and two iqamahs. The Hanafi school follows the first narration (one iqamah) as the practice of the Prophet on his farewell Hajj. The ghusl and the combined prayer are sunnah muakkadah. The prayer includes qasr (shortening) for Isha because the pilgrim is a traveler.

Key Terms
الوُقُوف (al-wuquf): The standing at Arafat on the 9th of Dhul Hijjah; the essential pillar of Hajj.
المُزْدَلِفَة (al-Muzdalifah): A plain between Arafat and Mina where pilgrims spend the night after Arafat.
الجَمْع بَيْنَ الصَّلَاتَيْن (al-jam' bayn al-salatayn): Combining Maghrib and Isha at Muzdalifah in the time of the earlier prayer.

Key Terms from Source Passage

Checkpoint
According to the text, how does the imam lead the Maghrib and Isha prayers at Muzdalifah?
A) With one adhan and one iqamah
B) With one adhan and two iqamahs
C) With two adhans and two iqamahs
D) With no adhan or iqamah

Key Takeaway
The Prophet's practice at Muzdalifah is to combine Maghrib and Isha with one adhan and one iqamah, shortening Isha to two rak'ahs.

6 min
When Praying Maghrib Alone on the Way Does Not Suffice
Intra-Hanafi dispute on sufficiency of Maghrib prayer on way to Muzdalifah

Learning Objective
By the end of this lesson, you will be able to state the Hanafi ruling on praying Maghrib alone before reaching Muzdalifah and explain the practical difference between the positions of Abu Hanifa/Muhammad and Abu Yusuf.

Core Idea
Praying Maghrib individually on the way to Muzdalifah does not fulfill the Hajj sunnah according to the stronger Hanafi view.

During Hajj, the Prophet combined Maghrib and Isha at Muzdalifah. A pilgrim may be tempted to pray Maghrib early on the way, but the Hanafi school holds that this does not suffice. This lesson examines the intra-Hanafi dispute: why Abu Hanifa and Muhammad require repetition, while Abu Yusuf considered it valid. You will see how the evidence from the Prophet's practice and Companion rulings supports the relied-upon position.

Guided Path
1
State the Hanafi majority position
Identify the ruling of Abu Hanifa and Muhammad: praying Maghrib alone on the way is not sufficient (lam yujzihi). The pilgrim must repeat it at Muzdalifah.
This is the mufta bihi position.
2
Identify the dissenting view
Abu Yusuf held that the prayer is valid and no repetition is needed. His reasoning likely relies on the general permissibility of praying on time.
Abu Yusuf's evidence is not detailed in the text but is inferred.
3
Analyse the Hanafi response
The majority supported their view with the hadith of Usamah, the practice of Ibn Mas'ud, and the statement of Ibn al-Zubayr. These show that the Prophet and Companions deliberately delayed Maghrib until Muzdalifah.
The evidence is from sahih hadith and qawl al-sahabi.
4
Determine the thamarah al-khilaf
The practical consequence: if a pilgrim prays on the way, according to the majority he must repeat it at Muzdalifah; according to Abu Yusuf he does not.
This affects the pilgrim's obligation after arriving at Muzdalifah.
5
Apply the tarjih
The relied-upon position is that of Abu Hanifa and Muhammad, as it is based on stronger evidence from the Sunnah.
Al-Quduri and later Hanafi works adopt this view.

وَمَنْ صَلَّى الْمَغْرِبَ فِي الطَّرِيقِ وَحْدَهُ لَمْ يُجْزِهِ عِنْدَ أَبِي حَنِيفَةَ وَمُحَمَّدٍ وجه : (۱) الحديث لثبوت وَمَنْ صَلَّى الْمَغْرِبَ فِي الطَّرِيقِ \ عَنْ أُسَامَةَ بْنِ زَيْدٍ رَضِيَ اللَّهُ عَنْهُمَا، أَنَّهُ سَمِعَهُ يَقُولُ: دَفَعَ رَسُولُ اللَّهِ صَلَّى اللهُ عَلَيْهِ وَسَلَّمَ مِنْ عَرَفَةَ، فَنَزَلَ الشَّعْبَ، فَبَالَ اصول : عرفہ کے دن جب سورج غروب ہو جائے تو مزدلفہ کو روانہ ہو جائے، اولا امام چلے بعد ازاں عوام۔ وجه : (۲) قول الصحابي لثبوت وَمَنْ صَلَّى الْمَغْرِبَ فِي الطَّرِيقِ \ حَجَّ عَبْدُ اللَّهِ رَضِيَ اللَّهُ عَنْهُ، فَأَتَيْنَا الْمُزْدَلِفَةَ حِينَ الْأَذَانِ بِالعَتَمَةِ أَوْ قَرِيبًا مِنْ ذَلِكَ، فَأَمَرَ رَجُلًا فَأَذَّنَ وَأَقَامَ، ثُمَّ صَلَّى الْمَغْرِبَ، وَصَلَّى بَعْدَهَا رَكْعَتَيْنِ، ثُمَّ دَعَا بِعَشَائِهِ ،فَتَعَشَّى ثُمَّ أَمَرَ أُرَى فَأَذَّنَ وَأَقَامَ - قَالَ عَمْرُو: لَا أَعْلَمُ الشَّكَ إِلَّا مِنْ زُهَيْرٍ ثُمَّ صَلَّى العِشَاءَ رَكْعَتَيْنِ (بخاري: بَابُ مَنْ أَذَّنَ وَأَقَامَ لِكُلِّ وَاحِدَةٍ مِنْهُمَا، غمبر: 1675) وجه : (۳) قول الصحابي لثبوت وَمَنْ صَلَّى الْمَغْرِبَ فِي الطَّرِيقِ عَنْ عَبْدِ اللَّهِ بْنِ الزُّبَيْرِ رَضِيَ اللَّهُ عَنْهُ, قَالَ: مِنْ سُنَّةِ الحَجَ ... ثُمَّ يُفِيضُ فَيُصَلِّي بِالْمُزْدَلِفَةِ أَوْحَيْثُ قَضَى اللَّهُ عَزَّ وَجَلَّ ثُمَّ يَقِفُ بِجَمْعِ (سنن للبيهقي: بَابُ مَنْ قَالَ : يُصَلِّيهِمَا بِالْمُزْدَلِفَةِ أَوْحَيْثُ قَضَى اللَّه عَزَّ وَجَلَّ، 9502)
And whoever prays Maghrib on the way alone is not sufficient according to Abu Hanifa and Muhammad. Evidence (1): The hadith for establishing that whoever prays Maghrib on the way alone: From Usamah ibn Zaid, may Allah be pleased with them, that he heard him say: The Messenger of Allah (peace be upon him) departed from Arafah, then descended the valley and urinated. Principle: On the day of Arafah, when the sun sets, one should proceed to Muzdalifah, first the imam then the people. Evidence (2): The statement of the Companion for establishing that whoever prays Maghrib on the way alone: 'Abdullah (ibn Mas'ud) performed Hajj, and we came to Muzdalifah at the time of the adhan for Isha or near it. He ordered a man to call adhan and iqamah, then he prayed Maghrib, then prayed two rak'ahs after it, then called for his dinner and ate, then he ordered (someone) - I think - to call adhan and iqamah (Amr said: I do not know the doubt except from Zuhayr), then he prayed Isha as two rak'ahs (Bukhari: Chapter of who gave adhan and iqamah for each of them, no. 1675). Evidence (3): The statement of the Companion for establishing that whoever prays Maghrib on the way alone: From 'Abdullah ibn al-Zubayr, may Allah be pleased with him, he said: From the Sunnah of Hajj… then he proceeds and prays at Muzdalifah or wherever Allah decrees, then stands at Muzdalifah (Sunan al-Bayhaqi: Chapter of who said: He prays them at Muzdalifah or wherever Allah decrees, 9502).
Source pages p. 250

Commentary
This passage is an intra-Hanafi dispute. The matn states that according to Abu Hanifa and Muhammad, if someone prays Maghrib alone on the way to Muzdalifah (i.e., before joining the congregation), it does not suffice; he must repeat it at Muzdalifah. Abu Yusuf differed, holding it valid. The relied-upon position (mufta bihi) is that of the two imams, as it aligns with the sunnah of delaying the prayer until reaching Muzdalifah. The hadith evidence: Usamah's narration shows the Prophet descended and did not pray until Muzdalifah. The principle added (in Urdu) confirms the order: the imam leads, then the people follow. The practice of 'Abdullah ibn Mas'ud and the statement of 'Abdullah ibn al-Zubayr further support that the proper place for the Maghrib prayer is Muzdalifah or wherever the pilgrim reaches if unable, but the sunnah is to pray at Muzdalifah. Thus, praying alone on the way contradicts the sunnah and must be repeated according to the stronger Hanafi opinion.

Key Terms
لَمْ يُجْزِهِ (lam yujzihi): It does not suffice; the action does not fulfill the religious obligation and must be repeated.
الطَّرِيق (al-tariq): The path between Arafat and Muzdalifah, while still en route.

Key Terms from Source Passage

Checkpoint
According to the mufta bihi position in the Hanafi school, what is the ruling for a pilgrim who prays Maghrib alone on the way to Muzdalifah?
A) It is valid and sufficient.
B) It is not sufficient and must be repeated at Muzdalifah.
C) It is forbidden and invalid.
D) It is makruh but sufficient.

Key Takeaway
The relied-upon Hanafi position requires a pilgrim to pray Maghrib at Muzdalifah with the congregation; praying alone on the way does not suffice and must be repeated.
