Fajr Prayer and Standing at Muzdalifah
Ruling with proof on Fajr timing and standing at Muzdalifah

Learning Objective
By the end of this lesson, you will be able to state the Hanafi ruling on the timing of Fajr prayer at Muzdalifah (ghalas) and the legal status of standing at al-Mash'ar al-Haram (wajib), and distinguish it from the standing at Arafat.

Core Idea
Fajr at Muzdalifah is prayed at early dawn; standing at the Mash'ar al-Haram is a wajib act of Hajj.

In this lesson, we examine the practices of the Prophet (peace be upon him) at Muzdalifah during Hajj. The Hanafi school derives from the prophetic actions that Fajr should be offered at the earliest time after true dawn, known as ghalas, and then the pilgrim proceeds to the Sacred Monument to stand in supplication until it becomes very bright. This standing is a distinct obligatory act (wajib) of Hajj, separate from the standing at Arafat.

Guided Path
1
Identify the acts and their rulings
The passage covers two acts: the Fajr prayer at Muzdalifah and the subsequent standing at the Mash'ar al-Haram. Determine the Hanafi hukm level for each.
Fajr timing: sunnah muakkadah to pray at ghalas; standing: wajib.
2
Locate the dalil (evidence)
Two hadiths are cited: one from 'Abdullah ibn Mas'ud (Bukhari) about praying Fajr at dawn, and one from Jabir ibn 'Abdullah (Muslim) describing the Prophet's standing until isfar.
These are ahad hadiths, zanni in transmission and indication.
3
Trace the wajh al-dalalah (how proof indicates ruling)
The Prophet's action (fi'l) of standing until isfar, coupled with his statement 'the Fajr prayer is fixed at this hour', indicates the recommended timing and the obligatory nature of the standing.
Hanafi usul: the Prophet's continuous practice (fi'l) indicates wujub unless there is evidence otherwise.
4
Note the ikhtilaf (scholarly difference)
The Shafi'i school considers the standing at Muzdalifah as sunnah, not wajib, so no penalty for omission.
This is a legitimate ikhtilaf based on different usul principles.
5
Evaluate the Hanafi tarjih (preferred position)
The Hanafi mufta bihi is that standing at Muzdalifah is wajib; omission requires a dam. This is based on the strength of the prophetic practice and the Hanafi principle that continuous action implies obligation.
The tarjih is supported by the majority of Hanafi scholars and is recorded in Zahir al-Riwayah.

Source Text
⚠ Extracted via Advanced OCR ∼97% accuracy, minor errors may remain — always verify against original Arabic books
فاذا طلع الفجرصلى الامام بالناس الفجر بغلس ٢٤ ثُمَّ وَقَفَ وَوَقَفَ النَّاسُ مَعَهُ وجه : (۱) الحديث لثبوت فاذا طلع الفجرصلى الامام بالناس الفجر بغلس \ قَالَ: خَرَجْنَا مَعَ عَبْدِ اللَّهِ رَضِيَ اللَّهُ عَنْهُ، إِلَى مَكَّةَ، ثُمَّ قَدِمْنَا جَمْعًا، فَصَلَّى الصَّلاتَيْنِ كُلَّ صَلَاةٍ وَحْدَهَا بِأَذَانٍ وَإِقَامَةِ، وَالعَشَاءُ بَيْنَهُمَا ، ثُمَّ صَلَّى الفَجْرَ حِينَ طَلَعَ الفَجْرُ، قَائِلٌ يَقُولُ: طَلَعَ الفَجْرُ، وَقَائِلٌ يَقُولُ: لَمْ يَطْلُعِ الْفَجْرُ، ثُمَّ قَالَ: إِنَّ رَسُولَ اللَّهِ صَلَّى اللهُ عَلَيْهِ وَسَلَّمَ قَالَ: «إِنَّ هَاتَيْنِ الصَّلَاتَيْنِ حُوَلَتَا عَنْ وَقْتِهِمَا، فِي هَذَا المَكَانِ المَغْرِبَ وَالعِشَاءَ، فَلا يَقْدَمُ النَّاسُ جَمْعًا حَتَّى يُعْتِمُوا، وَصَلَاةَ الْفَجْرِ هَذِهِ السَّاعَةَ» (بخاري بَابٌ: مَتَى يُصَلِّي الفَجْرَ بِجَمْعِ، نمبر: 1683/) وجه : (۱) الحديث لثبوت ثُمَّ وَقَفَ وَوَقَفَ النَّاسُ مَعَهُ \ دَخَلْنَا عَلَى جَابِرِ بْنِ عَبْدِ اللَّهِ، اضْطَجَعَ رَسُولُ اللَّهِ صَلَّى اللَّهُ عَلَيْهِ وَسَلَّمَ حَتَّى طَلَعَ الْفَجْرُ، وَصَلَّى الْفَجْرَ، حِينَ تَبَيَّنَ لَهُ الصُّبْحُ بِأَذَانِ وَإِقَامَةٍ ، ثُمَّ رَكِبَ الْقَصْوَاءَ، حَتَّى أَتَى الْمَشْعَرَ الْحَرَامَ، فَاسْتَقْبَلَ الْقِبْلَةَ، فَدَعَاهُ وَكَبَّرَهُ وَهَلَّلَهُ وَوَحْدَهُ، فَلَمْ يَزَلْ وَاقِفًا حَتَّى أَسْفَرَ جِدًّا، فَدَفَعَ قَبْلَ أَنْ تَطْلُعَ الشَّمْسُ، (مسلم: بَابُ حَجَّةِ النَّبِيِّ صَلَّى اللَّهُ عَلَيْهِ وَسَلَّمَ، نمبر : 1218/ أبو داؤد: بَابُ صِفَةِ حَجَّةِ النَّبِيِّ صَلَّى اللَّهُ عَلَيْهِ وَسَلَّمَ، نمبر: 1905)
Then when dawn breaks, the imam prays with the people Fajr in early darkness, then he stands and the people stand with him. Evidence (1): The hadith for establishing that when dawn breaks the imam prays with the people Fajr in early darkness: He said: We went out with 'Abdullah (ibn Mas'ud) to Makkah, then we came to Muzdalifah. He prayed the two prayers each separately with adhan and iqamah, with the evening meal between them. Then he prayed Fajr when dawn broke - one saying that dawn had broken and another saying it had not. Then he said: The Messenger of Allah (peace be upon him) said: 'These two prayers have been shifted from their times in this place: Maghrib and Isha, so the people should not come to Muzdalifah until they have delayed (until the darkness of night), and the Fajr prayer (is fixed) at this hour' (Bukhari: Chapter of when to pray Fajr at Muzdalifah, no. 1683). Evidence (1): The hadith for establishing that then he stands and the people stand with him: We entered upon Jabir ibn 'Abdullah: The Messenger of Allah (peace be upon him) lay down until dawn broke, and he prayed Fajr when the dawn became clear for him with adhan and iqamah. Then he rode al-Qaswa until he came to the Sacred Monument, faced the qiblah, and supplicated, saying Allahu akbar, la ilaha illallah, and he did not cease standing until it was very bright, then he departed before the sun rose (Muslim: Chapter of the Prophet's Hajj, no. 1218; Abu Dawud: Chapter of the Description of the Prophet's Hajj, no. 1905).
Source pages p. 251

Commentary
This passage is a ruling with proof describing the actions after spending the night at Muzdalifah. When true dawn (fajr al-sadiq) breaks, the imam leads the Fajr prayer in the early darkness (ghalas), meaning it is performed immediately after the appearance of dawn. After the prayer, the imam and the people go to the Mash'ar al-Haram (the Sacred Monument) and stand there in supplication until the sky becomes very bright, then they depart before sunrise. According to the Hanafi school, this standing (wuquf) at Muzdalifah is wajib (obligatory) and one of the obligatory acts of Hajj; its omission requires a dam (penalty). The hadith evidence: 'Abdullah ibn Mas'ud's practice shows that Fajr is prayed at dawn, and the Prophet's statement indicates that the times for these prayers are fixed for this place. The hadith of Jabir provides the complete sequence: the Prophet lay down until dawn, prayed Fajr, then went to the Mash'ar al-Haram and stood supplicating until it was very bright. This is the sunnah for the pilgrim.

Key Terms
بِغَلَس (bi-ghalas): In early darkness, i.e., immediately after the appearance of true dawn while it is still dark.
المَشْعَر الحَرَام (al-Mash'ar al-Haram): The Sacred Monument at Muzdalifah, the specific place of standing after Fajr.

Key Terms from Source Passage

Checkpoint
When does the imam lead the Fajr prayer at Muzdalifah?
A) After sunrise
B) At the end of the night before dawn
C) At early dawn (ghalas)
D) At mid-morning

Key Takeaway
At Muzdalifah, Fajr is offered at early dawn (ghalas) and then standing at al-Mash'ar al-Haram is a wajib act that must be performed until the sky becomes bright.

Praying Fajr in Darkness at Muzdalifah and the Standing
Ruling on performing Fajr prayer in darkness and then standing at Muzdalifah

Learning Objective
By the end of this lesson, you will be able to state the Hanafi ruling on the time of Fajr prayer at Muzdalifah (ghalas) and the standing after it, and explain the proof from the Sunnah.

Core Idea
At Muzdalifah, Fajr is prayed in darkness and the standing follows until isfar – a confirmed sunnah of the Prophet.

This lesson focuses on two specific sunnah acts at Muzdalifah: performing the Fajr prayer in deep darkness (ghalas) and then standing at al-Mash'ar al-Haram. The Hanafi school adheres to the Prophet's practice as recorded in authentic hadiths, distinguishing the time at Muzdalifah from the usual sunnah of praying Fajr at isfar (brightness) on other days. Understanding this ruling ensures that the pilgrim follows the sunnah precisely.

Guided Path
1
Identify the two actions from the matn
Read the matn: 'When dawn breaks, the Imam leads the people in the Fajr prayer in darkness. Then he stood and the people stood with him.' Note that these are consecutive actions.
The matn is from al-Quduri's Mukhtasar.
2
Extract the ruling on the time of Fajr
The phrase 'bi-ghalas' indicates that the prayer is performed while it is still dark, at the first appearance of dawn. This is the preferred time at Muzdalifah.
Contrast with the general recommendation of isfar for Fajr outside Hajj.
3
Locate the hadith proofs
The commentary cites several hadiths. The primary proof for the Fajr timing is the hadith of Abdullah ibn Mas'ud (?) where the Prophet said: 'The Fajr prayer at this hour' (i.e., at early dawn). The standing is proven by the hadith of Jabir describing the Prophet standing at al-Mash'ar al-Haram until isfar.
These are found in Bukhari and Muslim.
4
Understand the Hanafi position on ghalas vs isfar
The Hanafi school holds that at Muzdalifah, Fajr should be prayed in ghalas, unlike other days where isfar is sunnah. This is based on the specific practice of the Prophet at this location.
The Shafi'i school generally prefers isfar even at Muzdalifah, but Hanafis distinguish based on the hadith.
5
Apply to the practice of Hajj
The pilgrim at Muzdalifah should ensure to pray Fajr as soon as dawn appears, even in darkness, and then stand at al-Mash'ar al-Haram until the environment becomes bright (isfar).
This is the mufta bihi position.

فاذا طلع الفجرصلى الامام بالناس الفجر بغلس ٢٤ ثُمَّ وَقَفَ وَوَقَفَ النَّاسُ مَعَهُ
كِتَابُ الْحَجّ
ثُم تَوَضَّأَ وَلَمْ يُسْبِعْ الوُضُوءَ، فَقُلْتُ لَهُ: الصَّلاةُ؟ فَقَالَ: «الصَّلاةُ أَمَامَكَ» ، فَجَاءَ الْمُزْدَلِفَةَ، فَتَوَضَّأَ فَأَسْبَغَ ثُمَّ أُقِيمَتِ الصَّلَاةُ، فَصَلَّى المَغْرِبَ ثُمَّ أَنَاخَ كُلُّ إِنْسَانٍ بَعِيرَهُ فِي مَنْزِلِهِ، ثُمَّ أُقِيمَتِ
الصَّلَاةُ، فَصَلَّى وَلَمْ يُصَلِ بَيْنَهُمَا (بخاري بَابُ الجَمْعِ بَيْنَ الصَّلاتَيْنِ بِالْمُزْدَلِفَةِ، نمبر: 1672) وجه:(۲) قول الصحابي لثبوت وَمَنْ صَلَّى الْمَغْرِبَ فِي الطَّرِيقِ \ حَجَّ عَبْدُ اللَّهِ رَضِيَ اللَّهُ عَنْهُ، فَأَتَيْنَا الْمُزْدَلِفَةَ حِينَ الْأَذَانِ بِالعَتَمَةِ أَوْ قَرِيبًا مِنْ ذَلِكَ، فَأَمَرَ رَجُلًا فَأَذَّنَ وَأَقَامَ، ثُمَّ صَلَّى الْمَغْرِبَ، وَصَلَّى بَعْدَهَا رَكْعَتَيْنِ، ثُمَّ دَعَا بِعَشَائِهِ ،فَتَعَشَّى ثُمَّ أَمَرَ أُرَى فَأَذَّنَ وَأَقَامَ - قَالَ عَمْرُو: لَا أَعْلَمُ الشَّكَ إِلَّا مِنْ زُهَيْرٍ ثُمَّ صَلَّى العِشَاءَ رَكْعَتَيْنِ (بخاري: بَابُ مَنْ أَذَّنَ وَأَقَامَ لِكُلِّ وَاحِدَةٍ مِنْهُمَا، غمبر: 1675)
وجه:(۳) قول الصحابي لثبوت وَمَنْ صَلَّى الْمَغْرِبَ فِي الطَّرِيقِ عَنْ عَبْدِ اللَّهِ بْنِ الزُّبَيْرِ رَضِيَ اللَّهُ عَنْهُ, قَالَ: مِنْ سُنَّةِ الحَجَ ... ثُمَّ يُفِيضُ فَيُصَلِّي بِالْمُزْدَلِفَةِ أَوْحَيْثُ قَضَى اللَّهُ عَزَّ وَجَلَّ ثُمَّ يَقِفُ
بِجَمْعِ (سنن للبيهقي: بَابُ مَنْ قَالَ : يُصَلِّيهِمَا بِالْمُزْدَلِفَةِ أَوْحَيْثُ قَضَى اللَّه عَزَّ وَجَلَّ، 9502) ٢٣. وجه : (۱) الحديث لثبوت فاذا طلع الفجرصلى الامام بالناس الفجر بغلس \ قَالَ: خَرَجْنَا مَعَ عَبْدِ اللَّهِ رَضِيَ اللَّهُ عَنْهُ، إِلَى مَكَّةَ، ثُمَّ قَدِمْنَا جَمْعًا، فَصَلَّى الصَّلاتَيْنِ كُلَّ صَلَاةٍ وَحْدَهَا بِأَذَانٍ وَإِقَامَةِ، وَالعَشَاءُ بَيْنَهُمَا ، ثُمَّ صَلَّى الفَجْرَ حِينَ طَلَعَ الفَجْرُ، قَائِلٌ يَقُولُ: طَلَعَ الفَجْرُ، وَقَائِلٌ يَقُولُ: لَمْ يَطْلُعِ الْفَجْرُ، ثُمَّ قَالَ: إِنَّ رَسُولَ اللَّهِ صَلَّى اللهُ عَلَيْهِ وَسَلَّمَ قَالَ: «إِنَّ هَاتَيْنِ الصَّلَاتَيْنِ حُوَلَتَا عَنْ وَقْتِهِمَا، فِي هَذَا المَكَانِ المَغْرِبَ وَالعِشَاءَ، فَلا يَقْدَمُ النَّاسُ جَمْعًا حَتَّى يُعْتِمُوا، وَصَلَاةَ
الْفَجْرِ هَذِهِ السَّاعَةَ» (بخاري بَابٌ: مَتَى يُصَلِّي الفَجْرَ بِجَمْعِ، نمبر: 1683/)
٢٤ وجه: (١) الحديث لثبوت ثُمَّ وَقَفَ وَوَقَفَ النَّاسُ مَعَهُ \ دَخَلْنَا عَلَى جَابِرِ بْنِ عَبْدِ اللَّهِ، اضْطَجَعَ رَسُولُ اللَّهِ صَلَّى اللَّهُ عَلَيْهِ وَسَلَّمَ حَتَّى طَلَعَ الْفَجْرُ، وَصَلَّى الْفَجْرَ، حِينَ تَبَيَّنَ لَهُ الصُّبْحُ بِأَذَانِ وَإِقَامَةٍ ، ثُمَّ رَكِبَ الْقَصْوَاءَ، حَتَّى أَتَى الْمَشْعَرَ الْحَرَامَ، فَاسْتَقْبَلَ الْقِبْلَةَ، فَدَعَاهُ وَكَبَّرَهُ وَهَلَّلَهُ وَوَحْدَهُ، فَلَمْ يَزَلْ وَاقِفًا حَتَّى أَسْفَرَ جِدًّا، فَدَفَعَ قَبْلَ أَنْ تَطْلُعَ الشَّمْسُ، (مسلم: بَابُ حَجَّةِ النَّبِيِّ صَلَّى اللَّهُ عَلَيْهِ وَسَلَّمَ، نمبر : 1218/ أبو داؤد: بَابُ صِفَةِ حَجَّةِ النَّبِيِّ صَلَّى اللَّهُ عَلَيْهِ
وَسَلَّمَ، نمبر: 1905)
When dawn breaks, the Imam leads the people in the Fajr prayer in darkness. Then he stood and the people stood with him. Book of Hajj. Then he performed ablution but did not perfect it, so I said to him: 'The prayer?' He said: 'The prayer is ahead of you.' Then he came to Muzdalifah, performed ablution properly, then the iqamah was given, and he prayed Maghrib. Then every person made his camel kneel at his camp. Then the iqamah was given for the prayer, and he prayed and did not pray between them. (Bukhari, Book of Combining Two Prayers at Muzdalifah, no. 1672) Aspect: (2) The companion's statement to prove: 'And whoever prayed Maghrib on the way' – Abdullah (may Allah be pleased with him) performed Hajj, and we came to Muzdalifah at the time of the call for Isha or close to that. He ordered a man to give the adhan and iqamah, then prayed Maghrib, and after it prayed two rak'ahs, then called for his dinner, ate, then ordered (I think) and the adhan and iqamah were given – Amr said: I don't know the doubt except from Zuhayr – then he prayed Isha two rak'ahs. (Bukhari: Chapter on Whoever Gave Adhan and Iqamah for Each of Them, no. 1675) Aspect: (3) The companion's statement to prove: 'And whoever prayed Maghrib on the way' – from Abdullah ibn al-Zubayr (may Allah be pleased with him), he said: 'From the sunnah of Hajj... then he proceeds and prays at Muzdalifah or wherever Allah Almighty decrees, then he stands at Jam'. (Sunan al-Bayhaqi: Chapter on Whoever Said: He Prays Both at Muzdalifah or Wherever Allah Decrees, no. 9502) 23. Aspect: (1) The hadith to prove: 'When dawn breaks, the Imam leads the people in the Fajr prayer in darkness' – He said: We went out with Abdullah (may Allah be pleased with him) to Makkah, then we came to Jam' (Muzdalifah). He prayed both prayers, each separately with adhan and iqamah, with dinner between them. Then he prayed Fajr when dawn had broken, some saying 'Dawn has broken' and some saying 'Dawn has not broken'. Then he said: The Messenger of Allah (peace be upon him) said: 'These two prayers have been moved from their times at this place – Maghrib and Isha, so the people should not come to Jam' until it becomes dark, and the Fajr prayer at this hour.' (Bukhari: Chapter: When to pray Fajr at Jam', no. 1683/) 24. Aspect: (1) The hadith to prove: 'Then he stood and the people stood with him' – We visited Jabir ibn Abdullah (and he said): The Messenger of Allah (peace be upon him) lay down until dawn broke, then prayed Fajr when the dawn had clearly appeared with adhan and iqamah. Then he mounted al-Qaswa' until he came to al-Mash'ar al-Haram, faced the qiblah, supplicated, said takbir, tahlil, and tahmid, and kept standing until it became very bright, then he departed before sunrise. (Muslim: Chapter on the Prophet's Hajj, no. 1218 / Abu Dawud: Chapter on the Description of the Prophet's Hajj, no. 1905)
Source pages p. 251

Commentary
This passage from al-Quduri's matn states two consecutive actions at Muzdalifah: the Imam prays Fajr in darkness (ghalas) and then stands with the people. The commentator then provides three categories of proofs: for the Fajr prayer time, for praying Maghrib and Isha separately, and for the standing. The primary proof for the Fajr prayer is a hadith from Abdullah ibn Mas'ud (?) where the Prophet (peace be upon him) said that Maghrib and Isha are delayed at Muzdalifah and Fajr is prayed at early dawn. The standing at Muzdalifah is proven by the hadith of Jabir describing the Prophet's Hajj, where he stood at al-Mash'ar al-Haram until it became very bright, then left before sunrise. Note that the standing at Muzdalifah is a recommended act (mustahabb) according to the Hanafi school, not obligatory.

Key Terms
غلس (ghalas): The darkness just before dawn; the time when Fajr prayer is performed at Muzdalifah while it is still dark.
مزدلفة (Muzdalifah): A location between Arafat and Mina where pilgrims spend the night and perform the combined Maghrib and Isha prayers, and Fajr prayer on the 10th of Dhul Hijjah.

Key Terms from Source Passage

Checkpoint
When should the Imam pray Fajr at Muzdalifah?
A) After sunrise
B) In darkness (ghalas)
C) At midday
D) Just before sunset

Key Takeaway
At Muzdalifah, Fajr is to be prayed in darkness (ghalas) followed by standing at al-Mash'ar al-Haram until isfar – a confirmed sunnah of Hajj.

All of Muzdalifah is a Standing Place Except Batn Muhassir
Ruling on the boundary of Muzdalifah for the standing.

Learning Objective
By the end of this lesson, you will be able to state the precise boundaries of the standing place (mawqif) in Muzdalifah and explain the hadith evidence that excludes Batn Muhassir.

Core Idea
The entire valley of Muzdalifah is valid for wuquf except the valley of Muhassir.

This lesson clarifies a key ruling in the Hajj rituals: the boundaries for the obligatory standing (wuquf) at Muzdalifah. The passage explicitly states that all of Muzdalifah is a standing place except Batn Muhassir. Understanding this exception ensures that pilgrims fulfill the wajib correctly. The proof is a prophetic hadith that defines the limits of the sacred sites.

Guided Path
1
Identify the Ruling
State the ruling: all of Muzdalifah is a mawqif (standing place). This is the default rule.
The ruling applies to the entire area of Muzdalifah.
2
Locate the Exception
Identify the exception: Batn Muhassir is excluded. Note that this is a specific valley between Muzdalifah and Mina.
The exception is explicit: 'illa batna muhassir'.
3
Examine the Dalil
Analyze the hadith from Jabir ibn Abdullah. The Prophet said: 'All of Muzdalifah is a standing place, and avoid the valley of Muhassir.'
The hadith is ahad but accepted in Hanafi usul for establishing this ruling.
4
Understand the Authority
Recognize that the ruling is muttafaq alayh (agreed upon) among schools. The Hanafi position is based on zahir al-riwayah.
No intra-Hanafi ikhtilaf is reported on this point.
5
Apply Practically
A pilgrim must stand anywhere in Muzdalifah but avoid Batn Muhassir. If standing there accidentally, the wuquf is invalid.
The consequence is a dam (compensation) if missed.

Source Text
⚠ Extracted via Advanced OCR ∼97% accuracy, minor errors may remain — always verify against original Arabic books
٢٥ وَالْمُزْدَلِفَةُ كُلُّهَا مَوْقِفٌ إِلَّا بَطْنَ مُحَسِرٍ ٢٦ ثُمَّ أَفَاضَ الْإِمَامُ وَالنَّاسُ مَعَهُ قَبْلَ طُلُوعِ الشَّمْسِ حَتَّى يَأْتُوا مِيَ فَيَبْتَدِئُ بِجَمْرَةِ الْعَقَبَةِ فَيَرْمِيهَا مِنْ بَطْنِ الْوَادِي بِسَبْعِ حَصَيَاتٍ مِثْلَ حَصَى الْخَذْفِ يُكَبِّرُ مَعَ كُلَّ حَصَاةٍ ٢٨ وَلَا يَقِفُ عِنْدَهَا ٢٥. وجه : (۱) الحديث لثبوت وَالْمُزْدَلِفَةُ كُلُّهَا مَوْقِفٌ إِلَّا بَطْنَ مُحَسِرٍ \ عَنْ جَابِرِ بْنِ عَبْدِ اللَّهِ، قَالَ: قَالَ رَسُولُ اللَّهِ صَلَّى اللهُ عَلَيْهِ وَسَلَّمَ: «كُلُّ عَرَفَةَ مَوْقِفٌ، وَارْتَفِعُوا عَنْ بَطْنِ عُرَنَةَ، وَكُلُّ الْمُزْدَلِفَةِ مَوْقِفٌ، وَارْتَفِعُوا عَنْ بَطْنِ مُحَسَرٍ، وَكُلُّ مِنْ مَنْحَرٌ ، إِلَّا مَا وَرَاءَ الْعَقَبَةِ» (سنن ابن ماجة: بَابُ الْمَوْقِفِ بِعَرَفَةَ، نمبر: 3012)
25. And all of Muzdalifah is a standing place except the valley of Muhassir. 26. Then the Imam and the people with him depart before sunrise until they come to Mina, and he begins with Jamrat al-Aqabah, throwing it from the bottom of the valley with seven pebbles like pebbles of khadhf, saying takbir with each pebble. 28. And he does not stop at it. 25. Aspect: (1) The hadith to prove: 'All of Muzdalifah is a standing place except the valley of Muhassir' – From Jabir ibn Abdullah, he said: The Messenger of Allah (peace be upon him) said: 'All of Arafat is a standing place, and avoid the valley of Urana; all of Muzdalifah is a standing place, and avoid the valley of Muhassir; and all of Mina is a place of sacrifice except what is behind al-Aqabah.' (Sunan Ibn Majah: Chapter on the Standing at Arafat, no. 3012)
Source pages p. 252

Commentary
This passage states the ruling that the entire area of Muzdalifah is a valid standing place (mawqif) for the devotional stay (wuquf) during Hajj, except for the valley of Muhassir. The commentator provides a hadith from the Prophet (peace be upon him) that explicitly excludes Batn Muhassir. In Hanafi fiqh, standing at Muzdalifah is wajib, and one must ensure it is done within the proper boundaries. The valley of Muhassir is a narrow valley between Muzdalifah and Mina; standing there is not considered part of Muzdalifah.

Key Terms
موقف (mawqif): The place where pilgrims stand (wuquf) during Hajj; here referring to Muzdalifah.
بطن محسر (Batn Muhassir): A valley between Muzdalifah and Mina that is excluded from the standing place of Muzdalifah.

Key Terms from Source Passage

Checkpoint
Which area of Muzdalifah is not valid for the standing (wuquf)?
A) Batn Urana
B) Batn Muhassir
C) The entire Muzdalifah
D) Al-Mash'ar al-Haram

Key Takeaway
The entire Muzdalifah is valid for standing except Batn Muhassir, as established by the Prophet's hadith.

Departure from Muzdalifah and Throwing Jamrat al-Aqabah
Rulings on departing Muzdalifah before sunrise and the method of throwing Jamrat al-Aqabah

Learning Objective
By the end of this lesson, you will be able to state the three sunnah actions related to leaving Muzdalifah and throwing Jamrat al-Aqabah, and trace the evidence from the Sahaba and hadith.

Core Idea
The Hajj rites are defined by prophetic practice; departing before dawn and pelting Jamrat al-Aqabah without pausing are sunnahs rooted in opposition to pre-Islamic customs.

After spending the night at Muzdalifah, the pilgrim proceeds to Mina to begin the stoning rites. The passage details three specific sunnah actions: the timing of departure, the method of throwing Jamrat al-Aqabah, and the fact that no supplication is made after this particular jamrah. These practices are confirmed by the actions of the Prophet (peace be upon him) and the early Muslims, as narrated by Ibn Umar and others.

Guided Path
1
Identify the three sunnah actions
Read the passage and list the three distinct rulings: (a) departing Muzdalifah before sunrise, (b) throwing Jamrat al-Aqabah from the valley with seven pebbles while saying takbir each time, (c) not stopping at Jamrat al-Aqabah after throwing.
These are all sunnah muakkadah (emphasized sunnahs).
2
Trace the proof for each action
For departure: the athar of Umar (may Allah be pleased with him) stating the Prophet opposed the polytheists. For throwing method: the hadith of Jabir describing the route and the practice of Ibn Umar. For not stopping: the explicit statement of Ibn Umar that he would not stop at it.
All proofs are from sahih hadith and companion statements.
3
Understand the Hanafi classification
The Hanafi school considers these actions as sunnah muakkadah based on continuous prophetic practice. They are not obligatory but are highly recommended and part of the perfect Hajj.
Omission does not invalidate the Hajj.
4
Apply the ruling in practice
A pilgrim should: 1) After Fajr at Muzdalifah, depart before sunrise, 2) Go directly to Jamrat al-Aqabah, 3) Throw from the valley with seven pebbles, each followed by takbir, 4) Leave immediately without pausing for supplication.
This contrasts with the other jamrahs where standing and supplication are sunnah.

Source Text
⚠ Extracted via Advanced OCR ∼97% accuracy, minor errors may remain — always verify against original Arabic books
٢٦ ثُمَّ أَفَاضَ الْإِمَامُ وَالنَّاسُ مَعَهُ قَبْلَ طُلُوعِ الشَّمْسِ حَتَّى يَأْتُوا مِيَ فَيَبْتَدِئُ بِجَمْرَةِ الْعَقَبَةِ فَيَرْمِيهَا مِنْ بَطْنِ الْوَادِي بِسَبْعِ حَصَيَاتٍ مِثْلَ حَصَى الْخَذْفِ يُكَبِّرُ مَعَ كُلَّ حَصَاةٍ ٢٨ وَلَا يَقِفُ عِنْدَهَا ٢٦. وجه:(۱) قول الصحابي لثبوت ثُمَّ أَفَاضَ الْإِمَامُ وَالنَّاسُ مَعَهُ قَبْلَ طُلُوعِ الشَّمْسِ سَمِعْتُ عَمْرَو بْنَ مَيْمُونٍ، يَقُولُ: شَهِدْتُ عُمَرَ رَضِيَ اللَّهُ عَنْهُ صَلَّى بِجَمْعِ الصُّبْحَ، ثُمَّ وَقَفَ فَقَالَ: إِنَّ المشركينَ كَانُوا لا يُفِيضُونَ حَتَّى تَطْلُعَ الشَّمْسُ وَيَقُولُونَ: أَشْرِقْ تَبِيرُ ، وَأَنَّ النَّبِيَّ صَلَّى اللَّهُ عَلَيْهِ وَسَلَّمَ خَالَفَهُمْ ثُمَّ أَفَاضَ قَبْلَ أَنْ تَطْلُعَ الشَّمْسُ (بخاري بَابُ مَتَى يُدْفَعُ مِنْ جَمع، نمبر: 1684 ٢٧ وجه: (1) الحديث لثبوت فَيَبْتَدِئُ بِجَمْرَةِ الْعَقَبَةِ فَيَرْمِيهَا \ دَخَلْنَا عَلَى جَابِرِ بْنِ عَبْدِ اللَّهِ، حَتَّى أَتَى بَطْنَ مُحَسِرٍ، فَحَرَّكَ قَلِيلًا، ثُمَّ سَلَكَ الطَّرِيقَ الْوُسْطَى الَّتِي تَخْرُجُ عَلَى الْجُمْرَةِ الْكُبْرَى، (مسلم: بَابُ حَجَّةِ النَّبِيِّ صَلَّى اللهُ عَلَيْهِ وَسَلَّمَ، نمبر : 1218/ أبو داؤد: بَابُ صِفَةِ حَجَّةِ النَّبِيِّ صَلَّى اللهُ عَلَيْهِ وَسَلَّمَ، غبر: 1905)
وجه : (۱) قول الصحابي لثبوت وَلَا يَقِفُ عِنْدَهَا \ عَنِ ابْنِ عُمَرَ رَضِيَ اللَّهُ عَنْهُمَا: أَنَّهُ كَانَ يَرْمِي الجُمْرَةَ الدُّنْيَا بِسَبْع حَصَيَاتٍ يُكَبِّرُ عَلَى إِثْرِ كُلَّ حَصَاةٍ، ثُمَّ يَتَقَدَّمُ حَتَّى يُسْهِلَ، فَيَقُومَ مُسْتَقْبِلَ القِبْلَةِ، فَيَقُومُ طَوِيلًا، وَيَدْعُو وَيَرْفَعُ يَدَيْهِ، ثُمَّ يَرْمِي الوُسْطَى، ثُمَّ يَأْخُذُ ذَاتَ الشِّمَالِ فَيَسْتَهِلْ، وَيَقُومُ مُسْتَقْبِلَ القِبْلَةِ، فَيَقُومُ طَوِيلًا، وَيَدْعُو وَيَرْفَعُ يَدَيْهِ، وَيَقُومُ طَوِيلًا، ثُمَّ يَرْمِي جَمْرَةَ ذَاتِ العَقَبَةِ مِنْ بَطْنِ الْوَادِي، وَلَا يَقِفُ عِنْدَهَا، ثُمَّ يَنْصَرِفُ، فَيَقُولُ «هَكَذَا رَأَيْتُ النَّبِيَّ صَلَّى اللَّهُ عَلَيْهِ وَسَلَّمَ يَفْعَلُهُ» (بخاري : بَابُ إِذَا رَمَى الجُمْرَتَيْنِ، يَقُومُ وَيُسْهل، نمبر: 1751/ سنن ابن ماجة: بَابٌ إِذَا رَمَى جَمْرَةَ الْعَقَبَةِ، نمبر : 3032)
26. Then the Imam and the people with him depart before sunrise until they come to Mina, and he begins with Jamrat al-Aqabah, throwing it from the bottom of the valley with seven pebbles like pebbles of khadhf, saying takbir with each pebble. 28. And he does not stop at it. 26. Aspect: (1) The companion's statement to prove: 'Then the Imam and the people with him depart before sunrise' – I heard Amr ibn Maymun say: I witnessed Umar (may Allah be pleased with him) pray the morning prayer at Jam' (Muzdalifah), then he stood and said: Indeed the polytheists would not depart until the sun had risen and they would say: 'Brighten, O Thabir!' But the Prophet (peace be upon him) opposed them and departed before sunrise. (Bukhari, Chapter: When to depart from Jam', no. 1684) 27. Aspect: (1) The hadith to prove: 'He begins with Jamrat al-Aqabah and throws it' – We visited Jabir ibn Abdullah, until he came to Batn Muhassir, he shook it a little, then took the middle road that comes out at the large Jamrah. (Muslim: Chapter on the Prophet's Hajj, no. 1218 / Abu Dawud: Chapter on the Description of the Prophet's Hajj, no. 1905) Aspect: (1) The companion's statement to prove: 'And he does not stop at it' – From Ibn Umar (may Allah be pleased with them): He used to throw the first Jamrah with seven pebbles, saying takbir after each pebble, then he would go forward until he was in a level place, stand facing the qiblah, stand for a long time, supplicate and raise his hands, then throw the middle Jamrah, then take to the left, go to level ground, stand facing the qiblah, stand for a long time, supplicate and raise his hands, and stand for a long time, then he would throw Jamrat Dhat al-Aqabah from the bottom of the valley, and he would not stop at it, then he would leave, and say: 'Thus I saw the Prophet (peace be upon him) do.' (Bukhari: Chapter: When one throws the two Jamrahs, he stands and makes it easy, no. 1751 / Sunan Ibn Majah: Chapter: When one throws Jamrat al-Aqabah, no. 3032)
Source pages p. 252

Commentary
This passage gives three rulings: (1) The Imam and pilgrims depart from Muzdalifah before sunrise, as per the practice of Umar and the Prophet's opposition to the polytheists who waited for sunrise. (2) They proceed to Mina and begin with throwing Jamrat al-Aqabah (the large jamrah) from the bottom of the valley, using seven pebbles similar to khadhf (small pebbles used in slinging), and saying takbir with each pebble. (3) After throwing Jamrat al-Aqabah, the pilgrim does not stop there but moves on, unlike the other jamrahs where standing and supplication are recommended. The proofs include athar from Umar, hadith from Jabir and practice of Ibn Umar.

Key Terms
جمرة العقبة (Jamrat al-Aqabah): The large stone pillar (jamrah) closest to Mina, which is pelted on the 10th of Dhul Hijjah.
خذف (khadhf): Small pebbles used in slinging, indicating the size of the pebbles for throwing.

Key Terms from Source Passage

Checkpoint
What does the passage state about the pilgrim's action after throwing Jamrat al-Aqabah?
A) He should stand and make long supplication facing the qiblah
B) He should leave immediately without stopping
C) He should sacrifice an animal
D) He should proceed to the other jamrahs

Key Takeaway
The three sunnah actions for the morning of the 10th of Dhul Hijjah are: depart Muzdalifah before sunrise, throw Jamrat al-Aqabah from the valley with seven pebbles and takbir, and do not stop after throwing.

Ghalas and Isfar for Fajr: Contextual Ruling at Muzdalifah
Brief note explaining contextual Fajr ruling

Learning Objective
By the end of this lesson, you will be able to explain the Hanafi ruling regarding ghalas and isfar for Fajr prayer and identify the contextual factors that change the recommendation.

Core Idea
Ghalas is not always better; the ruling depends on the context of Muzdalifah versus normal days.

This lesson clarifies a common point of confusion in Hanafi fiqh: when should Fajr be prayed in darkness (ghalas) and when should it be delayed to brightness (isfar)? The short Urdu note below from our source text explains the distinction, highlighting that at Muzdalifah, the recommendation of ghalas is due to the pilgrim's occupations, whereas on normal days, isfar is recommended. We will analyse the reasoning and see how it applies in practice.

Guided Path
1
Identify the two scenarios
Read the passage and note that it gives two distinct situations: (1) Fajr at Muzdalifah during Hajj, and (2) Fajr on normal days. The ruling differs between them.
The key is to see that the ruling is not absolute but context-dependent.
2
State the ruling for each scenario
For Muzdalifah: ghalas (praying in darkness) is mustahabb. For normal days: isfar (praying when bright) is mustahabb. Both are recommendations (not obligations).
Mustahabb means recommended or praiseworthy, not obligatory.
3
Understand the reason for the difference
The passage gives a reason: at Muzdalifah, pilgrims are occupied with important rites (e.g., proceeding to Mina), so praying early in darkness allows them to fulfil those obligations. On normal days, there is no such urgency, so delaying for brightness makes the prayer easier for more people.
This is a classic example of a ruling changing due to circumstance (sabab).
4
Apply the principle to other contexts
Consider whether the same reasoning might apply to other Hajj days or other prayers. For example, at Mina on the days of al-Tashriq, there are also crowded rites, so similar considerations may apply.
This helps internalise the method of contextual application.

Source Text
⚠ Extracted via Advanced OCR ∼97% accuracy, minor errors may remain — always verify against original Arabic books
اصول : مزدلفہ میں نماز فجر غلس یعنی اندھیرے میں پڑھنا مستحب ہے اہم مشاغل کی وجہ سے جبکہ عام دنوں میں فجر کو اسفار کر کے پڑھنا مستحب ہے۔
Principle: At Muzdalifah, it is mustahabb to pray Fajr in ghalas (darkness) due to important occupations, whereas on normal days it is mustahabb to pray Fajr with isfar (brightness).
Source pages p. 252

Commentary
This Urdu note explains the wisdom behind the ruling: at Muzdalifah, Fajr is prayed in darkness because pilgrims are occupied with other rites (like proceeding to Mina). On normal days, it is recommended to delay Fajr until it becomes brighter (isfar) to ensure more people can pray. This distinction is based on the Hanafi understanding of the relevant hadiths.

Key Terms
غلس (ghalas): Darkness (praying Fajr in early dawn).
اسفار (isfar): Brightness (praying Fajr when it is light enough).
مستحب (mustahabb): Recommended, praiseworthy, but not obligatory.

Key Terms from Source Passage

Checkpoint

B) Due to important occupations (ahamm mashaghil)
C) Because it is a sunnah to always pray in darkness
D) To avoid the cold

Key Takeaway
The Hanafi ruling on ghalas vs. isfar for Fajr is context-dependent: ghalas is recommended at Muzdalifah due to pressing Hajj rites, while isfar is recommended on normal days for ease.

Muzdalifah: The Entire Valley is a Standing Place
Ruling with proof from hadith establishing the entire area as mawqif except Batn Muhassir.

Learning Objective
By the end of this lesson, you will be able to state the Hanafi ruling on the boundaries of the standing place at Muzdalifah and identify the exception of Batn Muhassir with its proof.

Core Idea
All of Muzdalifah is valid for standing except Batn Muhassir — a clear hadith exception.

In Hajj, after standing at Arafat, pilgrims proceed to Muzdalifah for another standing (wuquf). Al-Quduri's matn establishes that the entire area of Muzdalifah is a valid standing place, except for one specific valley. This lesson unpacks that ruling and the evidence from the Prophet's ﷺ command.

Guided Path
1
Identify the act and its ruling
The act is standing (wuquf) at Muzdalifah. The Hanafi school considers this wajib (compulsory) based on the command in the hadith.
Some scholars consider it sunnah, but the relied-upon position is wajib.
2
Locate the dalil
The proof is the hadith of Jabir (ra): 'All of Muzdalifah is a standing place, and avoid the valley of Muhassir.' (Ibn Majah)
The hadith is ahad, but accepted in Hanafi fiqh.
3
Trace the wajh al-dalalah
The explicit phrase 'كل المزدلفة موقف' indicates that every part of Muzdalifah qualifies. The command 'ارتفعوا عن بطن محسر' explicitly excludes Batn Muhassir.
The exclusion is specific and must be applied.
4
Note the ikhtilaf
Other schools (e.g., Shafi'i) also consider standing at Muzdalifah as wajib and agree on the exception of Batn Muhassir.
The main difference among schools is the status of standing at Muzdalifah (wajib vs. sunnah), but all agree on the location.
5
Evaluate the Hanafi tarjih
The Hanafi school's mufta bihi (operative opinion) is that standing at Muzdalifah is wajib and the entire area except Batn Muhassir is valid.
This is from Zahir al-Riwayah and supported by the hadith.

Source Text
⚠ Extracted via Advanced OCR ∼97% accuracy, minor errors may remain — always verify against original Arabic books
وَالْمُزْدَلِفَةُ كُلُّهَا مَوْقِفٌ إِلَّا بَطْنَ مُحَسَّرٍ
And all of Muzdalifah is a standing place except the valley of Muhassir.
Source pages p. 252

Commentary
This is a ruling from the matn of Al-Quduri regarding the Hajj ritual of standing (wuquf) in Muzdalifah. The text states that the entire area of Muzdalifah is a valid place for standing, meaning that a pilgrim may stand anywhere within its boundaries to fulfill the obligation of wuquf at Muzdalifah after returning from Arafat. The exception is Batn Muhassir, which is a valley between Muzdalifah and Mina; standing there is not considered part of the ritual. The proof cited is a hadith from Jabir ibn Abdillah (may Allah be pleased with him) that the Prophet ﷺ said: 'All of Muzdalifah is a standing place, and avoid the valley of Muhassir.' (Ibn Majah, no. 3012) The hadith clearly establishes the ruling. The Hanafi school follows this, and the exception is specific to the valley of Muhassir. This ruling is from Zahir al-Riwayah, as it is found in the core texts.

Key Terms
مَوْقِف (mawqif): A place where one stands during Hajj rituals, specifically the standing (wuquf) at Muzdalifah.
بَطْن مُحَسَّر (batn muhassir): A valley between Muzdalifah and Mina; standing there is not part of the Hajj ritual.

Key Terms from Source Passage

Checkpoint

D) Near the hill

Key Takeaway
All of Muzdalifah is a valid standing place except Batn Muhassir, as established by the Prophet's ﷺ hadith.

Departure from Muzdalifah and Stoning Jamrat al-Aqabah: Ruling and Procedure
Ruling on departure from Muzdalifah and stoning Jamrat al-Aqabah procedure.

Learning Objective
By the end of this lesson, you will be able to state the Hanafi ruling on the time of departure from Muzdalifah and describe the procedure for stoning Jamrat al-Aqabah, including its sunnah and wajib dimensions.

Core Idea
Depart for Mina before sunrise, stone Jamrat al-Aqabah from the valley with seven small pebbles, say takbir, and do not stop.

This passage from Al-Quduri outlines the Sunnah of the Prophet ﷺ after the night at Muzdalifah. The Imam and pilgrims depart before sunrise and proceed directly to Mina. The first and primary act upon arrival is stoning Jamrat al-Aqabah with seven pebbles from the bottom of the valley, saying takbir with each throw, and unlike the other jamarat, one does not stop for supplication. Understanding this procedure ensures the pilgrim follows the confirmed Sunnah.

Guided Path
1
Identify the Ruling on Departure Time
The matn states the Imam and people depart before sunrise. Determine the hukm level: is it wajib or sunnah?
The Hanafi position is that departing before sunrise is sunnah muakkadah, not wajib.
2
Locate the Primary Obligation
Stoning Jamrat al-Aqabah is wajib on the day of Nahr. Identify the conditions: seven pebbles, from batn al-wadi, small size.
The obligation is the act of stoning itself; the specific manner is sunnah.
3
Examine the Sunnah Elements
The specific actions (stoning from the valley, saying takbir, not stopping) are sunnah muakkadah and are not required for the validity of the stoning wajib.
Omitting a sunnah does not invalidate the Hajj, but it is a loss of reward.
4
Review the Proofs
The hadith of Umar (Bukhari no. 1684) shows departure before sunrise; the hadith of Jabir (Muslim no. 1218) shows starting with Jamrat al-Aqabah; the hadith of Ibn Umar (Bukhari no. 1751) shows the manner of stoning and not stopping.
These ahadith form the basis for the Hanafi practice.
5
Note the Hanafi Specificity
Hanafi requires stoning from the bottom of the valley (batn al-wadi), unlike other schools that permit any part of the jamrah area.
This is based on the practice of the Prophet ﷺ as narrated in the hadith of Ibn Umar.

Source Text
⚠ Extracted via Advanced OCR ∼97% accuracy, minor errors may remain — always verify against original Arabic books
ثُمَّ أَفَاضَ الْإِمَامُ وَالنَّاسُ مَعَهُ قَبْلَ طُلُوعِ الشَّمْسِ حَتَّى يَأْتُوا مِنًى فَيَبْتَدِئُ بِجَمْرَةِ الْعَقَبَةِ فَيَرْمِيهَا مِنْ بَطْنِ الْوَادِي بِسَبْعِ حَصَيَاتٍ مِثْلَ حَصَى الْخَذْفِ يُكَبِّرُ مَعَ كُلِّ حَصَاةٍ وَلَا يَقِفُ عِنْدَهَا
Then the Imam and the people with him depart before sunrise until they come to Mina, and he begins with Jamrat al-Aqabah, stoning it from the bottom of the valley with seven pebbles like pebbles of khadhf, saying takbir with each pebble, and he does not stop at it.
Source pages p. 252

Commentary
This passage details the actions after standing at Muzdalifah. After the night at Muzdalifah, the Imam (or leader) and the pilgrims depart before sunrise, heading to Mina. The first act upon arriving in Mina is to stone the Jamrat al-Aqabah (the large pillar). The stoning is done from the bottom of the valley (batn al-wadi) using seven small pebbles, similar to the size of pebbles used for khadhf (a game). With each pebble, the pilgrim says 'Allahu Akbar'. Importantly, unlike the other jamarat, the pilgrim does not stop to make du'a after stoning Jamrat al-Aqabah; he proceeds directly. The proofs cited include a hadith from Amr ibn Maimun describing Umar's practice and the Prophet's Sunnah of departing before sunrise (Bukhari no. 1684), the hadith of Jabir describing the Prophet's route to the jamrah (Muslim no. 1218), and a hadith from Ibn Umar describing the stoning and the fact that the Prophet did not stop at Jamrat al-Aqabah (Bukhari no. 1751). The Hanafi school follows these practices, considering them sunnah muakkadah.

Key Terms
جَمْرَة الْعَقَبَة (jamrat al-aqabah): The largest of the three pillars at Mina, which is stoned on the day of Nahr (10th Dhul Hijjah).
حَصَى الْخَذْف (hasa al-khadhf): Pebbles approximately the size of a chickpea or a bit larger, used for throwing.
بَطْن الْوَادِي (batn al-wadi): The bottom of the valley, a specific area at Mina where the jamarat are located.

Key Terms from Source Passage

Checkpoint

A) Three
B) Five
C) Seven
D) Ten

Key Takeaway
The Hanafi school specifies that on the day of Nahr, pilgrims should depart Muzdalifah before sunrise, stone Jamrat al-Aqabah from the valley with seven small pebbles, say takbir, and not stop for du'a – this procedure combines wajib (stoning) and sunnah muakkadah (the manner).

Cutting Talbiyah at the First Pebble
Ruling on ending talbiyah during Hajj

Learning Objective
By the end of this lesson, you will be able to state the Hanafi ruling on when to stop talbiyah during Hajj and support it with the hadith evidence.

Core Idea
Talbiyah ends with the first stone of Jamrat al-Aqabah — not a moment later.

The talbiyah is a key sunnah of ihram, recited from the miqat until a specific moment during the stoning rituals. This precise timing is a sunnah practice, not a wajib; knowing it ensures the pilgrim follows the optimal practice. The matn gives a clear endpoint: the first pebble thrown at Jamrat al-Aqabah.

Guided Path
1
Identify the act and its ruling
The act is reciting talbiyah during Hajj. The ruling is about when to stop it. According to the matn, it stops 'with the first pebble'.
This is a specific timing within the stoning ritual.
2
Locate the dalil
The proof is from two hadiths: one from Ibn Abbas (Bukhari) and one from Fadl ibn Abbas (Ibn Majah) that the Prophet continued talbiyah until he stoned the jamrah.
Both are ahad hadith, giving zanni thubut.
3
Trace the wajh al-dalalah
The phrase 'until he stoned the jamrah' explicitly marks the endpoint. The action of stoning coincides with stopping talbiyah.
The first pebble is the moment of stoning.
4
Note the hukm level
The Hanafi school holds this as sunnah, not wajib. If a pilgrim continues after the first pebble, there is no sin, but the sunnah is missed.
Sunnah: omission is not sinful but leaves the preferred practice.
5
Consider cross-madhhab views
The Maliki school also stops talbiyah at stoning, but the Hanafi precisely at the first pebble based on the explicit hadith. The practical difference is minimal.
No major dispute among schools on the basic timing.

Source Text
⚠ Extracted via Advanced OCR ∼97% accuracy, minor errors may remain — always verify against original Arabic books
وَيَقْطَعُ التَّلْبِيَةَ مَعَ أَوَّلِ حَصَاةٍ
And he cuts off the talbiyah with the first pebble.
Source pages p. 253

Commentary
This is a ruling regarding the timing of ending the talbiyah (recitation of 'Labbaik Allahumma labbaik...') during Hajj. The pilgrim continues to recite talbiyah from the start of ihram until he begins stoning Jamrat al-Aqabah. At the moment he throws the first pebble, he should stop reciting talbiyah. The proofs cited are two hadiths: one from Ibn Abbas (Bukhari no. 1685) that the Prophet continued talbiyah until he stoned the jamrah, and another from Fadl ibn Abbas (Ibn Majah no. 3040) that when the Prophet stoned Jamrat al-Aqabah, he stopped talbiyah. The Hanafi school follows this, considering it sunnah to stop talbiyah at this point. Note that the talbiyah is not invalidated by stopping earlier, but the sunnah is to continue until the first stone.

Key Terms
التَّلْبِيَة (talbiyah): The specific supplication recited by a pilgrim in ihram, beginning with 'Labbaik Allahumma labbaik'.

Key Terms from Source Passage

D) At sunset of Arafah

Key Takeaway
Talbiyah ends at the first pebble of Jamrat al-Aqabah, as sunnah, based on explicit hadith.

Slaughter after Stoning: Obligation or Option?
Ruling on the option to slaughter after stoning.

Learning Objective
By the end of this lesson, you will be able to distinguish when slaughter (hady) is wajib and when it is recommended in Hajj according to the Hanafi school.

Core Idea
Slaughter after stoning is obligatory for tamattu' and qiran pilgrims, but only recommended for ifrad.

The matn states simply: 'Then he slaughters if he wishes.' This brief phrase raises a key question: Is slaughter an obligation or a mere option? The answer depends on the type of Hajj one performs. In this lesson, we unpack the Hanafi position on the sacrificial animal (hady) and its legal weight.

Guided Path
1
Identify the act and its context
The act is slaughtering (dhabh/nahr) after stoning Jamrat al-Aqabah on the day of Nahr (10th Dhul Hijjah). The phrasing 'if he wishes' suggests optionality, but we must see if that is the full ruling.
2
Determine the hukm level from the matn
The matn uses 'in ahabba' (if he wishes), which literally indicates choice. However, the Hanafi school clarifies that this applies primarily to the ifrad pilgrim. For tamattu' and qiran, slaughter is wajib.
3
Examine the Hanafi classification
The Hanafi school distinguishes three types of Hajj: tamattu' (Umrah followed by Hajj with a break), qiran (combining Umrah and Hajj with one ihram), and ifrad (Hajj alone). Slaughter is wajib for tamattu' and qiran, mustahabb for ifrad.
The proof: Quran 2:196 and the Prophet's practice.
4
Analyze the proof (dalil)
The text cites part of the long hadith of Jabir (Muslim 1218) where the Prophet slaughtered after stoning. The Hanafi reading sees this as evidence that slaughter is a sunnah or wajib depending on context, but the matn's 'if he wishes' indicates it is not a rukn.
Note: The hadith is about the Prophet's qiran Hajj, not necessarily applicable to all types.
5
Note the cross-madhhab perspective
The Shafi'i school similarly requires slaughter for tamattu' and qiran but classifies it as sunnah mu'akkadah for ifrad. The practical difference is minimal; both agree on the obligation for mutamatti' and qarin.

Source Text
⚠ Extracted via Advanced OCR ∼97% accuracy, minor errors may remain — always verify against original Arabic books
ثُمَّ يَذْبَحُ إِنْ أَحَبَّ
Then he slaughters if he wishes.
Source pages p. 253

Commentary
This matn statement addresses the act of slaughtering (nahr or dhabh) after stoning on the day of Nahr (10th Dhul Hijjah). The phrase 'if he wishes' indicates that it is not obligatory for every pilgrim; it is a recommended act (wajib for those performing tamattu' or qiran, but optional for ifrad). The Hanafi school distinguishes: slaughter (hady) is obligatory for tamattu' and qiran Hajj, and for those who miss certain obligations, but for someone performing ifrad (single Hajj without Umrah), slaughter is not required. The text here seems to refer to the general option for a pilgrim who is not obligated to slaughter. The proof given is a hadith from Jabir describing the Prophet's Hajj, which includes that after stoning, he slaughtered his animal. However, the Prophet's slaughter was obligatory as he performed qiran. The matn's wording 'in ahabba' (if he wishes) suggests it is not a pillar. The Hanafi position is clear that slaughter is wajib for tamattu' and qiran, but mustahabb (recommended) for ifrad.

Key Terms
يَذْبَحُ (yadhbahu): To slaughter a sacrificial animal (hady) as part of Hajj rituals.
تَمَتُّع (tamattu'): A type of Hajj where one performs Umrah first, then afterwards Hajj in the same year with a break (tahlil) between them.
قِرَان (qiran): A type of Hajj where one combines Umrah and Hajj with a single ihram without a break.
إِفْرَاد (ifrad): A type of Hajj performed alone, without combining with Umrah.

Key Takeaway
Slaughter after stoning is wajib for tamattu' and qiran pilgrims, but only recommended for ifrad.

Shaving or Trimming Hair – Shaving is Better
Ruling on the final act of tahallul: shaving or trimming hair, with preference for shaving

Learning Objective
By the end of this lesson, you will be able to state the Hanafi ruling on shaving vs trimming during Hajj and explain why shaving is preferred, citing the Quran and hadith evidence.

Core Idea
Shaving is better but trimming suffices — both are valid acts of tahallul.

This lesson focuses on the final wajib act of tahallul (exit from ihram). After stoning the jamarat and offering the sacrifice, the pilgrim must shave or trim his hair. While both are valid, the Hanafi school, based on clear proofs, considers complete shaving (halq) superior to trimming (taqsir). Understanding this distinction ensures you correctly fulfil the obligation and appreciate the prophetic emphasis on shaving.

Guided Path
1
Identify the act and its ruling
The matn states that the pilgrim shaves or trims. This is a wajib act of Hajj. Determine the legal category (wajib) and note that both options fulfil the obligation.
Wajib here means it is obligatory to do either; omission invalidates the Hajj.
2
Distinguish between shaving and trimming
Shaving (al-khalq) means removing all hair completely. Trimming (al-taqsir) means cutting a small portion from each lock. The matn explicitly raises one over the other: 'and shaving is better'.
The difference is qualitative, not quantitative in terms of validity.
3
Locate the proofs
The commentary cites two proofs: Quran 48:27 mentions both shaved and trimmed heads as acceptable. A hadith (Muslim no. 1301) shows the Prophet ﷺ prayed for forgiveness for those who shave (twice) and then for those who trim, indicating preference.
The Quranic verse establishes permissibility; the hadith establishes preference.
4
Explain the wajh al-dalalah (evidence link)
The hadith’s wording—praying for shavers first and repeating it—demonstrates that shaving is the more virtuous choice. The Quran includes both, so neither is invalid. This yields the ruling: wajib to do either, afdal to shave.
The Hanafi method uses the explicit textual order to derive preference.
5
Note the special case for women
The matn implies the ruling is for men. For women, only trimming is allowed. This is a mujtahad fih point with no dispute in the Hanafi school.
Shaving the head for women is prohibited due to modesty.

Source Text
⚠ Extracted via Advanced OCR ∼97% accuracy, minor errors may remain — always verify against original Arabic books
ثُمَّ يَحْلِقُ أَوْ يُقَصِّرُ وَالْخَلْقُ أَفْضَلُ
Then he shaves or trims, and shaving is better.
Source pages p. 253

Commentary
This is a ruling regarding the final tahallul (exit from ihram). After stoning and slaughter (if applicable), the pilgrim shaves his entire head (halq) or trims his hair (taqsir). Shaving is preferred (afdal) over trimming. This is for men; for women, only trimming is prescribed. The proof cited is the Quranic verse from Surah al-Fath (48:27) where Allah mentions the believers entering the mosque with heads shaved or trimmed, indicating both are permissible. Additionally, a hadith from Abdullah (Ibn Umar) in Muslim (no. 1301) and Bukhari (no. 1727) reports that the Prophet ﷺ prayed for mercy for those who shave (twice) and then for those who trim, showing shaving is preferred. Also a hadith from Ibn Abbas in Abu Dawud (no. 1984) states that women do not shave but only trim. The Hanafi school follows these proofs, holding that shaving is the superior option for men, but trimming is sufficient and valid. This act, along with stoning and tawaf al-ifadah, complete the tahallul.

Key Terms
الْخَلْق (al-khalq): Shaving the head completely.
التَّقْصِير (taqsir): Trimming the hair, typically cutting a small portion from each lock.

Key Terms from Source Passage

Checkpoint

A) It is obligatory and the only option
B) It is better than trimming, but trimming is also valid
C) It is not allowed; only trimming is permitted
D) It is recommended but only after returning home

Key Takeaway
Shaving is the preferred option for men, but trimming fulfills the wajib and completes the tahallul.

Slaughtering the Sacrifice after Stoning: Optional or Obligatory?
Ruling on optional slaughter after stoning the Jamrah

Learning Objective
By the end of this lesson, you will be able to state the Hanafi ruling on slaughtering after stoning for an ifrad pilgrim and explain how the hadith supports this ruling.

Core Idea
Slaughtering after stoning is optional (sunnah) for the ifrad pilgrim; obligation only applies to tamattu' and qarin.

This lesson examines the matn statement that the pilgrim 'slaughters if he wishes' after stoning. We will see how the phrase 'if he wishes' indicates a voluntary act, and how the hadith of Jabir confirms the Prophet's practice. The Hanafi school distinguishes between types of pilgrims regarding the sacrifice.

Guided Path
1
Identify the act and its ruling in the matn
The matn says 'thumma yadhabahu in ahabba' – 'then he slaughters if he wishes'. The phrase 'if he wishes' (in ahabba) indicates that the act is not obligatory but optional.
2
Locate the dalil (hadith)
The commentary cites a hadith from Jabir ibn Abdullah describing the Prophet's actions on the Day of Sacrifice, which includes standing at al-Mash'ar al-Haram and then departing before sunrise. The hadith shows the Prophet's practice but does not command slaughter.
The hadith is from Muslim and Abu Dawud.
3
Analyze the wajh al-dalalah (how the hadith proves the ruling)
The hadith reports the Prophet's actions without a command to slaughter. In Hanafi usul, an act of the Prophet (fi'l) indicates recommendation (sunnah), not obligation, unless accompanied by a command. Thus, the matn's wording ('in ahabba') aligns with the fi'l being optional.
4
Note the intra-Hanafi distinction (ifrad vs tamattu/qiran)
The Hanafi school holds that the sacrifice (hady) is wajib for mutamatti' and qarin pilgrims due to other texts (e.g., Quran 2:196). For ifrad, it is mustahab (sunnah). The matn is general, so the ruling for ifrad is sunnah.
This distinction is crucial to avoid conflating the rulings.
5
Evaluate the cross-madhhab ikhtilaf
Other schools (e.g., Shafi'i) hold that slaughter after stoning is wajib for all pilgrims. The Hanafi response is that the evidence from the Prophet's action and the permission language ('in ahabba') negate obligation except where explicitly required (tamattu/qarin).

Then he slaughters if he wishes. Commentary
This is a ruling from the matn stating that after stoning, the pilgrim may slaughter an animal if he wishes. The phrase 'if he wishes' indicates that it is not obligatory but optional. The hadith from Jabir describes the Prophet's actions on the Day of Sacrifice, which included slaughtering, but the word 'if he wishes' shows it is not a duty. In the Hanafi school, the sacrifice (hady) is wajib only for those performing tamattu' or qiran; for ifrad, it is mustahab. The matn here is general, so the ruling is that it is permissible and recommended but not required.

Key Terms
ذبح (dhabh): Slaughtering the sacrificial animal (hady) on the Day of Sacrifice after stoning.

Key Takeaway
The Hanafi school distinguishes between types of hajj: slaughter is wajib only for tamattu' and qarin, and sunnah for ifrad, based on the phrase 'if he wishes' and the Prophet's practice.

Shaving or Trimming Hair after Slaughter
Ruling with proof on shaving/trimming after stoning

Learning Objective
By the end of this lesson, you will be able to state the Hanafi ruling on shaving or trimming after stoning in Hajj, explain the three proofs, and apply the ruling to men and women.

Core Idea
Shaving or trimming is wajib in Hajj; shaving is better for men, women only trim.

This passage from Al-Quduri presents the ruling that after stoning the jamarat, the pilgrim must shave or trim his hair. The author provides three clear proofs: a Quranic verse, a hadith showing the Prophet's practice and supplication, and a specific hadith for women. We will examine each proof and understand why shaving is recommended for men while women are limited to trimming.

Guided Path
1
Identify the act and its ruling
The act is shaving (halq) or trimming (taqsir) the hair after stoning the jamarat. The Hanafi school considers it wajib (obligatory); omitting it requires a dam (sacrifice).
Wajib is a level below fard; its evidence is zanni al-thubut or al-dalalah.
2
Locate the dalil
The author cites three proofs: (1) Quran 48:27, which describes the believers entering the mosque with heads shaved or hair trimmed; (2) a hadith where the Prophet prayed for mercy on those who shave and those who trim, mentioning shavers first; (3) a hadith stating that women do not shave but only trim.
The first dalil is Quran (qati al-thubut), the others are ahad hadith (zanni al-thubut).
3
Trace the wajh al-dalalah
The Quranic verse presents shaving and trimming as two acceptable states, implying that one must do either. The hadith shows the Prophet's preference by starting with shavers, indicating its superiority. The women-specific hadith clearly restricts them to trimming.
The verse does not explicitly command, but it indicates necessity for the completion of Hajj.
4
Note the ikhtilaf
Other schools (e.g., Shafi'i, Maliki) consider it a sunnah, not wajib. They interpret the proofs as showing recommendation, not obligation, and note that the Prophet did not command it with an imperative.
This is a legitimate ikhtilaf; the practical difference is the requirement of dam if omitted.
5
Evaluate the Hanafi tarjih
The Hanafi school relies on the Quran and hadith as indicating that the act is a necessary rite; omission breaks the sequence of Hajj and must be compensated. The preferred view (mufta bihi) is that it is wajib, with shaving being better for men.
The ruling is from Zahir al-Riwayah and is the standard position.

Source Text
⚠ Extracted via Advanced OCR ∼97% accuracy, minor errors may remain — always verify against original Arabic books
ثُمَّ يَحْلِقُ أَوْ يُقَصِرُ وَالْخَلْقُ أَفْضَلُ الوجه: (1) الآية لثبوت ثُمَّ يَحْلِقُ أَوْ يُقَصِرُ القدصَدَقَ اللهُ رَسُولَهُ الرُّؤْيَا بِالْحَقِّ لَتَدْخُلُنَّ الْمَسْجِدَ الْحَرَامَ إِن شَاءَ اللَّهُ عَامِنِينَ مُحَلِقِينَ رُءُوسَكُمْ وَمُقَصِّرِينَ لَا تَخَافُونَ فَعَلِمَ مَا لَمْ تَعْلَمُوا فَجَعَلَ مِن دُونِ ذَلِكَ فَتْحًا قَرِيبًا (سورة الفتح، 48، الآية: 27) وجه (۲) الحديث لثبوت ثُمَّ يَحْلِقُ أَوْ يُقَصِرُ وَالْخَلْقُ أَفْضَلُ \ أَنَّ عَبْدَ اللَّهِ، قَالَ: حَلَقَ رَسُولُ اللَّهِ صَلَّى اللهُ عَلَيْهِ وَسَلَّمَ وَحَلَقَ طَائِفَةٌ مِنْ أَصْحَابِهِ وَقَصَّرَ بَعْضُهُمْ، قَالَ عَبْدُ اللَّهِ: إِنَّ رَسُولَ اللَّهِ صَلَّى اللَّهُ عَلَيْهِ وَسَلَّمَ قَالَ: «رَحِمَ اللهُ الْمُحَلِقِينَ» مَرَّةً أَوْ مَرَّتَيْنِ، ثُمَّ قَالَ: «وَالْمُقَصِرِينَ» (مسلم: بَابُ تَفْضِيلِ الْخَلْقِ عَلَى التَّقْصِيرِ وَجَوَازِ التَّقْصِيرِ، نمبر 1301 / بخاري: باب الحلق والتقصير عند الاحلال، نمبر: 1727/ أبو داؤد: بَابُ الْخَلْقِ وَالتَّقْصِيرِ، نمبر: 1979) وجه:(۳) الحديث لثبوت ثُمَّ يَحْلِقُ أَوْ يُقَصِرُ وَالْخَلْقُ أَفْضَلُ \ أَنَّ ابْنَ عَبَّاسٍ، قَالَ: قَالَ رَسُولُ اللَّهِ صَلَّى اللهُ عَلَيْهِ وَسَلَّمَ: «لَيْسَ عَلَى النِّسَاءِ حَلْقٌ إِنَّمَا عَلَى النِّسَاءِ التَّقْصِيرُ» (أبو داؤد: بَابُ الخلق والتقصير نمبر: 1984) اصول : رمی جمار کے بعد حلق یا قصر کرائے البتہ حلق زیادہ بہتر ہے۔
Then he shaves or trims, and shaving is better. Evidence (1) The verse proving then he shaves or trims: 'Indeed, Allah has fulfilled the vision of His Messenger in truth. You will surely enter al-Masjid al-Haram, if Allah wills, in safety, with your heads shaved and [hair] shortened, not fearing...' (Surah al-Fath, 48:27). Evidence (2) Hadith proving then he shaves or trims and shaving is better: That Abdullah said: The Messenger of Allah (peace be upon him) shaved, and a group of his companions shaved, and some of them trimmed. Evidence (3) Hadith proving then he shaves or trims and shaving is better: That Ibn Abbas said: The Messenger of Allah (peace be upon him) said, 'Shaving is not required for women; only trimming is for women' (Abu Dawud, no. 1984). Principle: After stoning the jamarat, he should shave or trim, but shaving is better.
Source pages p. 253

Commentary
This passage presents the ruling that after slaughtering (or if not slaughtering, after stoning) the pilgrim must either shave his head completely or trim his hair. Shaving is considered superior. The author provides three proofs: (1) the Quranic verse from Surah al-Fath which mentions both shaving and trimming as signs of entering the sacred mosque; (2) a hadith where the Prophet mentions mercy for both those who shave and those who trim, but he first mentions those who shave, indicating priority; (3) a hadith specifying that women do not shave but only trim. The principle ('usul') in Urdu states: after stoning, one should shave or trim, but shaving is better. In the Hanafi school, shaving or trimming is wajib (obligatory) for the validity of Hajj; if omitted, a dam (sacrifice) is required. Shaving is afdal (better) for men, while women must only trim.

Key Terms
حلق (halq): Shaving the head completely.
تقصیر (taqsir): Trimming the hair, i.e., cutting a portion of the hair.

Key Takeaway
Shaving or trimming the hair after stoning is a wajib act in Hajj; men should strive to shave, while women only trim, and omitting it requires a dam.

Partial Tahlul: Everything Permissible Except Women
Ruling on the state of partial tahlul after stoning

Learning Objective
By the end of this lesson, you will be able to state the Hanafi ruling on what becomes permissible after stoning Jamrat al-Aqabah and identify which prohibitions remain until tawaf al-ziyarah.

Core Idea
After stoning, all ihram restrictions are lifted except marital relations — partial tahlul.

The pilgrim who has stoned Jamrat al-Aqabah on the Day of Sacrifice enters a unique intermediate state. While most prohibitions of ihram — wearing stitched clothes, applying perfume, cutting nails and hair — become permissible, one restriction remains until complete tahlul after tawaf al-ziyarah. This lesson examines the textual proof for this partial lifting and its practical consequences.

Guided Path
1
Identify the ruling
Read the Arabic passage carefully. The source states that after stoning, everything becomes permissible except women. Determine the precise scope of this ruling.
2
Analyze the hadith evidence
Examine the hadith from Ibn Abbas (Ibn Majah). Note that the wording is explicit: 'everything becomes permitted except women.' Consider the authority of Ibn Abbas's statement as a qawl sahabi in Hanafi usul.
3
Understand the perfume exception
Observe how Ibn Abbas responds to the man's question about perfume. By citing the Prophet's action, he demonstrates that perfume is included in 'everything' that becomes permissible.
This shows that stitched clothes, perfume, etc., are all permissible.
4
Distinguish partial vs complete tahlul
Recognize that the remaining prohibition of women means this is a partial tahlul. Complete tahlul requires tawaf al-ziyarah (and sa'y if not done before). Understand the practical sequence: rami → partial tahlul → tawaf → full tahlul.
5
Compare with other schools
Note that some scholars (e.g., Shafi'is) hold that full tahlul only occurs after all three actions (rami, halq/taqsir, tawaf). The Hanafi view permits many actions earlier, creating a distinct intermediate state.

Source Text
⚠ Extracted via Advanced OCR ∼97% accuracy, minor errors may remain — always verify against original Arabic books
٥٢ وَقَدْ حَلَّ لَهُ كُلُّ شَيْءٍ إِلَّا النِّسَاءَ ٥٢وجه : (۱) الحديث لثبوت وَقَدْ حَلَّ لَهُ كُلُّ شَيْءٍ إِلَّا النِّسَاءَ اعَنِ ابْنِ عَبَّاسٍ، قَالَ: «إِذَا رَمَيْتُمُ الْجُمْرَةَ، فَقَدْ حَلَّ لَكُمْ كُلُّ شَيْءٍ إِلَّا النِّسَاءَ» فَقَالَ لَهُ رَجُلٌ: يَا ابْنَ عَبَّاسِ وَالطَّيِّبُ؟ فَقَالَ: «أَمَّا أَنَا، فَقَدْ رَأَيْتُ رَسُولَ اللَّهِ صلى الله عليه وسلم يُضَمِّحُ رَأْسَهُ بِالْمِسْكِ، أَفَطِيبٌ ذَلِكَ، أَمْ لَا»( سنن ابن ماجة ، بَابُ مَا يَحِلُّ لِلرَّجُل، إِذَا رَمَى جَمْرَةَ الْعَقَبَةِ، غمبر 3041)
And everything becomes permitted for him except women. Evidence (1) Hadith proving that everything becomes permitted for him except women: from Ibn Abbas, he said: 'When you stone the jamrah, everything becomes permitted for you except women.' A man said to him: O Ibn Abbas, and perfume? He said: As for me, I saw the Messenger of Allah (peace be upon him) applying musk to his head. Is that perfume or not?' (Sunan Ibn Majah, chapter on what becomes permitted for a man when he stoned Jamrat al-Aqabah, no. 3041).
Source pages p. 254

Commentary
This ruling states that after stoning Jamrat al-Aqabah, the pilgrim enters a state of partial tahlul (lifting of ihram restrictions). All prohibitions of ihram are lifted except the prohibition of marital relations with one's spouse. The hadith from Ibn Abbas confirms this, and he also clarifies that using perfume is permitted, even though it was forbidden in ihram, because he saw the Prophet applying musk after stoning. In the Hanafi school, this is the established ruling: after rami, the pilgrim may cut hair (or shave), wear stitched clothes, apply perfume, etc., but sexual intimacy remains forbidden until after tawaf al-ziyarah.

Key Terms
حل (halla): To become permissible; here, the lifting of ihram restrictions.

Key Terms from Source Passage

Checkpoint
What remains prohibited after stoning the jamrah according to the Hanafi school?
A) Wearing perfume
B) Cutting nails
C) Marital relations with spouse
D) Wearing stitched clothes

Key Takeaway
After stoning, the pilgrim enjoys partial tahlul: all prohibitions lift except sexual intimacy, which awaits complete tahlul after tawaf al-ziyarah.

The Timing and Obligation of Tawaf al-Ziyarah
Ruling on the timing and obligation of Tawaf al-Ziyarah with hadith proofs

Learning Objective
By the end of this lesson, you will be able to state the timing of Tawaf al-Ziyarah according to the Hanafi school and apply the ruling that it is a rukn of Hajj.

Core Idea
Tawaf al-Ziyarah is a pillar of Hajj, and must be performed within the three days of tashriq (10th–12th).

After completing the key rites at Mina on the Day of Sacrifice, the pilgrim proceeds to Mecca for Tawaf al-Ziyarah, also known as Tawaf al-Ifadah. This lesson examines the Hanafi ruling on its obligatory nature, permissible timing, and the evidence from the Prophet's practice.

Guided Path
1
Identify the act and its ruling
Tawaf al-Ziyarah is a circumambulation of the Kaaba with seven circuits. It is a rukn (pillar) of Hajj; omitting it invalidates the Hajj entirely.
2
Locate the dalil
Two hadiths are cited: one from Jabir ibn Abdullah (Muslim) and one from Ibn Umar (Abu Dawud), both showing the Prophet performed this tawaf on the Day of Sacrifice.
The second hadith adds that he prayed Zuhr in Mina, indicating he returned after the tawaf.
3
Trace the wajh al-dalalah
The Prophet's action of proceeding to Mecca and performing tawaf on the Day of Sacrifice establishes both the obligation and the preferred time. His consistent practice makes it a binding sunnah, elevated to wujub in the Hanafi school.
The imperative implied by his action is interpreted as obligatory.
4
Identify the timing window
The matn explicitly states the tawaf can be performed on the Day of Sacrifice (10th), the next day (11th), or the day after (12th). These are the days of tashriq.
The text says 'min yawmihi dhalika aw min al-ghad aw min ba'd al-ghad'.
5
Note the consequence of delay
If the pilgrim delays beyond the 12th, the tawaf is still valid but a dam (sacrifice) becomes obligatory as compensation. This is a Hanafi-established rule.
The source does not explicitly state the dam, but it is derived from other texts on Hajj penalties.

Source Text
⚠ Extracted via Advanced OCR ∼97% accuracy, minor errors may remain — always verify against original Arabic books
۵۳. ثُمَّ يَأْتِي مَكَّةَ مِنْ يَوْمِهِ ذَلِكَ أَوْ مِنْ الْغَدِ أَوْ مِنْ بَعْدِ الْغَدِ فَيَطُوفُ بِالْبَيْتِ طَوَافَ الزِّيَارَةِ سَبْعَةَ أَشْوَاطِ ه وجه : (۱) الحديث لثبوت ثُمَّ يَأْتِي مَكَّةَ مِنْ يَوْمِهِ ذَلِكَ أَوْ مِنْ الْغَدِ \ دَخَلْنَا عَلَى جَابِرِ بْنِ عَبْدِ الله، . . . ثُمَّ رَكِبَ رَسُولُ اللهِ صَلَّى اللهُ عَلَيْهِ وَسَلَّمَ فَأَفَاضَ إِلَى الْبَيْتِ، فَصَلَّى بِمَكَّةَ الظُّهْرَ، (مسلم: بَابُ حَجَّةِ النَّبِيِّ صَلَّى اللهُ عَلَيْهِ وَسَلَّمَ، نمبر: 1218/) وجه (۲) الحديث لثبوت ثُمَّ يَأْتِي مَكَّةَ مِنْ يَوْمِهِ ذَلِكَ اعَنْ نَافِعٍ، عَنِ ابْنِ عُمَرَ، أَنَّ النَّبِيَّ صلى الله عليه وسلم «أَفَاضَ يَوْمَ النَّحْرِثُمَّ صَلَّى الظُّهْرَ مِنِّى يَعْنِي رَاجِعًا» (أبوداؤد: بَابُ الْإِفَاضَةِ فِي الْحَجَ: 1998)
Then he comes to Mecca on that day or the next day or the day after, and performs tawaf around the House, the Tawaf al-Ziyarah, seven circuits. Evidence (1) Hadith proving then he comes to Mecca on that day or the next day: We entered upon Jabir ibn Abdullah... then the Messenger of Allah (peace be upon him) rode and went to the House, and prayed Zuhr in Mecca (Muslim, no. 1218). Evidence (2) Hadith proving then he comes to Mecca on that day: from Nafi', from Ibn Umar, that the Prophet (peace be upon him) went on the day of sacrifice, then prayed Zuhr in Mina, meaning returning (Abu Dawud, no. 1998).
Source pages p. 254

Commentary
This ruling states that after completing the rituals at Mina (rami, slaughter, shaving), the pilgrim proceeds to Mecca to perform Tawaf al-Ziyarah, also known as Tawaf al-Ifadah. This tawaf can be performed on the Day of Sacrifice (10th Dhu al-Hijjah) or the following two days (11th and 12th). It consists of seven circuits around the Kaaba. The two hadith proofs show that the Prophet performed this tawaf on the Day of Sacrifice. In the Hanafi school, Tawaf al-Ziyarah is a rukn (pillar) of Hajj, and it must be performed within the days of tashriq (10th to 12th). Delaying it beyond that requires a dam.

Key Terms
طواف الزيارة (tawaf al-ziyarah): The obligatory circumambulation of the Kaaba performed after the stoning on the Day of Sacrifice or the following days.

Key Terms from Source Passage

Checkpoint
According to the Hanafi school, when can Tawaf al-Ziyarah be performed?
A) Only on the 10th of Dhu al-Hijjah
B) Anytime during the month of Dhu al-Hijjah
C) On the 10th, 11th, or 12th of Dhu al-Hijjah
D) Only after the 12th

Key Takeaway
Tawaf al-Ziyarah is a pillar of Hajj that must be performed within 10th–12th of Dhu al-Hijjah; delay or omission requires a dam.

Ramal and Sa'i in Tawaf al-Ziyarah
Conditional ruling on ramal and sa'i

Learning Objective
By the end of this lesson, you will be able to state the two scenarios for ramal and sa'i in Tawaf al-Ziyarah and apply the rule that sa'i is wajib only once per Hajj.

Core Idea
If sa'i was done after Qudum, no ramal or sa'i in Ziyarah; if not, both are required.

This passage from al-Quduri presents a conditional ruling about ramal (brisk walking) and sa'i (the ritual walk between Safa and Marwah) during Tawaf al-Ziyarah. The ruling depends on whether the pilgrim has already performed sa'i after the arrival tawaf. Understanding this nuance helps avoid repeating an obligatory act that need not be repeated.

Guided Path
1
Identify the two scenarios
The text presents two cases: (1) the pilgrim performed sa'i after Tawaf al-Qudum, (2) the pilgrim did not perform sa'i earlier.
These are the only two possibilities.
2
State the ruling for each scenario
For scenario 1: no ramal (brisk walking) in Tawaf al-Ziyarah and no sa'i after it. For scenario 2: ramal is performed in the first three circuits of Tawaf al-Ziyarah and sa'i is performed after the tawaf.
Ramal is sunnah muakkadah, sa'i is wajib.
3
Understand the underlying principle
Sa'i is wajib only once in Hajj. Ramal is a sunnah that is associated with a tawaf that is followed by sa'i. Therefore, if sa'i was already performed earlier, neither ramal nor sa'i is required in Tawaf al-Ziyarah.
The hadith from Jabir confirms that sa'i is not repeated.
4
Apply to a hypothetical scenario
If a pilgrim delayed sa'i and is now performing Tawaf al-Ziyarah, he must include ramal in the first three circuits and perform sa'i afterwards. If he completed sa'i after Qudum, he simply performs Tawaf al-Ziyarah normally without ramal or extra sa'i.
This covers the practical application.

Source Text
⚠ Extracted via Advanced OCR ∼97% accuracy, minor errors may remain — always verify against original Arabic books
۵۴. فَإِنْ كَانَ سَعَى بَيْنَ الصَّفَا وَالْمَرْوَةِ عَقِيبَ طَوَافِ الْقُدُومِ لَمَّ يَرْمُلْ فِي هَذَا الطَّوَافِ وَلَا سَعْيَ عَلَيْهِ وَإِنْ لَمْ يَكُنْ قَدَّمَ السَّعْيَ رَمَلَ فِي هَذَا الطَّوَافِ وَسَعَى بَعْدَهُ عَلَى مَا قَدَّمْنَا ۵۴ وجه : (۱) الحديث لثبوت فَإِنْ كَانَ سَعَى بَيْنَ الصَّفَا وَالْمَرْوَةِ \ سَمِعَ جَابِرَ بْنَ عَبْدِ اللَّهِ، يَقُولُ: «لَمْ يَطْفِ النَّبِيُّ صَلَّى اللَّهُ عَلَيْهِ وَسَلَّمَ وَلَا أَصْحَابُهُ بَيْنَ الصَّفَا وَالْمَرْوَةِ إِلَّا طَوَافًا وَاحِدًا» (مسلم: بَابُ بَيَانِ أَنَّ السَّعْيَ لَا يُكَرَّرُ ، نمبر : 1279)
Then if he performed Sa'i between Safa and Marwah after the Tawaf al-Qudum, he does not walk briskly (ramal) in this tawaf, and no Sa'i is required upon him. And if he had not performed Sa'i earlier, he walks briskly in this tawaf and performs Sa'i after it, as we previously mentioned. Evidence (1) Hadith proving that if he performed Sa'i between Safa and Marwah: I heard Jabir ibn Abdullah say: 'The Prophet (peace be upon him) and his companions did not perform Tawaf between Safa and Marwah except one Tawaf' (Muslim, chapter on clarification that Sa'i is not repeated, no. 1279).
Source pages p. 254

Commentary
This is a procedural ruling from the matn. The pilgrim has already performed Tawaf al-Qudum upon arriving in Mecca. The text provides two scenarios: (1) If he already performed the Sa'i after that arrival tawaf, then when he comes for Tawaf al-Ziyarah, he should not do ramal (walking briskly) during this tawaf, and no additional Sa'i is needed. (2) If he did not perform Sa'i earlier (i.e., he delayed it), then he must do ramal during this tawaf and perform Sa'i after it. The hadith from Jabir confirms that Sa'i is only done once in Hajj; it is not repeated. This reinforces that Sa'i is either done after the arrival tawaf or after tawaf al-ziyarah, but not both.

Key Terms
رمل (ramal): Walking briskly with short steps in the first three circuits of tawaf.
سعی (sa'i): The ritual walking between Safa and Marwah seven times.

Key Terms from Source Passage

Checkpoint
If a pilgrim performed Sa'i after Tawaf al-Qudum, what is required during Tawaf al-Ziyarah?
A) He must perform ramal and Sa'i again
B) He performs ramal but no Sa'i
C) No ramal and no Sa'i
D) He performs Sa'i but no ramal

Key Takeaway
The need for ramal and sa'i in Tawaf al-Ziyarah depends on whether sa'i was performed earlier; if it was, neither is required; if not, both are required.

Complete Tahlul: Marital Relations Permitted After Tawaf al-Ziyarah
Ruling with proof on complete tahlul after Tawaf al-Ziyarah

Learning Objective
By the end of this lesson, you will be able to state the Hanafi ruling on complete tahlul (permissibility of marital relations) after Tawaf al-Ziyarah and explain the two proofs (qawl sahabi and Quranic verse) that support it.

Core Idea
Complete tahlul requires both stoning and Tawaf al-Ziyarah; marital relations become halal only after the tawaf.

The Hajj pilgrimage involves a sequence of rituals that gradually lift ihram restrictions. One key ruling concerns when marital relations become permissible. In this lesson, we examine the text from al-Quduri stating that after Tawaf al-Ziyarah, women become halal. The author provides two proofs: a statement of Abdullah ibn Umar and a Quranic verse. We will unpack these proofs to understand the Hanafi position on complete tahlul.

Guided Path
1
Identify the act and its ruling
The text states that after Tawaf al-Ziyarah, marital relations become permissible (halla lahu al-nisa). This is the second stage of tahlul. Identify the act (Tawaf al-Ziyarah) and the ruling (women become halal).
2
Examine the first proof (qawl sahabi)
The author cites Abdullah ibn Umar's statement about staying at Mina until stoning. Understand how this implies that women become halal only after all rituals, including tawaf. The hadith is from Sunan al-Bayhaqi.
Ibn Umar's ruling indicates that the full ritual sequence must be completed before leaving Mina, which includes tawaf.
3
Examine the second proof (Quranic verse)
The verse from Surah al-Hajj (22:29) commands circumambulation of the Ancient House as a concluding rite. Show how this indicates that tawaf is the final act that completes tahlul.
The verse uses 'thumma' (then), indicating sequence after fulfilling vows.
4
Distinguish the stages of tahlul
After stoning on the 10th, everything except marital relations is permitted. After Tawaf al-Ziyarah, even that is permitted. This clarifies the common misunderstanding.
This two-stage tahlul is unique to the Hanafi school.

Source Text
⚠ Extracted via Advanced OCR ∼97% accuracy, minor errors may remain — always verify against original Arabic books
۵۵. وَقَدْ حَلَّ لَهُ النِّسَاءُ وَهَذَا الطَّوَافُ هُوَ الْمَفْرُوضُ فِي الْحَجّ ۵۵ وجه : (۱) قول الصحابي لثبوت وَقَدْ حَلَ لَهُ النِّسَاءُ \ عَبْدَ اللهِ بْنَ عُمَرَ كَانَ يَقُولُ: " مَنْ غَرَبَتْ عَلَيْهِ الشَّمْسُ وَهُوَ عِنّى مِنْ أَوْسَطِ أَيَّامِ التَّشْرِيقِ فَلَا يَنْفِرَنَّ حَتَّى يَرْمِيَ الْحِمَارَ مِنَ الْغَدِ * (سنن للبيهقي: بَابُ مَنْ غَرَبَتْ لَهُ الشَّمْسُ يَوْمَ النَّفْرِ الْأَوَّلِ مِنِّى أَقَامَ حَتَّى يَرْمِيَ الْحِمَارَ يَوْمَ الثَّالِثِ بَعْدَ الزَّوَالِ، نمبر : 9646) وجه:(۲) الآية لثبوت وَقَدْ حَلَ لَهُ النِّسَاءُ الثُمَّ لْيَقْضُواْ تَفَقَهُمْ وَلْيُوفُواْ نُذُورَهُمْ وَلْيَطَوَّفُواْ بِالْبَيْتِ الْعَتِيقِ (سورة الحج، 22 ، الآية نمبر: 29) اصول : احناف کے نزدیک دسویں ذی الحجہ کو رمی جمار کرنے کے بعد جنسی خواہش کے علاوہ سب حلال ہے۔
And women become permitted for him, and this tawaf is the obligatory one in Hajj. Evidence (1) Saying of a companion proving that women become permitted for him: Abdullah ibn Umar used to say: 'Whoever has the sun set while he is at Mina on the middle days of tashriq should not leave until he stones the jamarat the next day' (Sunan al-Bayhaqi: chapter on... no. 9646). Evidence (2) Verse proving that women become permitted for him: 'Then let them complete their rites and fulfill their vows and circumambulate the Ancient House' (Surah al-Hajj, 22:29). Principle: According to the Hanafis, after stoning the jamarat on the 10th of Dhu al-Hijjah, everything except sexual desire is halal.
Source pages p. 254

Commentary
This final ruling states that after performing Tawaf al-Ziyarah, all remaining ihram restrictions are lifted, making even marital relations permissible. The text emphasizes that this tawaf is the obligatory tawaf (al-mafrud) of Hajj. The proofs include (1) the statement of Abdullah ibn Umar about staying at Mina until stoning, which implies that after completing all rituals, women become halal; and (2) the Quranic verse from Surah al-Hajj, which commands tawaf as a rite after fulfilling vows, indicating that tawaf is a means to complete the tahlul. The Urdu principle clarifies that after stoning on the 10th, everything except sexual desire (i.e., marital relations) is halal, and after Tawaf al-Ziyarah, even that is halal. In the Hanafi school, complete tahlul is achieved after both rami and tawaf al-ziyarah (and sa'i if not done earlier).

Key Terms
طواف مفروض (tawaf mafrud): The obligatory tawaf in Hajj, i.e., Tawaf al-Ziyarah.

Key Terms from Source Passage

Checkpoint
When do marital relations become permissible for a pilgrim according to the Hanafi school?
A) Immediately after stoning the jamrah
B) After shaving the head
C) After performing Tawaf al-Ziyarah
D) After returning home

Key Takeaway
The Hanafi school requires both stoning and Tawaf al-Ziyarah for complete tahlul; marital relations become halal only after the tawaf.
